Excluding the Unborn Child in Sale and Commutative Contracts
Legal ruling with qiyas proof for sale and analogous contracts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that excluding the unborn child in a sale makes the contract fasid, and apply the qiyas reasoning to similar commutative contracts (kitabah, ijarah, rahn).

Core Idea
Excluding the unborn child from a sale is like excluding a limb — it invalidates the contract as a fasid condition.

This passage from the Hidayah begins a discussion on the effect of excluding the unborn child (haml) in various contracts. In Hanafi fiqh, the unborn child is treated like a limb of the mother due to physical attachment. Therefore, when a seller tries to exclude it from a sale, it contradicts the nature of the contract — the sale should include all attached parts. This creates a fasid (invalid) condition that nullifies the sale. The same reasoning extends to other commutative contracts such as kitabah (contract of manumission), ijarah (lease), and rahn (pledge).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being excluded (the unborn child) and from which contract (sale). The ruling given is that the sale becomes fasid (voidable) due to the invalid condition.
The passage uses the term 'batala bihi' meaning the sale is nullified.
2
Locate the dalil: qiyas with limbs
The author provides an analogy: the unborn child is like the limbs of an animal (atraf al-hayawan) because of physical attachment (ittisal khalqi). Since selling an animal includes the limbs, excluding them contradicts the contract requirement.
This is qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) based on the illa of physical attachment.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The physical attachment makes the unborn child a part of the mother, so excluding it from the sale is a condition contrary to the contract's essence. In Hanafi law, such a condition is fasid and invalidates commutative contracts.
The principle: 'بيعالأصليتناولوها' (the sale of the original encompasses the attached parts).
4
Note the extension to other commutative contracts
The same ruling applies to kitabah, ijarah, and rahn because they are also mu'awadat (commutative) and are invalidated by fasid conditions. However, for kitabah, only conditions that affect the substance (i.e., the price) are invalidating.
The nuance: the invalidating factor in kitabah is what pertains to the substance of the contract.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical outcome: in Hanafi fiqh such a sale is fasid and must be rescinded; other schools may consider it valid.
This is a mukhtalaf fih issue; the Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تاب البيوع والحمل من هذا القبيل وهذا لانه بمنزلة اطراف الحيوان لاتصاله به خلقة وبيع الاصل يتناولها فالا ستثناء يكون على خلاف الموجب فلم يصح فيصير شرطا فاسدا والبيع يبطل به والكتابة والاجارة والرهن بمنزلة البيع لانها تبطل بالشروط الفاسدة غيران المفسد فى الكتابة ما يتمكن في صلب، العقد منها والهبة والصدقة والنكاح والخلع والصلح عن دم العمد لا تبطل باستثناء الحمل بل يبطل الاستثناء لان هذه العقود لا تبطل بالشروط الفاسدة وكذا الوصية لا تبطل به لكن يصح الاستثناء حتى يكون الحمل مير اثار الجارية وصية لان الوصية اخت الميراث والميراث يجرى فيما فى البطن بخلاف ما اذا استثنى خدمتها لان الميراث لا يجرى فيها
Chapter of sales: The unborn child is of this category. This is because it is like the limbs of the animal due to its physical attachment. The sale of the original includes them, so the exclusion is contrary to the requirement [of the contract] and is thus invalid; it becomes an invalid condition, and the sale is nullified by it. Kitabah (contract of manumission), ijarah (lease), and rahn (pledge) are like the sale because they are invalidated by invalid conditions, except that the invalidating [condition] in kitabah is what pertains to the substance of the contract. Hiba (gift), sadaqah (charity), nikah (marriage), khul' (divorce by redemption), and sulh (compromise) for deliberate homicide are not invalidated by the exclusion of the unborn child; rather, the exclusion is invalid because these contracts are not invalidated by invalid conditions. Similarly, wasiyyah (will) is not invalidated by it, but the exclusion is valid, so the unborn child becomes inherited by the slave-girl as a bequest, because the bequest is the sibling of inheritance, and inheritance applies to what is in the womb, unlike the case where he excludes her service, because inheritance does not apply to it.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a legal ruling with proof from the Hidayah. The author establishes a general principle: excluding an unborn child (haml) from a sale of its mother is invalid, rendering the sale fasid (voidable). The reasoning is qiyas (analogy): the unborn child is like the limbs of the animal (atraf al-hayawan) because it is physically attached. Since selling the animal includes the limbs, excluding them contradicts the contract's requirement; thus the exclusion becomes a fasid condition that nullifies the sale. This ruling extends to other commutative contracts (mu'awadat) such as kitabah (contract of gradual manumission), ijarah (lease), and rahn (pledge) because they resemble sale. However, in kitabah, only conditions that affect the substance of the contract (i.e., the consideration) are invalidating. The second category includes non-commutative contracts like hiba, sadaqah, nikah, khul', and sulh 'an dam al-amd. These are not invalidated by a fasid condition; rather, the condition itself is void. The third category is wasiyyah: the contract is valid, but the exclusion of the unborn child is also valid because wasiyyah resembles inheritance, and inheritance applies to the unborn child. This contrasts with excluding the service of the slave-girl, which does not carry inheritance. Thus, if one stipulates in a will that the slave-girl is bequeathed but her unborn child is not, the child is nevertheless inherited by the legatee.

Key Terms
استثناء (istithna'): Excluding something from the object of a contract.
حمل (haml): Unborn child of a female slave.
شرط فاسد (shart fasid): An invalid condition that contradicts the contract's requirements.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person sells a slave-girl and explicitly excludes her unborn child, what is the ruling?
A) The sale is valid and the exclusion is valid.
B) The sale is invalid (fasid) because the exclusion is a fasid condition.
C) The sale is valid but the exclusion is void.
D) The sale is void (batil) and the child remains with the seller.

Key Takeaway
Excluding the unborn child from a sale is a fasid condition that makes the contract fasid, extended to all commutative contracts by qiyas.

Excluding the Unborn Child in Non-Commutative Contracts and Wasiyyah
Legal ruling on the effect of exclusion in non-commutative contracts and wasiyyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the effect of excluding the unborn child in non-commutative contracts (gift, marriage, etc.) where only the condition is void, versus the special case of wasiyyah where the exclusion is valid.

Core Idea
In gifts and marriage, excluding the unborn child is void but the contract remains valid; only in wasiyyah is the exclusion itself valid.

After establishing the rule for sale and commutative contracts, the passage turns to other transactions. For non-commutative contracts like gift (hiba), charity (sadaqah), marriage (nikah), khul', and sulh for deliberate blood-money, the presence of a fasid condition does not invalidate the entire contract; rather, the condition is void. Therefore, if someone gives a slave-girl as a gift and excludes her unborn child, the gift is valid and the child is included. A special case is wasiyyah (bequest): because wasiyyah is akin to inheritance, and inheritance applies to the unborn child, the exclusion here is valid — the child is not included. This contrasts with excluding the service of the slave-girl, which does not carry inheritance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of contracts
The passage lists hiba, sadaqah, nikah, khul', and sulh 'an dam al-'amd as non-commutative (ghayr mu'awadah). Also wasiyyah is discussed separately.
Non-commutative contracts are those involving donation or personal status.
2
State the general rule for non-commutative contracts
These contracts are not invalidated by fasid conditions. Only the condition itself is void; the contract remains valid.
The text says: 'la tabtal bi shurut al-fasidah' (they are not invalidated by invalid conditions).
3
Apply the rule to the exclusion of the unborn child
If one gifts a slave-girl and excludes her unborn child, the gift is valid and the child is included because the condition is void.
The exclusion becomes ineffective; the child passes with the mother.
4
Identify the exception: wasiyyah
Unlike other non-commutative contracts, the exclusion of the unborn child in a bequest is valid. The child does not pass with the mother.
Reason: wasiyyah is the sibling of inheritance (ukht al-mirath), and inheritance applies to the unborn child.
5
Understand the contrast with excluding service
Excluding the service (khidma) of the slave-girl in a bequest is invalid because inheritance does not apply to service — it is not property that can be inherited.
Service is a usufruct, not a tangible asset.

Source Text

Key Terms
استثناء (istithna'): Excluding something from the object of a contract.
وصية (wasiyyah): A bequest made after death; it is like inheritance.
غير معاوض (ghayr mu'awad): Non-commutative contract – one not based on exchange of consideration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person makes a bequest (wasiyyah) of a slave-girl and excludes her unborn child, what is the ruling?
A) The bequest is invalid because the condition is fasid.
B) The bequest is valid and the child is excluded from the bequest.
C) The bequest is valid and the child is included despite the condition.
D) The bequest is valid only if the child is also bequeathed.

Key Takeaway
In non-commutative contracts, the contract remains valid but the exclusion is void; in wasiyyah, the exclusion is valid due to its resemblance to inheritance.

Excluding the Foetus from Sale and Analogous Contracts
Explains first category of contracts voided by excluding foetus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that excluding a foetus from a sale is a corrupt condition that voids the contract, and explain why kitābah is treated differently when the condition is external.

Core Idea
Excluding the foetus voids the sale because it is like a limb—but kitābah tolerates external conditions like marriage.

In Hanafi fiqh, the foetus is legally inseparable from its mother, much like a limb. Therefore, any condition that excludes it from a sale violates the contract's nature and renders it void. This principle extends to similar contracts such as ijārah and rahn. However, kitābah (manumission contract) holds a unique position: only conditions that affect its essence are invalidating, while external conditions are simply voided, leaving the contract intact.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Rationale
The passage states that excluding the foetus from a sale is not permissible. Recognize that this is because the foetus is considered like a limb of the mother, and limbs are automatically included in the sale. A condition to exclude it contradicts the contract, making it a corrupt condition (shart fāsid) that voids the sale.
Focus on the analogy: foetus is to mother as limb is to animal.
2
Understand the Extension to Analogous Contracts
The author explains that contracts like kitābah, ijārah, and rahn are 'in the meaning of sale'—they involve transfer of ownership or usufruct. Therefore, corrupt conditions also void them, following the same logic.
Ijārah (lease) and rahn (pawn) are explicitly mentioned.
3
Analyze the Distinction for Kitābah
Kitābah is given special treatment because it resembles both sale (master receives payment) and marriage (slave is not property to himself). If the corrupt condition is inherent to the contract (e.g., payment in wine), the contract is void. But if the condition is external (e.g., restricting movement), the contract remains valid and the condition alone is void.
This dual nature explains why external conditions do not invalidate kitābah.
4
Connect the Reasoning to Legal Principles
The reasoning uses qiyas (analogy) to establish the ruling for the foetus and for kitābah's exception. The qiyas is based on the illah (effective cause) of 'attachment and inseparability' for the foetus, and 'resemblance to marriage' for kitābah's tolerance of external conditions.
This step reinforces the method of istidlal (legal reasoning) in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
چیز کا تنہا فروخت کرنا جائز نہیں ہے اس کا عقدیج سے استثناء کرنا بھی جائز نہیں ہے اور عمل بھی اسی قبیلہ سے ہے یعنی عمل کو تنہا پہنا جائزہ نہیں ہے اور حمل کو تنہا بیچنے کا عدم جواز اس لئے ہے کہ وہ حیوان کے اطراف یعنی اعضاء کے مرتبہ میں ہے یعنی جس طرح اطراف حیوان پیدائشی طور پر حیوان کے ساتھ متصل ہوتے ہیں۔ اسی طرح حمل بھی ذی حمل کے ساتھ متصل ہوتا ہے اور حیوان کی بیع اطراف کو شامل ہوتی ہے اس لئے اطراف کا استثناء موجب عقد کے خلاف ہوگا۔ اس طرح حمل کا استثناء بھی موجب عقد کے خلاف ہوگا۔ اور جو چیز موجب عقد کے خلاف ہو وہ صحیح نہیں ہوتی بلکہ شرط فاسد ہوتی ہے اس لئے حمل کا استثنا شرط فاسد ہو گا اور شرط فاسد سے بیع باطل ہو جاتی ہے اس لیئے حمل کے استثناء سے بیع باطل ہو جائے گی اور کتابت ، اجارہ اور رہن چونکہ بیع کے معنی میں ہیں۔ جیسا کہ ابھی گزرا اس لئے یہ عقود بھی شروط فاسدہ سے باطل ہو جائیں گے ہاں اتنا فرق ہے کہ بیچ مطلقا شرط فاسد سے باطل ہو جاتی ہے شرط خواہ بیع کی ذات میں داخل ہویا ذات میں داخل نہ ہو۔ اور کتابت کو ایسی شرط باطل کرتی ہے جو عقد کتابت کی ذات میں داخل ہو۔ مثلا مسلمان اپنے غلام کو شراب یا سور پر مکاتب کرے یعنی بدل کتابت شراب یا سور کو قرار دے۔ اور اگر شرط عقد کتابت کی ذات میں داخل نہ ہو۔ مثلاً مولی نے مکاتب پر یہ زاردے۔ شرط لگائی کہ وہ دیو بند سے باہر نہیں جائے گا تو اس صورت میں عقد کتابت درست ہوگا اور مکاتب کو دیو بند سے باہر جانے کی اجازت ہوگی یعنی یہ شرط خود باطل ہو جائے گی اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عقد کتابت انتہاء پیج کے مشابہ ہے کیونکہ مکاتب مولی کے حق میں مال ہے چنانچہ مولی مکاتب کے عوض مال یعنی بدل کتابت حاصل کرتا ہے اور نکاح کے مشابہ ہے کیونکہ مکاتب خود اپنے حق میں مال نہیں ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ مکاتب کو بدل کتابت کے عوض کوئی مال حاصل نہیں ہوتا پس ہم نے کتابت کو ایسی شر راتیں جو مند کتابت کی ذات میں داخل ہو بیچ کے ساتھ لاحق کر دیا یعنی جس طرح شرط کی وجہ سے بیع فاسد ہو جاتی ہے اسی طرح ایسی شرط کی وجہ سے جو کتابت کی ذات میں نہ ہو کتابت کو نکاح کے ساتھ لاحق کیا یعنی جس طرح نکاح شرط سے فاسد نہیں ہوتا بلکہ خود شرط باطل ہو جاتی ہے اسی طرح ایسی شرط سے جو کتابت کی ذات میں داخل نہ ہو عقد کتابت باطل نہ ہوگا ۔ جبکہ شرط خود باطل ہو جائے گی۔
Selling something alone is not permissible, and excluding it from the contract is also not permissible. And labour is also of this category, meaning selling labour alone is not permissible. The non-permissibility of selling the foetus alone is because it is in the rank of the limbs of the animal, i.e., just as the limbs of an animal are naturally attached to the animal, similarly the foetus is attached to the pregnant animal. The sale of an animal includes its limbs, so excluding the limbs would contradict the contract. Similarly, excluding the foetus would also contradict the contract. Anything that contradicts the contract is not valid but is a corrupt condition. Therefore, excluding the foetus is a corrupt condition, and a corrupt condition invalidates the sale. Thus, the sale becomes void due to the exclusion of the foetus. And since kitābah, ijārah, and rahn are in the meaning of sale, as has just passed, these contracts also become void due to corrupt conditions. However, there is this difference: sale becomes void absolutely due to a corrupt condition, whether the condition enters into the essence of the sale or not. But kitābah is invalidated only by a condition that enters into the essence of the kitābah contract. For example, a Muslim makes his slave a mukātib on wine or a pig, i.e., he makes the kitābah payment wine or a pig. But if the condition does not enter into the essence of the kitābah contract, e.g., the master stipulates on the mukātib that he will not go outside Deoband, then in this case the kitābah contract is valid, and the mukātib will have permission to go outside Deoband, meaning the condition itself becomes void. The evidence for this is that the kitābah contract resembles both sale and marriage because the mukātib is property in relation to the master, as the master obtains property (the kitābah payment) in exchange for him, and it resembles marriage because the mukātib is not property in his own right. This is why the mukātib does not receive any property in exchange for the kitābah payment. So we have attached kitābah to sale regarding conditions that enter into its essence, i.e., just as sale becomes void due to a condition, similarly such a condition that enters into the essence of kitābah voids it. And regarding conditions that do not enter into its essence, we attached kitābah to marriage, i.e., just as marriage does not become void due to a condition but the condition itself becomes void, similarly a condition that does not enter into the essence of kitābah does not void the kitābah contract; rather, the condition itself becomes void.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage presents the first category of contracts regarding the exclusion of a foetus. The author explains that selling a foetus alone or excluding it from a sale is invalid because the foetus is akin to a limb, inseparable from the mother. Consequently, any condition to exclude the foetus in a sale is a corrupt condition (shart fāsid) rendering the contract void. This ruling extends to contracts like kitābah (contract of manumission for payment), ijārah (lease), and rahn (pawn) because they are analogous to sale. However, a critical distinction is made regarding kitābah: if the corrupt condition is inherent to the essence of the contract (e.g., fixing prohibited items as payment), the contract is void; if the condition is external (e.g., restricting movement), the contract remains valid and the condition alone is void. This is because kitābah exhibits characteristics of both sale (the master receives payment) and marriage (the mukātib is not property to himself). Thus, external conditions in kitābah are treated like those in marriage, which do not invalidate the contract.

Key Terms
حمل (ḥaml): The foetus or unborn offspring of an animal.
شرط فاسد (sharṭ fāsid): A condition that is invalid according to Islamic law, typically because it contradicts the nature of the contract or benefits one party without equivalent.
کتابت (kitābah): A contract of manumission in which a slave earns their freedom by paying a sum to the master in installments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a sale contract that excludes the foetus from the transaction?
A) The sale is valid, but the condition is void.
B) The sale is void due to the corrupt condition.
C) The sale is valid only if the buyer agrees.
D) The sale is suspended until the foetus is born.

Key Takeaway
Excluding the foetus from a sale voids the entire contract because it is a corrupt condition analogous to excluding a limb; however, in kitābah, only conditions that strike at the essence void the contract, while external conditions are simply invalidated.

Contracts Valid Despite Foetus Exclusion: The Second Category
Explains contracts valid despite foetus exclusion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which contracts remain valid despite a corrupt condition excluding the foetus and explain the Hanafi rationale based on the absence of riba.

Core Idea
Gratuitous contracts survive corrupt conditions because riba only corrupts exchange contracts.

The passage introduces the second category of contracts regarding foetus exclusion. Unlike sales and other exchange contracts, gifts, charities, marriage, khulʿ, and settlements for intentional homicide remain valid even if the foetus is explicitly excluded. Understanding this distinction is key to applying Hanafi contract law correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the listed contracts
List the examples given: gift (hibah), charity (sadaqah), marriage (nikah), khulʿ, and settlement for intentional homicide (sulh an damm al-amd).
All involve a slave-girl as the subject, with the foetus excluded.
2
Recognize common feature: tabarruʿāt and isqāṭāt
These contracts are gratuitous transfers (tabarruʿāt) or relinquishments (isqāṭāt), not exchange contracts (muʿāwaḍāt).
Gift and charity are tabarruʿ; khulʿ and sulh are isqāṭ.
3
Understand the cause of corruption (riba) and its absence
The first category of contracts (like sale) are invalidated by a corrupt condition because it leads to riba. Riba only applies to exchange contracts. Since these are not exchange contracts, riba is absent, so the contract remains valid.
The presence of riba is the distinguishing factor.
4
Note the exception of hibah supported by hadith
Although hibah is a transfer of ownership (tamlīk), it is proven by the Prophet's permission for a conditional gift that corrupt conditions in gifts are void while the gift remains valid.
This hadith is specific evidence for hibah, but the general principle applies to all similar contracts.
5
Apply: contract valid, exclusion void
The conclusion: the contract is sahih, the condition (excluding the foetus) is batil, and thus the foetus is included in the contract along with its mother.
The foetus is not excluded; it becomes part of the subject matter.

Source Text

The second category: where the contract is valid and the exclusion is void, such as gift, charity, marriage, khulʿ, and reconciliation for intentional homicide. For example, a master gives his slave-girl as a gift but does not gift her foetus, or gives her in charity but not the foetus, or makes her a dower in marriage but the foetus is excluded, or a woman makes khulʿ with her husband and gives her slave-girl as compensation but does not include the foetus, or the intentional killer makes a settlement with the slave-girl but does not include the foetus in the compensation. All these contracts are not invalidated by the exclusion of the foetus; rather, the exclusion itself becomes void, and both the foetus and its mother are included in the contract. The proof is that these contracts are not invalidated by corrupt conditions because in the first category, the corruption was due to the condition leading to ribā (interest), and ribā occurs only in exchange contracts. In the second category, the mentioned contracts like charity etc. are all of the type of gratuitous transfers (tabarruʿāt) and relinquishments (isqāṭāt), and ribā is not found in them. So when the cause of corruption is not present, these contracts will not become corrupt due to corrupt conditions; rather, the corrupt condition itself becomes void. Yes, although hibah is from the category of transfers of ownership (tamlīkāt), it is known from textual evidence that it is not invalidated by a corrupt condition. Thus, the Prophet ﷺ permitted gifting with the condition that the gifted object would be returned to the giver after the donee's death. So this gift is valid and the condition is void, such that after the donee's death, the gifted object will be given to the donee's heirs, not to the giver or the giver's heirs. From this hadith, it is known that although hibah is from the category of tamlīkāt, it is not invalidated by a corrupt condition; rather, the corrupt condition itself becomes void.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage outlines the second category of contracts regarding the exclusion of a foetus. Unlike sale and similar compensatory contracts, contracts like gift (hibah), charity (sadaqah), marriage (nikah), khulʿ (divorce initiated by wife), and settlement for intentional homicide (sulh an damm al-amd) remain valid even if the foetus is explicitly excluded. The exclusion itself becomes void, and the foetus is included in the contract. The reasoning is that riba (interest) is the underlying cause of corruption in the first category, and riba only applies to exchange contracts (mu'awadāt). These second-category contracts are gratuitous transfers (tabarruʿāt) or relinquishments (isqāṭāt), so riba is not relevant. Even though hibah is a transfer of ownership (tamlīk), it is exempted by a specific hadith where the Prophet ﷺ allowed a gift with a condition that would normally be considered corrupt. Thus, the rule for these contracts is that the contract stands, and the corrupt condition is nullified.

Key Terms
تبرعات (tabarruʿāt): Gratuitous transfers where one party gives without receiving equivalent compensation, such as gifts and charity.
اسقاطات (isqāṭāt): Relinquishments or waivers of rights, such as in khulʿ.
ربوا (ribā): Interest or usury, prohibited in Islamic law. It is the cause of corruption in exchange contracts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT mentioned as a contract that remains valid despite a condition excluding the foetus?
A) Charity (sadaqah)
B) Sale (bayʿ)
C) Gift (hibah)
D) Khulʿ

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, gratuitous contracts (tabarruʿāt) and relinquishments (isqāṭāt) remain valid even with a corrupt condition; the condition itself is void.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Buying Cloth Conditioned on Tailoring: Invalid Sale
Ruling on conditional purchase of cloth with tailoring service

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sale conditioned on the seller’s service, explain why it is invalid, and apply the two proofs: the corrupt condition and the prohibition of a transaction within a transaction.

Core Idea
A sale is invalid if it includes a condition that benefits one party and creates a second transaction.

Can you buy cloth and demand that the seller also cut and sew it into a garment? In the Hanafi school, such a condition renders the sale invalid (fasid). This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning: why an extraneous benefit for one party corrupts the contract, and why combining a sale with a hire or gratuitous service is prohibited as a 'transaction within a transaction' (ṣafqah fī ṣafqah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is buying cloth with the condition that the seller cuts and sews it into a garment. The ruling is that the sale is invalid (fasid).
The term 'fasid' means the contract is defective and cannot be legally effective.
2
Locate the first proof: corrupt condition
The condition is not required by the contract of sale (sharṭ lā yaqtaḍīhi al-ʿaqd) and benefits only the buyer. According to Hanafi principles, a condition that provides benefit to one party without being necessitated by the contract invalidates the sale.
This is distinct from a condition that is customary or mutually beneficial.
3
Locate the second proof: transaction within a transaction
The tailoring service is either compensated (making it a hire) or gratuitous (making it a gift). Either way, it constitutes a second contract embedded in the sale, which is prohibited by the hadith 'two transactions in one'.
The hadith's prohibition is general and covers any combination of a sale with another contract.
4
Analyze the alternative scenarios
If a portion of the price is allocated for tailoring, it becomes a hire (ijarah) within the sale. If no portion is allocated, it becomes a gratuitous act (tabarru'). Both are impermissible because they introduce uncertainty (gharar) and violate the prohibition of ṣafqah fī ṣafqah.
This analysis shows that the condition cannot be integrated without corrupting the sale.
5
Confirm the muftā bihī ruling
The relied-upon position (muftā bihī) in the Hanafi school is that such a conditional sale is invalid. This is the view of Imam Abu Hanifa as transmitted in the Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah.
Other schools may permit it, but within Hanafi fiqh, the ruling is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كپڑا اس شرط پر خریدا کہ بائع اسے کاٹ کر کرتا یا قبا ہی دے تو بیع فاسد ہے
قال. ومن اشترى ثوبا على ان يقطعه البائع ويخيطه قميصا او قباء فالبيع فاسد لانه شرط لا يقتضيه العقد وفيه منفعة لاحد المتعاقدين ولانه يصير صفقة في صفقة على مامر
ترجمہ اور اگر کسی نے کپڑا اس شرط پر خریدا کہ بائع اس کو کاٹ کر اس کا کرتا یا قباء بیٹے تو بیع فاسد ہے کیونکہ یہ ایسی شرط ہے جس کا عقد تقاضہ نہیں کرتا اور اس میں احد المتعاقدین کا نفع ہے اور اس لئے کہ یہ معاملہ کے اندر معاملہ ہے جیسا کہ گذرا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک آدمی نے کپڑا خریدا اور یہ شرط کی کہ بائع اس کپڑے کو کاٹ کر اس کا کرتا بنائے یا قباء بنائے تو یہ بیچ فاسد ہے کیونکہ یہ شرطا متضئی عقد کے خلاف بھی ہے اور اس میں احد العاقدین یعنی مشتری کا نفع بھی ہے اور جو شروا متقضی عقد کے خلاف ہو اور اس میں احد العاقدین کا نفع ہو تو وہ مفسد بیع ہوتی ہے اس لئے اس شرط سے بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی۔
دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ کپڑا کاٹ کر سینے کے مقابلہ میں شمن کا کوئی حصہ ہوگا یا نہیں ؟ اگر اس کے مقابلہ میں شمن کا کوئی حصہ ہے تو اجارہ بیچ میں داخل ہو جائے گا اور اگر اس کے مقابلہ میں شمن کا کوئی حصہ نہیں ہے۔ تو اعادہ بیج میں داخل ہو جائے گا۔ اور ایک معاملہ کو دوسرے معاملہ میں داخل کرنے سے چونکہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے منع فرمایا ہے اس لئے یہ عقد فاسد اور نا جائز ہوگا۔ (بنا یہ )
Bought cloth on the condition that the seller cuts it and makes it a shirt or robe, then the sale is invalid.
He said: Whoever buys a cloth on condition that the seller cuts it and sews it into a shirt or robe, the sale is invalid because it is a condition not required by the contract and contains benefit for one of the contracting parties, and because it becomes a transaction within a transaction as has passed.
Translation: And if someone bought cloth on condition that the seller cuts it and makes it a shirt or robe, then the sale is invalid because this is a condition that the contract does not necessitate and there is benefit for one of the contracting parties, and because it is a transaction within a transaction as has passed. Explanation: The case is that a man bought cloth and stipulated that the seller should cut this cloth and make it into a shirt or robe. This sale is invalid because this condition contradicts the requirement of the contract and contains benefit for one of the contracting parties, i.e., the buyer. And any condition that contradicts the requirement of the contract and contains benefit for one of the contracting parties invalidates the sale. So the sale becomes invalid due to this condition.
The second proof: Is there a portion of the price in exchange for cutting and sewing? If there is a portion of the price for it, then a contract of hire enters into the sale. And if there is no portion of the price for it, then it is a gratuitous act included in the sale. And because the Prophet ﷺ prohibited including one transaction in another, therefore this contract is invalid and impermissible.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage rules that buying cloth with the condition that the seller cuts and sews it into a garment renders the sale invalid (fasid). Two reasons are given: First, such a condition is not required by the contract of sale and benefits one party (the buyer), which makes it a corrupt condition. Second, it constitutes a transaction within a transaction (صفقة في صفقة), which the Prophet ﷺ prohibited. The explanation clarifies that if a portion of the price is allocated for the tailoring, it becomes a hire (ijarah) embedded in the sale, creating a dual transaction; if no portion is allocated, it becomes a gratuitous act (tabarru') included in the sale, which is also impermissible. Thus, the sale is void.

Key Terms
صفقة في صفقة (ṣafqah fī ṣafqah): A transaction within a transaction, i.e., combining two different contracts into one, which is prohibited.
شرط لا يقتضيه العقد (sharṭ lā yaqtaḍīhi al-ʿaqd): A condition not required by the contract, i.e., an extraneous stipulation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the seller is not a tailor.
B) Because it creates a transaction within a transaction.
C) Because the buyer must specify the exact garment.
D) Because the cloth is not yet owned.

Key Takeaway
A sale conditioned on the seller's service is invalid because the extraneous benefit creates a prohibited second transaction.

Buying Shoes with Condition of Adjustment
Ruling on purchase of shoes with condition seller adjusts/fits them

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of istihsan to override qiyas in customary transactions and explain why a condition of adjustment in shoe sales is valid.

Core Idea
Custom overrides strict analogy: a condition customary in shoe buying is valid by istihsan.

When you buy shoes, you often need them adjusted or strapped. Strict analogy (qiyas) would make such a condition invalid, as it adds a term not required by the sale. But the Hanafi school, using juristic preference (istihsan), permits it because people commonly deal this way. In this lesson, we will see how custom can override analogy in commercial transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the condition
The case is buying shoes with a condition that the seller will adjust them or add a strap. What exactly is being conditioned?
The condition is additional work not integral to the sale.
2
State the ruling by qiyas
According to strict analogy (qiyas), this sale is invalid because the condition is not required by the contract and creates an extra transaction, like buying cloth with a condition to tailor it.
Qiyas treats the shoe condition like the cloth tailoring condition.
3
Apply istihsan to override qiyas
Istihsan (juristic preference) permits the sale because such conditions are customary (ta'ammul) among people. The same reasoning permits dyeing cloth with conditions and the istisna' contract.
Custom and necessity justify departure from analogy.
4
Derive the operative rule
The reliance on istihsan means the sale is valid, the condition is binding. The analogy to cloth tailoring is rejected because shoe adjustment is a widespread practice.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جوتا اس شرط پر خریدا کہ بائع اسے برابر کر دے گا یا تسمہ بنا کر دے گا تو بیع استحسانا جائز ہے۔
قال ومن اشترى نعلا على ان يحذوه البائع او يشركه فالبیع فاسد قال ما ذكره جواب القياس ووجهه ما بينا وفى الاستحسان يجوز التعامل فيه فصار كصبغ الثوب وللتعامل جوزنا الاستصناع
Bought shoes on condition that the seller levels/adjusts them or makes a strap, then the sale is permissible by istihsan.
He said: Whoever buys shoes on condition that the seller adjusts them or makes a strap, the sale is invalid. He said: What he mentioned is the answer of qiyas (analogy), and its justification is as we explained. And by istihsan, dealing is permissible in it, so it becomes like dyeing the cloth, and due to custom, we have permitted istisnāʿ (contract of manufacture).
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on buying shoes with a condition that the seller will adjust them or add a strap. According to qiyas (analogy), such a condition would invalidate the sale, similar to the cloth case above. However, by istihsan (juristic preference), it is permissible because it is a common practice (ta'ammul) among people. The analogy is drawn to dyeing cloth (صبغ الثوب) where such conditions are accepted, and to the contract of istisnāʿ (manufacturing contract) which is permitted despite involving uncertainty. Thus, custom ('urf) and necessity justify departing from the strict analogy.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsān): Juristic preference that allows departing from strict analogy in favor of a more equitable ruling based on custom, necessity, or public benefit.
تعامل (taʿāmul): Common practice or custom of people in their transactions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because shoes are cheap.
B) Because it is customary and people commonly deal with such conditions.
C) Because the Prophet specifically allowed it.
D) Because adjustment is considered part of the sale.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a condition that is customary (ta'ammul) in a sale can override strict analogy (qiyas) through istihsan, making the sale valid and the condition binding.

Purchase of Cloth with Tailoring Condition is Void
Ruling that buying cloth on condition seller sews it renders the sale fasid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sale with a condition of tailoring and explain the two proofs given in the Hidayah.

Core Idea
A sale is void if the seller's additional work is stipulated — it makes the transaction a prohibited two-in-one deal.

In daily transactions, conditions are sometimes added to a sale, such as asking the seller to perform extra service. The Hanafi school carefully examines such conditions. This lesson focuses on a classic ruling from the Hidayah: buying cloth on condition that the seller cuts and sews it into a garment. You will learn why this renders the sale fasid and how the school derives this ruling from principles of contract and Prophetic prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the condition
Read the source: the sale of cloth with the condition that the seller cuts and sews it into a shirt or cloak. The author rules this sale is fasid. Notice the two specific conditions: cutting and sewing.
The condition must be stated at the time of contract.
2
Understand the first proof: condition not required by contract and gives benefit
The condition of tailoring is not an inherent part of a sale contract. It benefits one party (the buyer) exclusively. In Hanafi law, a condition that is extraneous and gives benefit to one party corrupts the contract.
Compare with conditions that are customary and equally beneficial, like delivery terms.
3
Understand the second proof: transaction within a transaction
The condition creates two deals: one for the cloth and one for the tailoring work. If the tailoring is compensated, it is a hire (ijarah) mixed with sale; if uncompensated, it is a gift (hiba) mixed with sale. Both are prohibited by the hadith forbiding 'two transactions in one'.
The hadith reference: 'Whoever makes two transactions in one transaction, he is entitled to the lesser of them or the sale is void'.
4
Analyse the authority and weight of the evidence
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah, the core transmitted corpus of the school. The dalil is a hadith (zanni thubut and dalala). The school considers the general prohibition of safqatain fi safqah as applying here.
Other schools may differentiate if the work is customary and part of the price.
5
Apply the ruling to similar cases
Now consider analogous conditions: e.g., buying a phone with condition that the seller installs a screen protector. Apply the same reasoning to see if the sale would be fasid.
Hanafi jurists distinguish based on the nature of the condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کپڑا اس شرط پر خریدا کہ بائع اسے کاٹ کر کرتا یا قبا ہی دے تو بیع فاسد ہے
قال. ومن اشترى ثوبا على ان يقطعه البائع ويخيطه قميصا او قباء فالبيع فاسد لانه شرط لا يقتضيه العقد وفيه منفعة لاحد المتعاقدين ولانه يصير صفقة في صفقة على مامر
ترجمہ اور اگر کسی نے کپڑا اس شرط پر خریدا کہ بائع اس کو کاٹ کر اس کا کرتا یا قباء بیٹے تو بیع فاسد ہے کیونکہ یہ ایسی شرط ہے جس کا عقد تقاضہ نہیں کرتا اور اس میں احد المتعاقدین کا نفع ہے اور اس لئے کہ یہ معاملہ کے اندر معاملہ ہے جیسا کہ گذرا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک آدمی نے کپڑا خریدا اور یہ شرط کی کہ بائع اس کپڑے کو کاٹ کر اس کا کرتا بنائے یا قباء بنائے تو یہ بیچ فاسد ہے کیونکہ یہ شرطا متضئی عقد کے خلاف بھی ہے اور اس میں احد العاقدین یعنی مشتری کا نفع بھی ہے اور جو شروا متقضی عقد کے خلاف ہو اور اس میں احد العاقدین کا نفع ہو تو وہ مفسد بیع ہوتی ہے اس لئے اس شرط سے بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی۔
دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ کپڑا کاٹ کر سینے کے مقابلہ میں شمن کا کوئی حصہ ہوگا یا نہیں ؟ اگر اس کے مقابلہ میں شمن کا کوئی حصہ ہے تو اجارہ بیچ میں داخل ہو جائے گا اور اگر اس کے مقابلہ میں شمن کا کوئی حصہ نہیں ہے تو اعادہ بیج میں داخل ہو جائے گا۔ اور ایک معاملہ کو دوسرے معاملہ میں داخل کرنے سے چونکہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے منع فرمایا ہے اس لئے یہ عقد فاسد اور نا جائز ہوگا۔ (بنا یہ )
If a cloth is purchased on condition that the seller cuts it and sews it into a shirt or cloak, the sale is void. [The author] said: And whoever buys a cloth on condition that the seller cuts it and sews it into a shirt or cloak, the sale is void, because it is a condition that the contract does not require, and it contains benefit for one of the two contracting parties, and because it becomes a transaction within a transaction as previously mentioned. Translation: And if someone purchased a cloth on condition that the seller cuts it and makes it into a shirt or cloak, then the sale is void, because this is a condition that the contract does not require, and it contains benefit for one of the contracting parties, and because it is a transaction within a transaction as has passed. Explanation: The scenario is that a man bought a cloth and stipulated that the seller cut the cloth and make it into a shirt or cloak. This sale is void because this condition is contrary to the requirement of the contract and it contains benefit for one of the contracting parties, i.e., the buyer. And whatever is contrary to the requirement of the contract and contains benefit for one of the contracting parties is a corrupting factor in the sale, so this condition renders the sale void. The second proof is that for cutting and sewing, will there be any portion of the price or not? If there is a portion of the price for it, then hire enters into the sale, and if there is no portion of the price for it, then a gift enters into the sale. And because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) prohibited including one transaction in another, this contract is void and impermissible.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hidayah on a sale with a condition that the seller perform additional work (cutting and sewing) on the item. The ruling: such a sale is fasid. Two proofs are given: (1) The condition is not required by the contract and gives benefit to one party (the buyer), which is a recognised cause of corruption in sales. (2) The transaction involves two deals in one: either the work is compensated (making it a hire contract mixed with sale) or it is uncompensated (making it a gift mixed with sale). Both are prohibited by a hadith of the Prophet. Therefore, the contract is invalid.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition stipulated by one of the contracting parties in a sale.
بیع فاسد (bay' fasid): A voidable sale; one that is invalid due to a defect in its conditions but can be corrected.
صفقة في صفقة (safqah fi safqah): A transaction within a transaction; combining two sales into one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a sale of cloth with condition of tailoring considered fasid in the Hanafi school?
A) Because tailoring is prohibited in Islam
B) Because it creates two transactions in one
C) Because the buyer didn't specify the price
D) Because the seller must be the tailor

Key Takeaway
A sale is fasid when an extraneous condition benefits one party and creates a transaction within a transaction, as per the Hidayah and Prophetic prohibition.

Purchase of Shoes with Condition of Repair: Istihsan Overrides Qiyas
Ruling that by qiyas such sale is fasid but by istihsan it is permissible due to custom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi ruling by qiyas and by istihsan for conditional sales and identify the role of custom (ta'amul) in overriding qiyas.

Core Idea
Custom (ta'amul) can override qiyas and make a sale valid where strict analogy would invalidate it.

This lesson examines a case where custom overrides strict analogy in Hanafi fiqh. While qiyas would render a conditional sale void because the condition benefits the buyer and contradicts the nature of the contract, istihsan based on widespread customary practice (ta'amul) makes it permissible. Understanding this principle reveals how the Hanafi school balances textual reasoning with practical necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and condition
The scenario is a sale of shoes where the seller agrees to repair (sole or add straps) as a condition. Recognize that this is a condition attached to the sale contract.
2
Derive the ruling by qiyas
By strict analogy (qiyas), the sale is fasid because the condition is not part of the contract's requirements and gives an extra benefit to the buyer, resembling a prohibited sale with an extra condition.
3
Derive the ruling by istihsan
By istihsan (juristic preference), the sale is permissible due to widespread custom (ta'amul). Custom is given precedence over qiyas in such transactions, as people commonly deal in this manner.
4
Compare with analogous cases
Similar istihsan rulings apply to hiring a dyer (vigarding dyeing cloth) and to istisna' (manufacturing contracts), both allowed due to custom despite being problematic by qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جوتا اس شرط پر خریدا کہ بائع اسے برابر کر دے گا یا تسمہ بنا کر دے گا تو بیع استحسانا جائز ہے۔
قال ومن اشترى نعلا على ان يحذوه البائع او يشركه فالبیع فاسد قال ما ذكره جواب القياس ووجهه ما بينا وفى الاستحسان يجوز التعامل فيه فصار كصبغ الثوب وللتعامل جوزنا الاستصناع
ترجمہ اور اگر چھڑا اس شرط پر خریدا کہ بائع اس کی جوتیاں بنائے یا جوتے کا تسمہ بنائے تو بیع فاسد ہے۔ مصنف نے فرمایا کہ متن میں مذکور قیاسی حکم ہے اور اس کی وجہ وہ ہے جو ہم نے بیان کی اور استحسانا جائز ہے کیونکہ اس میں لوگوں کا تعامل ہے پس یہ کمپزار نگلنے کے مانند ہو گیا اور تعامل ہی کی وجہ سے ہم نے کاریگر سے کسی چیز کے بنوانے کو جائز قرار دیا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے چھڑا اس شرط پر خریدا کہ بائع اس کا جوتا بنا کر دے یا جوتا اس شرط پر خریدا کہ بائع اس میں تسمہ لگا کر دے تو قیاس کے مطابق یہ بیع فاسد ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ شرط متقصائے عقد کے خلاف بھی ہے اور اس میں مشتری کا نفع بھی ہے ہاں تعامل ناس کی وجہ سے استحسانا اس کو جائز قرار دیا گیا جیسے رنگریز کو کپڑا رنگنے کے لئے اجرت پر لینا قیا سانا جائز ہے کیونکہ اجارہ منافع کی بیچ کا نام ہے اور یہاں عین جئی یعنی رنگ کی بیج ہے پس یہ اسی طرح نا جائز ہے جیسے دودھ پینے کے لئے گائے کو اجرت پر لینا نا جائز ہے لیکن استحسانا لوگوں کے تعامل کی وجہ سے رنگریز کو اجرت پر لینے کی اجازت دی گئی اور اسی تعامل کی وجہ سے آرڈر دیگر کوئی چیز بنوانے کی اجازت ہے حالانکہ یہ معدوم کی بیج ہے جائز نہ ہونی چاہئے تھی، لیکن لوگوں کے تعامل کی وجہ سے اس کو جائز قرار دیا گیا اور تعامل اور عرف کو قیاس پر ترجیح حاصل ہوتی ہے اس لئے ان مسائل میں تعامل کو بنیاد بنا کر جواز کا فتوی دیا گیا اگر چہ قیا سانا جائز ہے
If a shoe is purchased on condition that the seller soles it or puts a strap, the sale is void - [this is] what the author mentioned as the answer of qiyas and its reasoning is what we explained. And by istihsan it is permissible because people customarily deal in it, so it becomes like dyeing a garment, and due to custom we allowed manufacturing contract. Translation: And if a shoe is purchased on condition that the seller makes the shoes or makes the strap, the sale is void. The author said that what is mentioned in the text is the ruling of qiyas, and its reason is what we explained. And by istihsan it is permissible because people customarily deal in it. So it has become like dyeing a garment, and due to custom we allowed manufacturing. Explanation: The scenario is that a person bought a shoe on condition that the seller make the shoe and give it, or bought a shoe on condition that the seller put a strap on it. According to qiyas, this sale is void because this condition is contrary to the requirement of the contract and gives benefit to the buyer. However, due to people's custom, it is deemed permissible by istihsan, just like hiring a dyer to dye cloth is permissible by qiyas? Actually, by qiyas it is not permissible because hire is for usufruct, and here it is for the dye itself, but by istihsan it is allowed due to custom. Similarly, manufacturing (istisna') is allowed due to custom even though it is a sale of a non-existent item. Thus, custom is given precedence over qiyas, and fatwa is given on permissibility based on custom.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This ruling distinguishes between qiyas and istihsan. By strict analogy, a sale of shoes with a condition that the seller repairs them (soling or adding a strap) would be fasid for the same reasons as the previous lesson: it is a condition not required by the sale and benefits the buyer. However, the Hanafi school applies istihsan (juristic preference) to permit such transactions because of widespread custom (ta'amul). This is similar to the permissibility of hiring a dyer (where the dye itself is sold) and the contract of istisna' (manufacturing contract). Custom is given priority over qiyas in these matters, and fatwa is given accordingly. The ruling is a clear example of how Hanafi fiqh balances textual analogy with practical necessity.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method that overrides qiyas for a stronger reason like custom or necessity.
تعامل (ta'amul): Customary practice or mutual dealing among people.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning from an established case to a new case.
استصناع (istisna'): A manufacturing contract for ordered goods; a sale of a non-existent item allowed by custom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the sale of shoes with a condition of repair by the seller permissible?
A) Because it is strictly required by qiyas
B) Because custom (ta'amul) and istihsan make it permissible
C) Because the Prophet explicitly allowed it
D) Because it is a sale of a non-existent item

Key Takeaway
Custom (ta'amul) can override qiyas in Hanafi law, allowing sales that would otherwise be fasid.

Sale to Unknown Festival Dates: The Ruling of Fasid due to Jahl al-Ajal
Ruling on sale with term tied to non-Muslim festivals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when a sale with a term linked to non-Muslim festivals is fasid or sahih, and identify the key condition of mutual knowledge of the term.

Core Idea
A sale to a festival date is fasid if the date is unknown; but if both parties know it, the sale is sahih.

This lesson examines a specific scenario from al-Hidayah where the payment term is tied to non-Muslim festivals such as Nowruz or Mehrgan. The ruling hinges on whether the exact date is known to both parties. If it is unknown, the sale is void due to jahl al-ajal (ignorance of the term), which leads to dispute. However, if the date is known, the sale is valid. This demonstrates the general principle that uncertainty in a contract's essential terms invalidates it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is fixing a payment term to a festival (Nowruz, Mehrgan, Christian fast, Jewish breaking of fast). The ruling is fasid (void) when the date is unknown.
The text also provides exceptions where the sale is valid.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is not a scriptural text but a rational argument: jahl al-ajal leads to dispute (munaza'a). This is based on the Hanafi principle that major uncertainty (gharar) invalidates contracts.
The term is unknown because the festival date may not be fixed in the parties' minds.
3
Trace the condition
The fasid ruling applies only when the parties do not know the festival's date. If both know it (ma'lum 'indahuma), the sale is valid. Also, if the term is after the start of Christian fast (since its duration is known), there is no ignorance.
Knowledge must be present in both parties.
4
Note the exception
The text explicitly provides two exceptions: (1) both parties know the date, (2) the term is after the start of Christian fast (because the fast duration is known in days). In such cases, the sale is valid.
This shows that certainty can be established even with an event-based term if the duration is known.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نوروز، مهرگان، صوم نصاری ، فطر یہود بیع کے لئے مدت ٹھہرانا جب کہ متبايعان اس کو نہ جانتے ہوں بیع فاسد ہے
قال والبيع الى النيروزو المهرجان وصوم النصارى وفطر اليهود اذا لم يعرف المتبايعان ذالک فاسد لجهالة الأجل وهى مفضية الى المنازعة فى البيع لا بتنائها على المماكسة الا اذا كانا يعرفانه لكونه معلوما عندهما أو كان التاجيل الى فطر النصارى بعد ما شرعوا في صومهم لان مدة صومهم بالايام معلومة فلا جهالة فيه
ترجمہ اور بیع نوروز ، مہرگان ، نصاری کے روزوں اور یہود کے افطار کے وعدہ پر فاسد ہے جبکہ بائع اور مشتری اس کو پہچانتے نہ ہوں کیونکہ میعاد مجہول ہے اور بیج کے اندر مجہول ہو نا مفضی الی المنازعہ ہے کیونکہ ٹال مٹول پر مبنی ہے مگر جبکہ دونوں اس کو پہچانتے ہوں کیونکہ بائع اور مشتری کو میعاد معلوم ہے یا میعاد نصاری کے افطار کے وعدہ پر ہو ان کے روزے شروع کرنے کے بعد کیونکہ ان کے روزوں کی مدت ایام کے ذریعہ معلوم ہے اس لئے مدت میں جہالت نہ ہوگی ۔ تشریح نیز روز نوروز کا مغرب ہے اس کا سب سے پہلے حضرت عمر رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ نے تکلم فرمایا ہے یعنی جب کفار اس دن میں خوشیاں مناتے تھے تو حضرت عمر نے فرمایا كل يوم لنا نوروز ، ہمارے لئے ہر دن نوروز ہے۔ نو روز موسم ربیع کا پہلا دن ہے اور مہر جان مہرگان کا مغرب ہے مہرگان موسم خریف کا پہلا دن ہے۔
صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے کوئی سامان خریدا اور ثمن ادا کرنے کے لئے تو روز کا دن یا مهرگان کا دن مقر کیا یا یہ کہا کہ جس دن نصاری روزے شروع کریں گے اس دن ادا کروں گا یا یہ کہا کہ یہود کے افطار کے دن یعنی ان کی عید کے دن ادا کروں گا ۔ ان تمام صورتوں میں بیع فاسد ہے لیکن ان صورتوں میں بیج اسی وقت فاسد ہوگی جبکہ بائع اور مشتری کو ان ایام کا علم نہ ہو ۔ اور اگر ان ایام کا علم ہو تو
And the sale to Nowruz, Mehrgan, the fast of Christians, and the breaking of fast of Jews, when the two contracting parties do not know that, is void due to ignorance of the term, and it leads to dispute in the sale because it is based on postponement. Except when they both know it, because it is known to them, or if the term is to the breaking of fast of the Christians after they have started their fast, because the duration of their fast is known by days, so there is no ignorance in it. Translation: And the sale on credit to Nowruz, Mehrgan, the fast of Christians, and the breaking of fast of Jews is void when the buyer and seller do not recognize it, because the term is unknown, and ignorance in sale leads to dispute, as it is based on delay. Except when both recognize it, because the term is known to them, or if the term is to the breaking of fast of the Christians after they have started their fast, because the duration of their fast is known by days, so there is no ignorance in the term. Explanation: Nowruz is the first day of spring, it is a Persian festival. Mehrgan is the first day of autumn. The scenario: if someone buys an item and fixes as the payment term the day of Nowruz or Mehrgan, or says 'on the day the Christians start fasting', or 'on the day of the breaking of fast of the Jews', in all these the sale is void if the parties do not know these dates. But if they know them, the sale is valid.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This ruling addresses sales where the payment term is fixed to a specific future event that is not a fixed calendar date. If the event's date is not known to the contracting parties, the sale is fasid because the term is unknown (jahl al-ajal), which leads to dispute. However, if both parties know the date (e.g., they know when Nowruz falls), or if the term is defined by a known duration (like after Christians start fasting, because their fast has a known number of days), then the term is known and the sale is valid. This shows the importance of certainty in contracts.

Key Terms
نوروز (nowruz): The Persian New Year, the first day of spring.
مهرگان (mehrgan): The Persian autumn festival, the first day of autumn.
جهالة الأجل (jahl al-ajal): Ignorance of the term or due date in a contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if someone sells an item with payment due on the day of Nowruz, the sale is:
A) Always valid
B) Always invalid
C) Valid only if both parties know the date of Nowruz
D) Valid only if Nowruz falls within a year

Key Takeaway
A sale whose term is based on a non-Muslim festival is fasid only if the date is unknown to the contracting parties; if known, it is sahih.

Buying a Strap with Condition: Qiyas vs Istihsan
Ruling on conditional sale with work by seller: qiyas vs istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the qiyas and istihsan rulings for a conditional sale (buying a strap with condition to make shoes) and apply the principle that custom can override qiyas in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Custom can override qiyas: istihsan permits what strict analogy forbids.

You walk into a shop to buy a shoe strap, but you also ask the seller to make the shoes. Is this sale valid? If we follow strict analogy (qiyas), the sale is invalid because it includes an extra condition that benefits the buyer. However, the Hanafi school recognizes that people commonly engage in such transactions, so by juristic preference (istihsan) the sale is permissible. This lesson examines how custom ('urf) can change a ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transaction and its ruling by qiyas
The transaction is buying a strap (or shoe) with a condition that the seller does work (makes shoes or attaches a strap). According to qiyas, this sale is fasid (invalid) because the condition is not required by the contract and gives the buyer a benefit without additional consideration.
The text says 'bi' fasid' – the sale is invalid.
2
Understand the reason for the qiyas ruling
The condition is contrary to the requirement of the contract (muqtada al-'aqd) and involves a benefit for the buyer, which makes it a conditional sale that is generally invalid in strict analogy.
Analogous to other cases like hiring a cow for its milk or hiring a dyer for dye – these are also invalid by qiyas.
3
Learn the istihsan argument
Despite qiyas, the Hanafi school uses istihsan (juristic preference) to permit the sale because of the widespread custom (ta'amul) of people engaging in such transactions. Custom is recognized as a source of law in commercial matters.
The commentator compares this to hiring a dyer – invalid by qiyas but permitted by istihsan due to custom.
4
Compare with analogous cases
The text analogizes the strap case with hiring a dyer to dye cloth and ordering any item to be made. In both, strict analogy would invalidate the contract because it involves a sale of a non-existent item or a sale of the actual material (like dye) instead of benefits. But custom makes them permissible.
The underlying principle is that custom is given precedence over qiyas.
5
Apply the principle
The operative ruling (mufta bihi) is permissibility (ja'iz) due to custom. When issuing fatwa, the mufti should follow this istihsan position because it reflects the actual practice of Muslims and prevents hardship.
This is a classic example of Hanafi istihsan based on 'urf.

اور اگر چھڑا اس شرط پر خریدا کہ بائع اس کی جوتیاں بنائے یا جوتے کا تسمہ بنائے تو بیع فاسد ہے۔ مصنف نے فرمایا کہ متن میں مذکور قیاسی حکم ہے اور اس کی وجہ وہ ہے جو ہم نے بیان کی اور استحسانا جائز ہے کیونکہ اس میں لوگوں کا تعامل ہے پس یہ کمپزار نگلنے کے مانند ہو گیا اور تعامل ہی کی وجہ سے ہم نے کاریگر سے کسی چیز کے بنوانے کو جائز قرار دیا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے چھڑا اس شرط پر خریدا کہ بائع اس کا جوتا بنا کر دے یا جوتا اس شرط پر خریدا کہ بائع اس میں تسمہ لگا کر دے تو قیاس کے مطابق یہ بیع فاسد ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ شرط متقصائے عقد کے خلاف بھی ہے اور اس میں مشتری کا نفع بھی ہے ہاں تعامل ناس کی وجہ سے استحسانا اس کو جائز قرار دیا گیا جیسے رنگریز کو کپڑا رنگنے کے لئے اجرت پر لینا قیاسانا جائز ہے کیونکہ اجارہ منافع کی بیچ کا نام ہے اور یہاں عین جئی یعنی رنگ کی بیج ہے پس یہ اسی طرح نا جائز ہے جیسے دودھ پینے کے لئے گائے کو اجرت پر لینا نا جائز ہے لیکن استحسانا لوگوں کے تعامل کی وجہ سے رنگریز کو اجرت پر لینے کی اجازت دی گئی اور اسی تعامل کی وجہ سے آرڈر دیگر کوئی چیز بنوانے کی اجازت ہے حالانکہ یہ معدوم کی بیج ہے جائز نہ ہونی چاہئے تھی، لیکن لوگوں کے تعامل کی وجہ سے اس کو جائز قرار دیا گیا اور تعامل اور عرف کو قیاس پر ترجیح حاصل ہوتی ہے اس لئے ان مسائل میں تعامل کو بنیاد بنا کر جواز کا فتوی دیا گیا اگر چہ قیاسانا جائز ہے
And if he bought a strap with the condition that the seller make his shoes, or [bought] a shoe with the condition that the seller make a strap for it, then the sale is invalid (fasid). The author said that the ruling mentioned in the text is by qiyas, and its reason is what we have stated, and by istihsan it is permissible because there is people's custom (ta'amul) in it. Thus it became like [the case of] a weaver [contract] and because of custom we permitted having an artisan make something. Explanation: The issue is that a person bought a strap with the condition that the seller make his shoe, or bought a shoe with the condition that the seller attach a strap to it. According to qiyas, this sale is invalid because this condition is contrary to the requirement of the contract and also contains benefit for the buyer. However, due to people's custom, it is deemed permissible by istihsan, just like hiring a dyer to dye cloth is impermissible by qiyas because hire (ijarah) is a sale of benefits, but here it is a sale of the actual dye (ayn), so it is impermissible like hiring a cow for its milk. But by istihsan, due to people's custom, hiring a dyer is permitted, and similarly, ordering any item to be made is permitted even though it is a sale of a non-existent item, which should not be permissible. However, due to people's custom, it has been deemed permissible. And custom (ta'amul) and 'urf take precedence over qiyas. Therefore, in these issues, permissibility is pronounced based on custom, even if it is impermissible by qiyas.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific transaction: buying a strap (chhada) or a shoe with a condition that the seller will make something (shoes or a strap) for the buyer. The author begins by noting the ruling according to qiyas (analogical reasoning): such a sale is fasid (invalid). The reason is that the condition is not required by the contract itself and it provides benefit to the buyer without additional consideration, which makes it a conditional sale that is generally impermissible. However, the text then introduces istihsan (juristic preference) based on the custom (ta'amul) of people. Because people commonly engage in such transactions, the Hanafi school deems them permissible. The commentator draws an analogy with hiring a dyer or ordering any item to be made, which by qiyas would be invalid because it involves the sale of a non-existent object (ma'dum) or a sale of an 'ayn (like dye) when the contract should be for benefits. But due to widespread custom, these are permitted. The key principle is that recognized custom can override the result of qiyas. This is a classic Hanafi use of istihsan where the strict analogy is set aside in favor of practice and necessity.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that sets aside the result of qiyas in favor of a different ruling due to custom, necessity, or other considerations.
تعامل (ta'amul): The prevalent custom or practice of people in transactions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the sale of a strap with the condition that the seller makes shoes considered permissible despite qiyas?
A) Because the condition is required by the contract.
B) Because the buyer needs shoes.
C) Because of the widespread custom (ta'amul) of people.
D) Because the strap is cheap.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, istihsan based on custom can override the result of qiyas to permit transactions that are commonly practiced, even if they would otherwise be invalid.

Deferred Payment to Unknown Festivals: Ignorance of Term Invalidates
Ruling on deferred payment tied to unknown festivals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sales deferred to unknown festivals and explain why ignorance of the term invalidates the sale.

Core Idea
A sale is invalid if the payment term is unknown because uncertainty leads to dispute.

This passage deals with a common scenario in earlier times: setting a payment deadline based on a festival or religious observance that does not have a fixed date. The Hanafi school rules that such a sale is fasid (invalid) if the parties do not know when that event will occur, because the term becomes unknown (majhool), and any contractual uncertainty that leads to dispute invalidates the transaction. However, if the parties know the date of the festival, or if the term becomes determinable (e.g., after Christians start fasting, the remaining days to their Eid are fixed), the sale is valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
List the four scenarios: deferred to Nawroz, Mihrajan, Christian fasts, Jewish Eid. The ruling is fasid when the parties are ignorant of the dates.
2
Locate the illa (effective cause)
The cause is jahalat al-ajal (ignorance of the term), which leads to dispute (mufdi ila al-munaza'ah) because it opens the door to procrastination.
3
Apply the exceptions
When both parties know the dates, the term is known so the sale is valid. Also, if deferment is to Christian Eid after starting their fast, the term becomes known because the number of days is fixed.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a difference of opinion on whether Christians fast 50 or 55 days, but both agree the term is known after fasting starts.
5
Derive the general principle
Any term that is unknown at the time of contract renders the sale fasid; if it can be known with certainty, the sale is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال والبيع الى النيروزو المهرجان وصوم النصارى وفطر اليهود اذا لم يعرف المتبايعان ذالک فاسد لجهالة الأجل وهى مفضية الى المنازعة فى البيع لا بتنائها على المماكسة الا اذا كانا يعرفانه لكونه معلوما عندهما أو كان التاجيل الى فطر النصارى بعد ما شرعوا في صومهم لان مدة صومهم بالايام معلومة فلا جهالة فيه۔ ترجمہ اور بیع نوروز ، مہرگان ، نصاری کے روزوں اور یہود کے افطار کے وعدہ پر فاسد ہے جبکہ بائع اور مشتری اس کو پہچانتے نہ ہوں کیونکہ میعاد مجہول ہے اور بیج کے اندر مجہول ہونا مفضی الی المنازعہ ہے کیونکہ ٹال مٹول پر مبنی ہے مگر جبکہ دونوں اس کو پہچانتے ہوں کیونکہ بائع اور مشتری کو میعاد معلوم ہے یا میعاد نصاری کے افطار کے وعدہ پر ہو ان کے روزے شروع کرنے کے بعد کیونکہ ان کے روزوں کی مدت ایام کے ذریعہ معلوم ہے اس لئے مدت میں جہالت نہ ہوگی ۔ تشریح نیز روز نوروز کا مغرب ہے اس کا سب سے پہلے حضرت عمر رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ نے تکلم فرمایا ہے یعنی جب کفار اس دن میں خوشیاں مناتے تھے تو حضرت عمر نے فرمایا كل يوم لنا نوروز ، ہمارے لئے ہر دن نوروز ہے۔ نوروز موسم ربیع کا پہلا دن ہے اور مہرجان مہرگان کا مغرب ہے مہرگان موسم خریف کا پہلا دن ہے۔ صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے کوئی سامان خریدا اور ثمن ادا کرنے کے لئے نوروز کا دن یا مهرگان کا دن مقر کیا یا یہ کہا کہ جس دن نصاری روزے شروع کریں گے اس دن ادا کروں گا یا یہ کہا کہ یہود کے افطار کے دن یعنی ان کی عید کے دن ادا کروں گا ۔ ان تمام صورتوں میں بیع فاسد ہے لیکن ان صورتوں میں بیع اسی وقت فاسد ہوگی جبکہ بائع اور مشتری کو ان ایام کا علم نہ ہو ۔ اور اگر ان ایام کا علم ہو تو بیع فاسد نہ ہوگی۔ وجہ فساد یہ ہے کہ بائع اور مشتری کو جب ان ایام کا علم نہیں ہے تو ثمن کی میعاد مجہول ہو گئی ہے اور بیع کے اندر میعاد کا مجہول ہونا چونکہ کمال مسول پر مبنی ہے اس لئے میعاد کی جہالت مقتضی الی المنازعہ ہوگی اور جو جہالت مقتضی الی المنازعہ ہو وہ مفسد بیع ہوتی ہے اس لئے ان صورتوں میں بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی ۔ اور اگر بائع اور مشتری مذکورہ ایام کو پہچانتے ہوں تو بیع فاسد نہ ہوگی کیونکہ اس صورت میں بائع اور مشتری کو میعاد معلوم ہے اور اگر نصاری کے روزے شروع ہونے کے بعد نصاری کے افطار یعنی عید کے دن کو میعاد قرار دیا تو بھی بیع فاسد نہ ہوگی کیونکہ اس صورت میں ان کے روزوں کی تعداد معلوم ہے یعنی بقول صاحب عنایہ کے ان کے پچاس روزے ہیں۔ اور بقول علامہ ابن الہمام کے پچپن روزے ہیں۔ روزے شروع کرنے کے بعد جب بیع ہوئی اور عید نصاری کا دن ثمن کی ادائیگی کے لئے مقرر کیا گیا تو اس صورت میں ان کی عید کا دن معلوم ہے کیونکہ بیع کے دن یہ بھی معلوم ہے کہ کتنے روز گذر چکے ہیں اور جب گزارے ہوئے روزوں کا علم ہے تو جو باقی رہ گئے ان کا بھی علم ہو گا کیونکہ ان کے مذہب میں پچاس یا پچپن روزوں سے زائد نہیں ہوتے ۔ حاصل یہ کہ اس صورت میں افطار کا دن معلوم ہے اور جب افطار کا دن معلوم ہے تو میعاد مجہول نہ رہی بلکہ معلوم ہوگی ۔ اور میعاد معلوم ہونے کی صورت میں بیع فاسد نہیں ہوتی اس لئے اس صورت میں بیع فاسد نہ ہوگی ۔
He said: And the sale deferred to Nawroz, Mihrajan, the fast of the Christians, and the breaking of the fast of the Jews is invalid when the two parties do not know that, due to ignorance of the term, and it leads to dispute in the sale because it is based on procrastination. Unless they both know it, because it is known to them, or the deferment is to the breaking of the fast of the Christians after they have started their fast, because the duration of their fast is known by days, so there is no ignorance in it. Translation: And the sale to Nawroz, Mihrajan, the fasts of the Christians, and the breaking of the fast of the Jews on a promise is invalid when the seller and buyer do not recognize it, because the term is unknown, and ignorance in sale leads to dispute because it is based on evasion. But when both recognize it, because the seller and buyer know the term, or the term is to the breaking of the fast of the Christians after they start their fast, because the duration of their fast is known by days, so there is no ignorance in the term. Explanation: Also, the day of Nawroz is uncertain; it was first spoken of by Umar (may Allah be pleased with him), meaning when the disbelievers celebrated on that day, Umar said, 'Every day is Nawroz for us.' Nawroz is the first day of spring, and Mihrajan is the first day of autumn. The issue is: if someone buys goods and sets the day of Nawroz or Mihrajan for payment, or says 'I will pay on the day the Christians start their fast' or 'on the day of the Jews' breaking of the fast (their Eid)', in all these cases the sale is invalid, but only if the seller and buyer do not know those days. If they know those days, the sale is not invalid. The reason for invalidity is that when the seller and buyer do not know those days, the term for payment becomes unknown, and ignorance of the term in a sale leads to dispute, and any ignorance that leads to dispute invalidates the sale. So in these cases, the sale is invalid. But if the seller and buyer recognize the mentioned days, the sale is not invalid because the term is known to them. And if after the Christians have started their fast, the term is set to their breaking of the fast (Eid), then the sale is also not invalid because in that case the number of their fast days is known: according to Sahib al-'Inayah, they have fifty fasts, and according to Allama Ibn al-Humam, fifty-five. Once the fast has started and the sale is made, and the day of Christian Eid is set for payment, that day is known because on the day of sale it is known how many days have passed, and when the number of passed days is known, the remaining days are also known, because in their religion they do not exceed fifty or fifty-five days. So in this case, the day of breaking the fast is known, and when it is known, the term is not unknown but known. And when the term is known, the sale is not invalid.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage deals with the validity of a sale where payment is deferred to a specific but variable event, such as a festival or religious observance that does not have a fixed date according to the Gregorian calendar (like Nawroz, Mihrajan, Christian fasts, Jewish Eid). The ruling is that if the parties are ignorant of the actual date of that event, the term is considered unknown (majhool), and such uncertainty leads to potential dispute, which invalidates the sale. However, if both parties know the date (e.g., they know when Nawroz falls), then the term is known and the sale is valid. Also, if the deferment is to the Christian Eid after they have started their fast, the number of days remaining becomes known (50 or 55 days according to different scholars), so the term is no longer unknown. The commentary explains that the reason for invalidity is that ignorance of the term (jahalat al-ajal) leads to dispute, which is a fundamental flaw in sales. The example of Umar's statement indicates that for Muslims, every day is like Nawroz, so there is no special significance that would cause confusion. The key principle is that any term that is unknown at the time of the contract renders the sale invalid, unless it can be determined with reasonable certainty.

Key Terms
جہالت الاجل (jahalat al-ajal): Ignorance or uncertainty regarding the due date or term of payment in a sale.
مفضی الی المنازعہ (mufdi ila al-munaza'ah): Leading to dispute or conflict, used to describe an uncertainty that is likely to cause disagreement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man sells an item with payment due on the day Christians start their fast. Neither party knows exactly when that is. What is the ruling?
A) The sale is valid because the event will happen.
B) The sale is invalid because the term is unknown.
C) The sale is valid if the seller fixes the date later.
D) The sale is suspended until the fast begins.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling: a sale is invalid if the payment term is unknown at the time of contract because ignorance leads to dispute; but if the term is known or can be determined, the sale is valid.
