Deferring Payment to Uncertain Seasons: Sale vs Kafala
Ruling on sale deferred to uncertain seasonal events; exception for kafala.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on deferring payment to uncertain seasonal events in sale and kafala, and explain the underlying principle of tolerance for ignorance.

Core Idea
Sale cannot tolerate uncertainty in the term; kafala can, because it is a gratuitous contract.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a practical scenario: deferring payment to a vague future event like harvest or the coming of pilgrims. The author explains why such a deferment invalidates a sale but is permissible in a suretyship (kafala). Understanding this distinction hinges on the Hanafi principle that commutative contracts require certainty, while gratuitous contracts tolerate minor ignorance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for sale
Read the opening sentence. The author states it is not permissible to sell with payment deferred to uncertain events. Note that the ruling is fasid (invalid) because the term is unknown.
2
Identify the ruling for kafala
Contrast with the next sentence: if one guarantees (kafala) a debt up to these times, it is permissible. The reason given is that slight ignorance (jahala yasira) is tolerated in kafala.
3
Analyze the analogy (qiyas)
The author uses qiyas: in sale, ignorance in the principal sum invalidates, so ignorance in its description (term) also invalidates. In kafala, ignorance in the original debt is tolerated, so ignorance in the term is even more tolerated.
This is a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) based on the nature of the contracts.
4
Distinguish deferment after absolute sale
The passage notes an exception: if the sale is concluded absolutely and then the price is deferred to these times, it is permissible. This is because it becomes a deferment of an existing debt, similar to kafala, and the slight ignorance is tolerated.
5
Apply the principle to new scenarios
Consider other uncertain terms like 'when it rains' or 'next market day'. Use the same reasoning: sale invalid, kafala valid. Also consider whether a condition for certainty can be fulfilled later; only absolute deferment after the contract is allowed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غال ولا يجوز البيع الى قدوم الحاج وکذالک الى الحصاد والدياس والقطاف والجزاز لانها تتقدم وتتاخر وار نفل إلى هذه الأوقات جازلان الجهالة اليسيرة متحملة فى الكفالة وهذه الجهالة يسيرة مستدركة لاختلاف الصحابة فيها ولا نه معلوم الاصل الاترى انها تحتمل الجهالة فى اصل الدين بان تكفل بما ذاب على فلان ففى الوصف أولى بخلاف البيع فانه لا يحتملها فى اصل الثمن فكذافى وصفه بخلاف ما اذا باع مطلقا ئم اجل الثمن الى هذه الاوقات حيث جازلان هذا تاجيل فى الدين وهذه الجهالة فيه متحملة بمنزلة الكفالة ولا كذالك اشتراطه فى اصل العقد لانه يبطل بالشرط الفاسد ترجمہ اور حاجیوں کے آنے کے (وعدہ پر ) بیع جائز نہیں ہے اور اسی طرح کھیتی کٹنے کے وقت اور گانے کے وقت اور انگور توڑے جانے کے وقت اور اون کاٹے جانے کے وقت تک کیونکہ یہ چیزیں آگے پیچھے ہوتی ہی رہتی ہیں۔ اور اگر ان اوقات تک قرضہ کی کفالت کی تو جائز ہے اسلیے کہ کفالت میں تھوڑی جہالت برداشت ہوتی ہے اور یہ جہالت ایسی خفیف ہے کہ اس کا تدارک ممکن ہے کیونکہ صحابہ اس طرح کی مجہول مدت میں مختلف ہیں اور اس لئے کہ جو اصل ہے وہ معدوم ہے کیا نہیں دیکھتے ہو کہ اصلی قرضہ کا مجمبول ہونا برداشت کر لیا جاتا ہے بایں طور کہ ( یہ کہا ) جو کچھ تیر افلاں شخص پر واجب ہو میں اس کا کفیل ہوں تو وصف کے اندر بدرجہ اولی (جہالت برداشت ہوگی ) بر خلاف بیع کے کیونکہ اصل ثمن میں جہالت برداشت نہیں ہوتی ہے پس اس طرح اس کے وصف میں بھی برداشت نہ ہوگی برخلاف اس کے کہ جب مطلقا فروخت کیا پھر بائع نے ان اوقات تک ثمن کو مؤجل کیا تو جائز ہے کیونکہ یہ دین میں میعادی مہلت ہے اور ادائے قرض
He said: And it is not permissible to sell up to the coming of the pilgrims, and likewise up to the harvest, threshing, grape-picking, and shearing, because these advance and delay. And if he guarantees (kafala) a debt up to these times, it is permissible because slight ignorance is tolerated in kafala, and this ignorance is slight and rectifiable because the Companions differed about it, and because it is known in origin. Do you not see that ignorance is tolerated in the original debt such that one says, 'I am surety for whatever is owed to you by so-and-so'? So in the description, it is more appropriate. Contrary to sale, because it does not tolerate ignorance in the original price, so likewise in its description. Unlike when he sells absolutely then defers the price to these times, for it is permissible because this is a deferment of a debt, and this ignorance in it is tolerated like kafala. But stipulating it in the original contract is not, because it is invalidated by an invalid condition.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage distinguishes between a sale that is deferred to uncertain seasonal events (such as the arrival of pilgrims, harvest, threshing, grape-picking, wool shearing) and a guarantee (kafala) that is deferred to the same events. The ruling is that in a sale, deferring payment to such uncertain times is not permissible because the term is unknown and this ignorance cannot be tolerated in sale contracts. However, in a suretyship (kafala) contract, slight ignorance is tolerated because the contract is based on beneficence (tabarru') and can absorb some uncertainty, as evidenced by the fact that the Companions had differing views on similar terms, and even the original debt can be unknown (e.g., 'I guarantee whatever is owed to you'). Since the original can tolerate ignorance, the description (i.e., the term) is even more lenient. The passage further distinguishes between stipulating such a term in the original sale contract (invalid) and deferring payment to those times after the sale has been made absolutely (this is permissible because it becomes a deferment of an existing debt). The key principle is that ignorance in the principal sum (asl al-thaman) invalidates the sale, so ignorance in its description (the term) also invalidates it. But for kafala, the original debt can be unknown, so the term being unknown is also acceptable.

Key Terms
كفالة (kafala): Suretyship; a contract where one person guarantees a debt or obligation of another.
جهالة يسيرة (jahala yasira): Slight or minor ignorance that can be tolerated in certain contracts like kafala.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is deferring payment to an uncertain harvest allowed in kafala but not in sale?
A) Because kafala is a commutative contract.
B) Because sale is a gratuitous contract.
C) Because kafala tolerates slight ignorance, but sale does not.
D) Because harvest is always in summer.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, uncertainty in the term invalidates a sale but is permissible in a suretyship (kafala) due to the differing natures of the contracts.

Ruling on Setting Payment Term to Christian Fast Days
Ruling on validity of sale with payment term tied to Christian fasting days.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when a sale with a term tied to Christian fasting days is valid or invalid and apply the Hanafi rule on known vs unknown terms.

Core Idea
A sale is valid if the payment term is known; an unknown term that can be calculated is considered known.

This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah examines a unique scenario: a sale where the payment term is linked to the fasting period of Christians. The core issue is whether the term is known (ma'lum) or unknown (majhul), which determines the validity under Hanafi fiqh. The commentator expands on the general principle that an unknown term invalidates a sale to show how this applies to non-Islamic calendars and calculations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a sale (bay') with deferred payment (salam or ordinary sale with deferred price). The ruling depends on the certainty of the payment term.
This is not a specific sale type but a general rule applied to deferred payment.
2
Distinguish the three scenarios
The passage presents three cases: (1) parties know the Christian fast days → valid; (2) parties do not know them → invalid; (3) term set to Eid after fast has started → valid because remaining days are calculable.
The third scenario is the focus of the expansion.
3
Extract the condition for validity
The condition is that the payment term must be known (ma'lum) to both parties at the time of the contract. Unknown terms lead to dispute (munaza'ah), which invalidates the sale.
Hanafi fiqh distinguishes between slight (yasira) and substantial (fahisha) ignorance.
4
Apply the calculation logic
When the term is set to a fixed event (Christian Eid) after the fasting period has started, the number of remaining days can be calculated because the total number of fast days is known (50 or 55). Thus the term becomes known.
The difference between 50 and 55 does not invalidate because it is a known range, not complete uncertainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب البيوع بیع فاسد نہ ہوگی۔
اشرف الهدا به شرح اردو برای جلد داشتم
وجہ فساد یہ ہے کہ بائع اور مشتری کو جب ان ایام کا علم نہیں ہے تو شمن کی میعاد مجہول ہو گئی ہے اور بیچ کے اندر میعاد کا مجہول ہونا چونکہ کمال مسول پر مبنی ہے اس لئے میعاد کی جہالت مخضی الی المنازعہ ہوگی اور جو جہالت مقتضی الی المنازعہ ہو وہ مفسد بیج ہوتی ہے اس لئے ان صورتوں میں بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی ۔ اور اگر بائع اور مشتری مذکورہ ایام کو پہچانتے ہوں تو بیع فاسد نہ ہوگی کیونکہ اس صورت میں بائع اور مشتری کو میعاد معلوم ہے اور اگر نصاری کے روزے شروع ہونے کے بعد نصاری کے افطار یعنی عید کے دن کو میعاد قرار دیا تو بھی بیچ فاسد نہ ہوگی کیونکہ اس صورت میں ان کے روزوں کی تعداد معلوم ہے یعنی بقول صاحب عنایہ کے ان کے پچاس روزے ہیں۔ اور بقول علامہ ابن الہمام کے پچپن روزے ہیں پیس روزے شروع کرنے کے بعد جب بیج ہوئی اور عید نصاری کا دن شمن کی ادائیگی کے لئے مقرر کیا گیا تو اس صورت میں ان کی عید کا دن معلوم ہے کیونکہ بیج کے دن یہ بھی معلوم ہے کہ کتنے روز گذر چکے ہیں اور جب گزارے ہوئے روزوں کا علم ہے تو جو باقی رہ گئے ان کا بھی علم ہو گا کیونکہ ان کے مذہب میں پچاس یا پچپن روزوں سے زائد نہیں ہوتے ۔ حاصل یہ کہ اس صورت میں اتھارٹی کے افکار کا دن معلوم ہے اور جب افطار کا ان معلوم ہے تو میعاد مجہول نہ رہی بلکہ معلوم ہوگی ۔ اور میعاد معلوم ہونے کی صو میں بیچ کا سر نہیں ہوئی اس لئے اس صورت میں بیع فاسد نہ ہوگی ۔
Book of sales. The sale will not be invalid. Reason for invalidity is that when the seller and buyer do not know those days, the term of payment becomes unknown, and unknown term in a sale leads to dispute, and dispute invalidates the sale. So in these cases the sale is invalid. But if the seller and buyer know the mentioned days, the sale is not invalid because the term is known. And if, after the Christians have started their fast, the term is set to the day of their breaking of fast (Eid), then also the sale is not invalid because in that case the number of their fasts is known: according to Sahib al-Inayah, they have fifty fasts; according to Allama Ibn al-Humam, fifty-five fasts. When the sale occurred after the start of the fasts and the day of Christian Eid is set for payment, then their Eid day is known because it is known how many days have passed, and knowing the past days gives knowledge of the remaining days since their sect has no more than fifty or fifty-five fasts. Summary: in this case, the day of their breaking of fast is known, so the term is not unknown but known. With the term known, the sale is not invalid; thus in this case the sale is not invalid.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah addresses the validity of a sale where the payment term is linked to the fasting period of Christians. The discussion is an expansion of the principle that a sale is invalid if the term is unknown (majhul) because such uncertainty leads to dispute. The author first states the general rule: if neither seller nor buyer knows the exact days of the Christian fast, the term is unknown, and the sale is fasid (invalid). This is because the unknown term is a cause of dispute, which in turn invalidates the contract. However, if both parties are aware of the days, the term is known and the sale is valid. The passage then examines a specific scenario: the term is set to the Christian Eid (the day they break their fast) after they have already started fasting. In this case, the number of fast days is known (50 or 55 depending on the scholar), so when the contract is made after some days have passed, the remaining days can be calculated. Thus the Eid day becomes known, and the sale is valid. This shows that the Hanafi school carefully considers whether the uncertainty (jahala) in the term is slight or substantial; slight uncertainty that can be resolved does not invalidate the contract.

Key Terms
میعاد (mi'ad): The appointed term for payment of the price in a sale.
جہالت (jahala): Lack of knowledge causing uncertainty about a critical element of the contract.
بیع فاسد (bay' fasid): A sale that is defective in its conditions but can be rectified by removing the defect; not completely void.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the discussed scenario, if a seller sets the payment term to the Christian Eid after the fast has started, and the parties do not know the exact number of days remaining, is the sale valid?
A) Yes, because the number of fast days is fixed in their religion.
B) No, because the term is still unknown.
C) Yes, because any unknown term is permissible in sales.
D) No, because uncertainty always invalidates the sale.

Key Takeaway
A sale is valid if the payment term is known or can be determined by calculation; uncertainty that leads to dispute invalidates the sale.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

12 min
Sale with Term to Hajj or Harvest: Invalid; But Valid in Kafalah
Ruling with proof on payment term uncertainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on setting a payment term to uncertain events in a sale, explain why it is fasid, and distinguish the case of kafalah.

Core Idea
A sale with an uncertain payment term is fasid; but the same term in kafalah is valid because kafalah tolerates slight uncertainty.

In this lesson, we examine a key Hanafi ruling from the Hidayah: if a buyer and seller agree that payment is due upon the arrival of pilgrims or the harvest, the sale is invalid (fasid) because the term is unknown. However, if the same uncertain term is used in a contract of guarantee (kafalah), it is valid. Why the difference? The author explains through a comparison with kafalah, which is more tolerant of minor uncertainty because it resembles a voluntary vow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is a sale (bay') where the payment term is set to an uncertain future event like the arrival of pilgrims (hajj) or harvest. The ruling: such a sale is fasid (invalid) in the Hanafi school.
The term 'fasid' means the contract is defective and not enforceable.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The proof is rational: these events are not fixed in time; they can come early or late. Thus the payment term is unknown, and uncertainty in the price or term invalidates a commutative contract like sale.
The proof is based on qiyas and the principle that sale requires certainty (ma'lum).
3
Contrast with kafalah
If the same uncertain term is used in a kafalah (surety) contract, the kafalah is valid because kafalah tolerates slight uncertainty (jahala yasira). This is because kafalah is analogous to a vow (nazr), which is voluntary and can tolerate minor unknowns.
The difference among the Companions (e.g., Aisha vs. Ibn Abbas) proves the uncertainty is slight and manageable.
4
Distinguish original stipulation vs. subsequent deferment
If the uncertain term is stipulated in the original sale contract, the sale is fasid. But if the sale is made absolutely (without condition) and later the parties agree to defer payment to an uncertain time, this deferment is valid because it is a modification of an existing debt, similar to kafalah.
The original contract must be free from uncertainty; subsequent changes are more lenient.

غال ولا يجوز البيع الى قدوم الحاج وکذالک الى الحصاد والدياس والقطاف والجزاز لانها تتقدم وتتاخر وار نفل إلى هذه الأوقات جازلان الجهالة اليسيرة متحملة فى الكفالة وهذه الجهالة يسيرة مستدركة لاختلاف الصحابة فيها ولا نه معلوم الاصل الاترى انها تحتمل الجهالة فى اصل الدين بان تكفل بما ذاب على فلان ففى الوصف أولى بخلاف البيع فانه لا يحتملها فى اصل الثمن فكذافى وصفه بخلاف ما اذا باع مطلقا ئم اجل الثمن الى هذه الاوقات حيث جازلان هذا تاجيل فى الدين وهذه الجهالة فيه متحملة بمنزلة الكفالة ولا كذالك اشتراطه فى اصل العقد لانه يبطل بالشرط الفاسد
ترجمہ اور حاجیوں کے آنے کے (وعدہ پر ) بیع جائز نہیں ہے اور اسی طرح کھیتی کٹنے کے وقت اور گانے کے وقت اور انگور توڑے جانے کے وقت اور اون کاٹے جانے کے وقت تک کیونکہ یہ چیزیں آگے پیچھے ہوتی رہتی ہیں۔ اور اگر ان اوقات تک قرضہ کی کفالت کی تو جائز ہے اسلیے کہ کفالت میں تھوڑی جہالت برداشت ہوتی ہے اور یہ جہالت ایسی خفیف ہے کہ اس کا تدارک ممکن ہے کیونکہ صحابہ اس طرح کی مجہول مدت میں مختلف ہیں اور اس لئے کہ جو اصل ہے وہ معدوم ہے کیا نہیں دیکھتے ہو کہ اصلی قرضہ کا مجمبول ہونا برداشت کر لیا جاتا ہے بایں طور کہ ( یہ کہا ) جو کچھ تیر افلاں شخص پر واجب ہو میں اس کا کفیل ہوں تو وصف کے اندر بدرجہ اولی (جہالت برداشت ہوگی ) بر خلاف بیچ کے کیونکہ اصل شمن میں جہالت برداشت نہیں ہوتی ہے پس اس طرح اس کے وصف میں بھی برداشت نہ ہوگی برخلاف اس کے کہ جب مطلقا فروخت کیا پھر بائع نے ان اوقات تک شمن کو مؤجل کیا تو جائز ہے کیونکہ یہ دین میں میعادی مہلت ہے اور ادائے قرض

سیرہ کہلائے گی ان اوقات کی جہالت کے پیرہ ہونے کی دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان اشیاء کی اصل اس سال میں معلوم الوقوع ہے یعنی یہ بات قطعی طور پر معلوم ہے کہ اس سال حاجیوں کی آمد ہوگی۔ کھیتیاں کئیں گی ، اناج گاہا جائے گا، انگور توڑے جائیں گے، جانوروں کے بال کاٹے جائیں گے، ہاں وصف تقدم اور تأخر مجہول ہے پس جب ان اشیاء کی اصل معلوم الوقوع ہے اور وصف مجہول ہے تو ان اوقات کی جہالت، جہالت بیرہ ہوگی اور کفالہ چونکہ جہالت بیرہ برداشت کر لیتا ہے اس لئے ان اوقات کو میعاد بنا کر کفالہ جائز ہوگا۔ رہی یہ بات کہ کفالہ جہالت بیرہ کیوں برداشت کر لیتا ہے۔ جواب تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ کفالہ ابتداء نذر کے مشابہ ہے کیونکہ جس طرح نذر کے اندر الزام محض یعنی اپنے اوپر غیر لازم چیز کو
Ruling on setting a term to the arrival of pilgrims, similarly to harvest, threshing, picking fruits, shearing wool. [Matn:] 'And the sale to the arrival of the pilgrim is not permissible, and likewise to the harvest, threshing, grape-picking, and shearing, because they are subject to advancement and delay. But if a guarantee (kafalah) is made to these times, it is permissible because slight uncertainty is tolerated in kafalah, and this uncertainty is slight and can be rectified due to the difference among the Companions concerning it, and because its origin is known. Do you not see that kafalah tolerates uncertainty in the original debt, such as when one guarantees 'whatever is owed by so-and-so'? So in the description it is more tolerable. Contrary to sale, which does not tolerate uncertainty in the original price, and likewise in its description. Contrary to when one sells absolutely and then defers the price to these times, which is permissible because this is a deferment of a debt, and this uncertainty is tolerated in the same way as in kafalah. But stipulating it in the original contract is not so, because the contract is invalidated by a void condition.' Translation: And selling (promising) upon the arrival of pilgrims is not permissible, and likewise to the time of harvest, threshing, grape-picking, and wool-shearing, because these things vary. And if one makes a guarantee to these times, it is permissible because kafalah tolerates slight ignorance, and this ignorance is slight and can be rectified because the Companions differed regarding it, and because its origin is known. Do you not see that kafalah tolerates ignorance in the original debt, such as saying 'I guarantee whatever is owed to you by so-and-so'? So in the description it is more tolerable. Contrary to sale, which does not tolerate ignorance in the original price, and thus not in its description. Contrary to when one sells absolutely and then defers the price to these times, which is permissible because this is a deferment of a debt and this ignorance is tolerated like in kafalah. But stipulating it in the original contract is not so because the contract is invalidated by a void condition.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the Hidayah's matn on the validity of a sale when the payment term is set to uncertain future events like the arrival of pilgrims (hajj) or harvest. The author first presents the ruling: such a sale is invalid because these times are not fixed; they vary with climate and are thus unknown. However, if one makes a kafalah (surety) with the same term, it is valid because kafalah tolerates slight uncertainty. The proof given is twofold: first, the Companions themselves differed on whether such uncertainty is acceptable in a sale—Aisha bint Abi Bakr permitted it (as in the case of 'bay' al-ata') while Ibn Abbas did not. This difference indicates that the uncertainty is slight and not fatal. Second, the original event (e.g., the arrival of pilgrims) is known to occur within the year, so the uncertainty is only in the exact timing, not in its occurrence. Kafalah is analogous to a vow (nazr) in that it creates an obligation voluntarily, so it can bear slight uncertainty. In contrast, a sale is a commutative contract where the price must be known precisely; stipulating an unknown term in the original contract makes the sale fasid. However, if the sale is made without such condition and later the parties agree to defer payment to an uncertain time, it is valid as a deferment of a debt (tajil al-dayn), which is similar to kafalah. The passage emphasizes the Hanafi position that the validity hinges on whether the uncertainty is in the original contract (not tolerated) or in a subsequent deferment (tolerated).

Key Terms
كفالة (kafalah): A contract of surety where a person guarantees payment of a debt or performance of an act.
جهالة يسيرة (jahala yasira): Slight or minor uncertainty that does not lead to dispute and is tolerable in certain contracts.
بيع إلى أجل (bay' ila ajal): A sale where payment is deferred to a future term.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person buys an item and stipulates in the contract that payment will be made upon the arrival of the pilgrims (hajj), what is the ruling?
A) The sale is valid because the event is known to occur.
B) The sale is valid because the uncertainty is slight.
C) The sale is invalid (fasid) because the term is uncertain.
D) The sale is valid only if both parties agree to it later.

Key Takeaway
Slight uncertainty invalidates a sale when stipulated in the original contract, but is tolerated in kafalah and subsequent deferment of debt.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
12 min
Sale with Uncertain Deferred Payment is Fasid; Suretyship Tolerates Light Ignorance
Ruling with rational proof and comparison to kafalah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sale conditioned on an uncertain future event and explain why the same condition is valid in a suretyship contract.

Core Idea
A sale requires a known term; an unknown term makes it fasid, but suretyship tolerates light ignorance because it blends vow and sale.

This lesson examines a key distinction in Hanafi contract law: while uncertainty about the payment term invalidates a sale, the same condition is permissible in a suretyship. The passage provides a rational proof and introduces the concept of light ignorance (jahalah yasirah) versus gross ignorance (jahalah fahishah). Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying Hanafi rulings in financial transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on a sale where payment is deferred to an uncertain future event (e.g., pilgrims' arrival, harvest). The ruling is that such a sale is fasid (irregular).
Fasid means the contract is defective but may become valid if the defect is removed before finalization.
2
Locate the proof
The proof is rational: the timing of these events varies with seasons, so the term is unknown. An unknown term creates gharar, which makes the sale fasid.
The Hanafi school uses rational reasoning (dalil aqli) when no explicit text exists.
3
Contrast with suretyship (kafalah)
The same condition (payment upon an uncertain event) is valid in a suretyship because kafalah tolerates light ignorance (jahalah yasirah). The passage explains that the uncertainty here is 'light' because the event is certain to occur within the year, only the exact time is unknown.
Light ignorance is distinguished from gross ignorance by the possibility of rectification and the type of contract.
4
Understand the reasoning behind kafalah's tolerance
Kafalah initially resembles a vow (nadhr), which tolerates all ignorance, and ultimately resembles a sale, which tolerates none. Therefore, kafalah strikes a balance: it tolerates light ignorance but not gross ignorance.
This dual resemblance is a unique Hanafi argument (talil) for the rule.
5
Evaluate the Companion disagreement
The passage notes that Aisha considered such uncertainty not a barrier to sale (as in bay' al-'ata'), while Ibn Abbas disagreed. This difference confirms that the ignorance is 'light' — it is not unanimously invalidating.
The ikhtilaf among the Companions is used as evidence for the lightness of the ignorance.

میعاد مجہول ہوئی اور میعاد مجہول ہونے کی صورت میں بیع فاسد ہوتی ہے اس لئے ان صورتوں میں بیع فاسد ہوگی اور اگر کوئی شخص ان اوقات کو میعاد بنا کر کسی کے قرضہ کا کفیل ہوا تو یہ کفالہ جائز ہے یعنی مثلاً یہ کہا کہ میں تیرے قرضہ کا کفیل ہوں اور حاجیوں کے آنے پر یا کھیتیاں کٹنے کے زمانہ میں ادا کردوں گا تو یہ جائز ہے کیونکہ کفالہ معمولی جہالت برداشت کر لیتا ہے اگر چہ جہالت فاحشہ برداشت نہیں کرتا اور ان کے لئے مانع ہیں یا مانع نہیں ہیں چنانچہ حضرت عائشہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ ان اوقات کی جہالتیں جواز بیع کے لئے مانع نہیں ہیں یہی وجہ ہے کہ صدیقہ عائشہ بیع الی العطاء کی جواز کی قائل ہیں عطاء اس عطیہ کو کہا گہا جائے گا، انگور توڑے جائیں گے، جانوروں کے بال کاٹے جائیں گے، ہاں وصف تقدم اور تأخر مجہول ہے پس جب ان اشیاء کی اصل معلوم الوقوع ہے اور وصف مجہول ہے تو ان اوقات کی جہالت، جہالت بیرہ ہوگی اور کفالہ چونکہ جہالت بیرہ برداشت کر لیتا ہے اس لئے ان اوقات کو میعاد بنا کر کفالہ جائز ہوگا۔ رہی یہ بات کہ کفالہ جہالت بیرہ کیوں برداشت کر لیتا ہے۔ جواب تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ کفالہ ابتداء نذر کے مشابہ ہے کیونکہ جس طرح نذر کے اندر الزام محض یعنی اپنے اوپر غیر لازم چیز کو لازم کرنا ہوتا ہے اسی طرح ابتدا کفیل بھی اپنے اوپر غیر لازم قرض کو لازم کرتا ہے اور کفالہ انتہاء بیع کے مشابہ ہے کیونکہ جس طرح بیع عقد معاوضہ ہے اسی طرح کفالہ بھی انتہاء عقد معاوضہ ہے کیونکہ کفیل قرض کی جو مقدار مکفول عنہ کی طرف سے مکفول لہ کو ادا کرتا ہے وہ اس کے عوض مکفول عنہ سے اس کے بقدر لیتا ہے پس انتہاء کے اعتبار سے کفالہ بھی عقد معاوضہ ہوگا اور یہ امر مسلم ہے کہ نذر جہالت بیرہ اور جہالت فاحشہ دونوں کو برداشت کر لیتی ہے اور بیع دونوں کو برداشت نہیں کرتی پس ہم نے کفالہ میں دونوں کی مشابہتوں کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ کفالہ جہالت بیرہ برداشت کرتا ہے جیسا کہ نذر جہالت برداشت کرتی ہے اور کفالہ جہالت فاحشہ برداشت نہیں کرتا جیسا کہ بیع جہالت برداشت نہیں کرتی ہے۔
حاصل یہ کہ جہالت بیرہ میں نذر کی مشابہت کا اعتبار کیا ہے اور جہالت فاحشہ میں بیع کی مشابہت کا اعتبار کیا ہے صاحب ہدایہ نے مزید ترقی کر کے کہا کہ کفالت میں اصلی قرضہ کا مجہول ہونا برداشت کر لیا جاتا ہے مثلاً کہا کہ تیرا جو کچھ فلاں پر واجب ہو میں اس کا کفیل ہوں باوجود یکہ یہاں اصلی قرضہ مجہول ہے لیکن کفالہ تب بھی جائز ہے پس وصف کا مجہول ہونا بدرجہ اولی برداشت ہوگا یعنی اگر قرضہ ادا کرنے کی مدت مجہول ہو اور قرضہ مجہول نہ ہو تو کفالہ بدرجہ اولی جائز ہے برخلاف بیع کے کہ اس میں اصل ثمن کا مجہول ہونا برداشت نہیں ہوتا ہے تو ثمن ادا کرنے کا وصف یعنی مدت مجہول ہونا بھی برداشت نہیں تو وصف ثمن یعنی ادائیگی کی میعاد مجہول ہونا بھی قابل برداشت نہ ہوگا۔
This ignorance is tolerated like suretyship, and in the original sale, stipulating it is not tolerated because the contract of sale becomes void by an invalid condition. Explanation of the issue: If someone says, 'I bought this item for ten rupees on condition that I will pay the price when the pilgrims arrive,' or says, 'I will pay the price when the harvest begins,' or says, 'I will pay at the time of threshing the grain,' or 'at the time of picking the grapes,' or 'at the time of shearing the animals' hair and wool,' in all these cases the sale is not permissible, i.e., setting these times as the term for payment is not permissible. Consequently, by making these times the term for payment, the sale becomes fasid. The proof is that the times of these things vary earlier and later due to differences in heat and cold, so there is no known and specified time for them. When these times are not known and specified, the term for payment becomes unknown, and when the term is unknown, the sale is fasid. Therefore, in these cases the sale will be fasid. And if a person becomes a guarantor for someone's loan using these times as the term, then this suretyship is valid. For example, he said, 'I am a guarantor for your loan and I will pay upon the arrival of the pilgrims or at the time of the harvest,' this is valid because suretyship tolerates minor ignorance, although it does not tolerate gross ignorance. The ignorance in setting these mentioned times as the term for suretyship is light ignorance; its rectification is possible. And the ignorance in these times is light because there is disagreement among the Companions regarding these ignorances: whether they are a barrier to the validity of sale or not. Indeed, Aisha said that these ignorances are not a barrier to the validity of sale. This is why Siddiqa Aisha believed in the validity of bay' al-'ata'. 'Ata' is the annual grant distributed from the treasury to Muslims. Receiving this grant once a year was certain, but its time varied earlier or later. Similarly, the arrival of pilgrims, harvest of crops, threshing of grain, picking of grapes, shearing of wool and hair definitely occur once a year, but their time varies. So if a buyer purchases an item on condition that he will pay the price upon receiving the grant, then according to Aisha this sale is valid; as if Aisha did not consider such ignorances as barriers to the validity of sale. And Ibn Abbas did not believe in the validity of bay' al-'ata' and similar ignorances. Thus, due to the disagreement among the Companions regarding these mentioned times being a barrier to the validity of sale or not, lightness (khiffah) occurs. And when lightness occurs in the ignorances of these times, their ignorance is called light ignorance. The second proof of these times being light ignorance is that the occurrence of these things is known in that year, i.e., it is definitively known that this year the pilgrims will come, crops will be harvested, grain will be threshed, grapes will be picked, animal hair will be sheared. However, the attribute of earliness or lateness is unknown. So when the occurrence of these things is known and the attribute is unknown, the ignorance of these times is light ignorance. And since suretyship tolerates light ignorance, therefore making these times the term for suretyship is valid. As for why suretyship tolerates light ignorance, the answer is that suretyship initially resembles a vow because just as in a vow there is pure obligation, i.e., making something non-obligatory obligatory upon oneself, similarly initially the guarantor makes a non-obligatory loan obligatory upon himself. And suretyship ultimately resembles a sale because just as a sale is a commutative contract, similarly in the end suretyship is also a commutative contract, because the amount of the loan that the guarantor pays from the principal debtor to the creditor, he takes its equivalent from the principal debtor. Thus, from the perspective of its end, suretyship is also a commutative contract. And it is agreed that a vow tolerates both light ignorance and gross ignorance, while a sale tolerates neither. So, considering both similarities in suretyship, we said that suretyship tolerates light ignorance, just as a vow tolerates ignorance, and suretyship does not tolerate gross ignorance, just as a sale does not tolerate ignorance. The conclusion is that in light ignorance, the similarity to a vow is considered, and in gross ignorance, the similarity to a sale is considered. The author of Hidayah further added that in suretyship, the ignorance of the principal debt is tolerated. For example, he said, 'Whatever is owed to you by so-and-so, I am its guarantor,' even though here the principal debt is unknown, but suretyship is still valid. So the ignorance of the attribute is a fortiori tolerated, i.e., if the term for paying the debt is unknown and the debt itself is known, then suretyship is a fortiori valid. Contrary to a sale, where ignorance of the principal price is not tolerated, so the ignorance of the attribute of payment, i.e., an unknown term, is also not tolerated; thus the attribute of the price, i.e., an unknown term of payment, is also not tolerable.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the effect of uncertain deferred payment in a sale and in suretyship. The author first states the ruling: if a sale is conditioned on payment at an uncertain time (like the arrival of pilgrims or harvest), the sale is fasid because the term is unknown, which introduces gharar. The proof is rational: these times vary with seasons, so they are not specific enough to constitute a valid term. However, the same condition in a suretyship is valid because suretyship tolerates light ignorance (jahalah yasirah). The author explains that the ignorance is considered 'light' because the occurrence of these events is certain within the year, only the exact timing is unknown. This is supported by the disagreement among Companions: Aisha considered such ignorance not a barrier to sale (as in bay' al-'ata'), while Ibn Abbas disagreed. This difference shows that the ignorance is not gross. The author then provides a deeper rationale: suretyship initially resembles a vow (nadhr), which tolerates all ignorance, and ultimately resembles a sale, which tolerates none. Therefore, suretyship strikes a balance: it tolerates light ignorance but not gross ignorance. The Hidayah further notes that even ignorance of the principal debt is tolerated in suretyship, so ignorance of the term is a fortiori tolerated. In contrast, a sale does not tolerate ignorance of the price, so neither does it tolerate ignorance of the term. This distinction is crucial for understanding the Hanafi position on contracts.

Key Terms
بیع فاسد (bay' fasid): A sale that is irregular due to a defect (e.g., unknown term) but may become valid if the defect is removed before it is finalized.
جہالت بیرہ (jahalah yasirah): Minor ignorance that is tolerable in certain contracts like kafalah; the occurrence is known but the exact detail is uncertain.
کفالہ (kafalah): A contract of suretyship where one person guarantees the debt of another, undertaking to pay if the debtor defaults.
نذر (nadhr): A vow by which a person makes an act obligatory upon themselves voluntarily; tolerates all types of jahalah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone buys an item on the condition that payment will be made when the pilgrims arrive, the sale is:
A) Valid
B) Fasid
C) Batil
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
In a sale, an uncertain deferred term makes the contract fasid, but the same condition in a suretyship is valid due to kafalah's tolerance of light ignorance based on its dual resemblance to vow and sale.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
Ruling on Giving Respite After a Sale with Uncertain Times
Clarifies that if a sale is unconditional, subsequent respite until uncertain time is valid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a condition inserted in the original sale contract and a subsequent agreement to defer payment, and state the validity of each case.

Core Idea
A subsequent respite to an uncertain time is valid; the same condition in the original contract would invalidate the sale.

This passage clarifies a subtle but important distinction in Hanafi contract law: the timing of a condition matters. If a sale is made without any payment term, the seller may later grant a deferment until an uncertain event (e.g., harvest). This is valid because the original contract was unconditional and the respite is a separate agreement to defer an existing debt. Conversely, if the sale was conditioned on such uncertain payment from the start, the sale is invalid due to gharar. Understanding this difference is crucial for drafting valid contracts and avoiding nullification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
First, note the passage describes two distinct situations: (1) a sale conditioned on payment at an uncertain time, and (2) an unconditional sale followed by a separate respite to an uncertain time.
2
Analyse the conditional sale
If the sale is made with a condition that payment be made at an uncertain time (e.g., 'when the harvest comes'), the sale is fasid (voidable) because the condition introduces gharar into the original contract.
The Hanafi school considers any uncertain term in the original contract as invalidating because it affects the core exchange.
3
Analyse the subsequent respite
If the sale was absolute (no payment term), the seller may later grant a muhlat (respite) until an uncertain time. This is valid because the original contract is sound, and the respite is a separate agreement to defer an existing debt.
The uncertainty in the debt payment is tolerated, similar to suretyship (kafalah), where light ignorance is overlooked.
4
Understand the rationale
The key principle is that forbidding conditions in the original contract is strict to preserve the essence of sale, but subsequent modifications to debt terms are more lenient because the debt is already established.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہاں اگر بیع کو مطلق رکھا یعنی ثمن ادا کرنے کی کوئی میعاد مقرر نہیں کی پھر بائع نے مذکورہ بالا وقتوں میں سے کسی وقت تک ثمن ادا کرنے کی مہلت دیدی تو یہ جائز ہے کیونکہ اب یہ ثمن کا قرضہ ادا کرنے میں میعاد ہوئی۔ اصل عقد میں شرط لگانا نہ ہوا اور قرضہ ادا کرنے میں ایسی خفیف جہالت بمنزلہ کفالہ کے برداشت ہوتی ہے اگر چہ یہ شرط اصل عقد میں برداشت نہیں ہوتی کیونکہ عقد بیع فاسد شرطوں سے باطل ہو جاتا ہے حاصل یہ کہ اگر خریداری اس شرط پر ہو کہ ادائے ثمن کی میعاد کے یہ اوقات ہیں تو بیع فاسد ہے اور اگر عقد بیع کے بعد بائع نے مشتری کو ادائے ثمن کے واسطے ان اوقات تک مہلت دیدی تو بیع بھی جائز ہے اور یہ مہلت بھی جائز ہے۔
Yes, if the sale was left absolute, i.e., no term for payment was fixed, and then the seller gave a respite until one of the mentioned times for payment, then this is valid because now it has become a term for paying the debt of the price. The condition was not placed in the original contract, and in debt payment, such light ignorance is tolerated like in suretyship, even though this condition is not tolerated in the original contract because the contract of sale becomes void by invalid conditions. The conclusion is that if the purchase is on the condition that these times are the term for payment, then the sale is fasid; and if after the sale contract the seller gives the buyer a respite until these times for payment, then both the sale and this respite are valid.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is a ruling that distinguishes between a condition inserted in the original contract and a subsequent agreement. If a sale is made without any condition about payment time (absolute sale), the seller may later give the buyer time to pay until an uncertain event (like harvest or pilgrim arrival). This is valid because the original sale was sound, and the subsequent agreement to defer payment is like a new contract of debt with a term. The Hanafi school tolerates light ignorance in debt payment terms, similar to suretyship. The key point is that the condition was not part of the original contract; if it were, it would invalidate the sale. Therefore, this scenario avoids the problem of fasād.

Key Terms
بیع مطلق (bay' mutlaq): An absolute sale with no conditions or restrictions regarding payment time.
مہلت (muhlat): A respite or deferment given by the creditor to the debtor for payment, which may be set to an uncertain time if the debt is already established.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a sale is concluded without any condition about payment time, and later the seller gives the buyer until the harvest time to pay, the sale and the respite are:
A) Both fasid
B) Sale valid, respite fasid
C) Both valid
D) Sale batil, respite valid

Key Takeaway
A condition in the original contract invalidates the sale; a subsequent agreement to defer payment to an uncertain time is valid.

Dropping the Uncertain Term: Majority vs Zufar
Intra-Hanafi dispute on curing a fasid sale by dropping the condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi majority ruling on dropping an uncertain term in a sale and distinguish between fasād in an excessive condition vs fasād in the essence of the contract.

Core Idea
A fasid sale from an uncertain term can be cured by dropping that term before dispute arises, if the fasād is in a condition, not the essence.

This passage addresses a key intra-Hanafi dispute: can a sale that is fasid due to an uncertain payment term be made valid if the parties later agree to drop that term before the time arrives? The majority holds it can; Imam Zufar disagrees. Understanding the distinction between fasād in a condition (shart za'id) and fasād in the essence (sulb al-'aqd) is crucial for applying this ruling correctly.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi majority position and its proof
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad: the sale becomes valid upon dropping the uncertain term before the specified time. The proof is that the fasād was due to potential dispute (munaza'ah), which is removed before it crystallizes.
2
Present Imam Zufar's objection and his proof
Zufar argues the sale occurred as fasid and cannot become valid later, analogizing to temporary marriage where dropping the term does not validate it.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response distinguishing types of fasād
The key distinction: fasād can be in an excessive condition (shart za'id) or in the essence (sulb al-'aqd). If in a condition, it can be dropped; if in the essence (like riba or temporary marriage), it cannot.
Temporary marriage is invalid because its essence is impermissible (mut'ah), not just a condition.
4
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) and the mufta bihi
Majority: sale becomes valid, no need for a new contract. Zufar: remain fasid, must recontract. The relied-upon position is the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مذکورہ اشیاء کو آجال ٹھہرایا پھر اجل ساقط کر دیا، حکم
ولو باع الى هذه الاجال ثم تراضيا باسقاط الاجل قبل ان ياخذ الناس فى الحصاد و الدياس وقبل قدوم الحاج جاز البيع ايضا وقال زفر لا يجوز لانه وقع فاسدا فلا ينقلب جائزا او صار كاسقاط الاجل في النكاح الى اجل ولنا ان الفساد للمنازعة وقد ارتفع قبل تقرره وهذه الجهالة فى شرط زائد لا في صلب العقد فيمكن اسقاطه بخلاف ما اذا باع الدرهم بالدرهمين ثم اسقط الدرهم الزائد لان الفساد في صلب العقد و بخلاف النكاح الى اجل لانه متعة وهو عقد غير عقد النكاح وقوله فى الكتاب ثم تراضيا خرج وفاقا لان من له الاجل يستبد باسقاطه لانه خالص حقه
ترجمہ اور اگر ان اوقات تک بیع کی پھر بائع اور مشتری لوگوں کے کھیتیاں کاٹنے اور گانے اور حاجیوں کے آنے سے پہلے میعاد ساقط کرنے پر راضی ہو گئے تو بیع جائز ہے اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ بیع فاسد ہو کر واقع ہوتی تھی لہذا بدل کر جائز نہ ہوگی اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے میعادی نکاح میں میعاد کو ساقط کرنا اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ بیع فاسد ہونا جھگڑے کی وجہ سے تھا حالانکہ وہ تقریر سے پہلے
Setting the mentioned things as terms, then dropping the term, the ruling: And if one sold until these terms, then they mutually agree to drop the term before people begin harvesting and threshing and before the arrival of the pilgrims, the sale is valid as well. Zufar said: It is not valid because it occurred as fasid, so it does not turn into valid; or it becomes like dropping the term in temporary marriage. Our proof is that the fasād is due to potential dispute, and it has been removed before it becomes established. And this ignorance is in an excessive condition, not in the essence of the contract, so it can be dropped. Unlike if one sold one dirham for two dirhams and then dropped the extra dirham, because the fasād is in the essence of the contract. And unlike marriage for a term because it is temporary marriage, which is not the contract of marriage. And his statement in the book 'then they mutually agree' is an exception to consensus because the one to whom the term is due can unilaterally drop it, as it is his exclusive right. Translation: And if they sold until these times, then the seller and buyer agree to drop the term before people harvest and thresh and before the arrival of the pilgrims, the sale is valid. Imam Zufar said it is not valid because this sale occurred as fasid, so it cannot become valid by change; it becomes like dropping the term in temporary marriage. And our proof is that the fasād was due to potential dispute, and it has been removed before it became established.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a sale after the uncertain term is dropped. The Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) holds that if the parties agree to drop the uncertain term before the specified time (e.g., before harvest or pilgrim arrival), the sale becomes valid. The reason is that the fasād was due to the potential for future dispute (munaza'ah) arising from the unknown term. Once the term is dropped before any dispute crystallizes, the cause of fasād is removed. This is different from cases where the fasād is in the essence of the contract (like selling one dirham for two) or where the contract itself is impermissible (like temporary marriage). Imam Zufar argues that the sale was initially fasid and cannot be rectified by later dropping the condition. The Hanafi response distinguishes between fasād in the essence and fasād in an excessive condition. Here, the condition is not integral; it can be dropped. The text also notes that if the term is only for the benefit of one party (e.g., the buyer has the right to defer), that party can unilaterally drop it.

Key Terms
فساد للمنازعة (fasād li al-munaza'ah): Invalidity due to potential future dispute; the reason why a condition of uncertain term makes a sale fasid is that it could lead to disagreement between parties.
شرط زائد (shart za'id): An excessive condition that is not part of the essence of the contract; in this case, the condition of deferred payment to an uncertain time.
صلب العقد (sulb al-'aqd): The essence or core of the contract; if the fasād is in the essence, the contract is incurably void.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view, if a sale is made with an uncertain payment term and the parties drop that term before the time, the sale becomes:
A) Fasid
B) Batil
C) Valid
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
A fasid sale caused by an uncertain condition can be rectified by dropping that condition before the dispute arises, provided the fasād is not in the essence of the contract.

Kafalah's Tolerance of Ignorance Compared to Nadhr and Bay'
Analogy of kafalah with nadhr and bay' regarding jahalah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school tolerates minor ignorance (jahalah yasirah) in kafalah but not major ignorance, using the analogies with nadhr and bay'.

Core Idea
Kafalah tolerates minor ignorance like nadhr, but not major ignorance like bay' — its dual nature determines the threshold.

This passage explores the Hanafi ruling on kafalah (suretyship) and its treatment of uncertainty (jahalah). The author compares kafalah to nadhr (vow) and bay' (sale) to derive the rule that minor ignorance is tolerated while major ignorance is not. Understanding this analogy is key to grasping the Hanafi approach to contractual flexibility in gratuitous vs. commutative contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dual nature of kafalah
Kafalah has two aspects: initiation (making a non-binding debt binding) resembles nadhr (tabarru'), and conclusion (the surety recovers from the debtor) resembles bay' (mu'awadah).
2
Recognize established rulings for nadhr and bay'
Nadhr tolerates both minor and major jahalah; bay' tolerates neither. These are established matters (amr musallam).
3
Apply the similarity to kafalah
Since kafalah shares initiation with nadhr, it tolerates minor ignorance like nadhr. Since it shares conclusion with bay', it does not tolerate major ignorance, like bay'.
This is a qiyas of prior analogy (qiyas jaliy).
4
Examine the refinement from al-Hidayah
Even ignorance of the principal debt is tolerated in kafalah; a fortiori, ignorance of a descriptor (e.g., term) is tolerated. Unlike bay', where ignorance of the principal price is not tolerated, so ignorance of the term is also not tolerated.
5
Contrast with bay' when term is added after contract
If a sale is absolute and the seller later grants a term, it is valid because no condition was in the original contract. This shows that minor uncertainty in repayment (like in kafalah) is tolerated if not stipulated in the original contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا زم کرنا ہوتا ہے اسی طرح ابتدا کفیل بھی اپنے اوپر غیر لازم قرض کو لازم کرتا ہے اور کفالہ انتہاء ربیع کے مشابہ ہے کیونکہ جس طرح بیع عقد معاوضہ ہے اسی طرح کفالہ بھی انتہاء عقد معاوضہ ہے کیونکہ کفیل قرض کی جو مقدار مکفول عنہ کی طرف سے مکفول لہ کو ادا کرتا ہے وہ اس کے عوض مکفول عنہ سے اس کے بقدر لیتا ہے پس انتہاء کے اعتبار سے کفالہ بھی عقد معاوضہ ہوگا اور یہ امر مسلم ہے کہ نذر جہالت سیرہ اور جہالت فاحشہ دونوں کو برداشت کر لیتی ہے اور بیچ دونوں کو برداشت نہیں کرتی پس ہم نے کفالہ میں دونوں کی مشابہتوں کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے کہا کہ کفالہ جہالت پیمرہ برداشت کرتا ہے جیسا کہ نذر جہالت برداشت کرتی ہے اور کفالہ جہالت فاحشہ برداشت نہیں کرتا جیسا کہ بیچ جہالت برداشت نہیں کرتی ہے۔

حاصل یہ کہ جہالت بیرہ میں نذر کی مشابہت کا اعتبار کیا ہے اور جہالت فاحشہ میں بیع کی مشابہت کا اعتبار کیا ہے صاحب ہدایہ نے مزید ترقی کر کے کہا کہ کفالت میں اصلی قرضہ کا مجہول ہونا برداشت کر لیا جاتا ہے مثلاً کہا کہ تیرا جو کچھ فلاں پر واجب ہو میں اس کا کفیل ہوں باوجود یکہ یہاں اصلی قرضہ مجہول ہے لیکن کفالہ تب بھی جائز ہے پس وصف کا مجہول ہونا بدرجہ اولی برداشت ہوگا یعنی اگر قرضہ ادا کرنے کی مدت مجہول ہو اور قرضہ مجہول نہ ہو تو کفالہ بدرجہ اولی جائز ہے برخلاف بیع کے کہ اس میں اصل ثمن کا مجہول ہونا برداشت نہیں ہوتا ہے تو شمن ادا کرنے کا وصف یعنی مدت مجہول ہونا بھی برداشت نہیں تو وصف ثمن یعنی ادائیگی کی میعاد مجہول ہونا بھی قابل برداشت نہ ہوگا۔ ہاں اگر بیع کو مطلق رکھا یعنی شن ادا کرنے کی کوئی میعاد مقرر نہیں کی پھر بائع نے مذکورہ بالا وقتوں میں سے کسی وقت تک شمن ادا کرنے کی مہلت دیدی تو یہ جائز ہے کیونکہ اب یہ ثمن کا قرضہ ادا کرنے میں میعاد ہوئی۔ اصل عقد میں شرط لگانا نہ ہوا اور قرضہ ادا کرنے میں ایسی خفیف جہالت بمنزلہ کفالہ کے برداشت ہوتی ہے اگر چہ یہ شرط اصل عقد میں برداشت نہیں ہوتی کیونکہ عقد بیع فاسد شرطوں سے باطل ہو جاتا ہے حاصل یہ کہ اگر خریداری اس شرط پر ہو کہ ادائے ثمن کی میعاد کے یہ اوقات ہیں تو بیع فاسد ہے اور اگر عقد بیع کے بعد بائع نے مشتری کو ادائے شمن کے واسطے ان اوقات تک مہلت دیدی تو بیع بھی جائز ہے اور یہ مہلت بھی جائز ہے۔
It is necessary to make binding; similarly, the initiator of the surety also makes a non-binding debt binding upon himself. And kafalah (suretyship) resembles bay' (sale) in its conclusion, because just as sale is a commutative contract, so too kafalah is a commutative contract in its conclusion, because the surety pays the amount of debt to the creditor from the principal debtor, and then he takes an equivalent from the principal debtor. Thus, from the perspective of conclusion, kafalah is also a commutative contract. And it is an established matter that nadhr (vow) tolerates both minor ignorance and major ignorance, while bay' tolerates neither. So we, considering the resemblance of kafalah to both, said that kafalah tolerates minor ignorance just as nadhr tolerates it, and kafalah does not tolerate major ignorance just as bay' does not tolerate it.

In summary, in minor ignorance, resemblance to nadhr is considered, and in major ignorance, resemblance to bay' is considered. The author of al-Hidayah further advanced and said that in kafalah, ignorance of the principal debt is tolerated; for example, if one says, 'Whatever is owed to you by so-and-so, I am the surety for it,' despite the principal debt being unknown, the suretyship is still valid. So ignorance of the descriptor is a fortiori tolerated, meaning if the term of payment is unknown but the debt is known, the suretyship is a fortiori valid. Unlike bay', where ignorance of the principal price is not tolerated, so ignorance of the descriptor of the price, i.e., the term of payment, is also not tolerated. Rather, the ignorance of the descriptor of the price, i.e., the term of payment, would not be tolerated. However, if the sale is left absolute, i.e., no term for payment is specified, then the seller grants the buyer a respite until one of the mentioned times, this is permissible, because this becomes a term in the repayment of the debt of the price. No stipulation was made in the original contract, and such minor ignorance in repayment is tolerated like in kafalah, even though such a stipulation would not be tolerated in the original contract, because a sale contract is invalidated by invalid conditions. In summary, if the purchase is conditioned that the term for payment is these times, the sale is invalid; but if after the contract, the seller grants the buyer a respite until these times for payment, then both the sale and this respite are valid.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage explains the Hanafi ruling on kafalah (suretyship) and its resemblance to nadhr (vow) and bay' (sale) regarding the tolerance of ignorance (jahalah). The author begins by stating that kafalah is similar to bay' in its conclusion because both are commutative contracts—the surety pays the debt and then recovers from the principal debtor. However, in its initiation, it resembles nadhr because the surety makes a non-binding debt binding upon himself. Then it mentions that nadhr tolerates both minor and major ignorance, while bay' tolerates neither. Combining these, the Hanafi ruling is that kafalah tolerates minor ignorance (like nadhr) but not major ignorance (like bay'). The author then quotes from al-Hidayah that even ignorance of the principal debt is tolerated in kafalah, a fortiori ignorance of a descriptor like the term. Unlike bay', where ignorance of the principal price is not tolerated, so ignorance of the term is also not tolerated. However, if the sale is absolute (no term stipulated), and the seller later grants a term, that is valid because it is a new concession and not a condition in the original contract. This shows the Hanafi position that kafalah is more flexible than sale in tolerating certain types of uncertainty.

Key Terms
جہالت (jahalah): Ignorance or uncertainty in a contractual matter, classified into minor (yasirah) and major (fahishah).
کفالہ (kafalah): Suretyship: a contract where a person guarantees a debt owed by another.
نذر (nadhr): Vow: a binding promise to perform an act of worship or charity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It tolerates both.
B) It tolerates neither.
C) It tolerates minor ignorance like nadhr but not major ignorance like bay'.
D) It tolerates major ignorance but not minor.

Key Takeaway
Kafalah tolerates minor ignorance (jahalah yasirah) because it resembles nadhr at initiation, but does not tolerate major ignorance because it resembles bay' at conclusion.

Cancellation of an Uncertain Deferred Payment Term in a Sale
Ruling on sale with future term and dispute between Abu Hanifa and Zufar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on when a fasid sale can become valid by removing a defective condition and evaluate Zufar's counterargument using core vs. peripheral defect distinction.

Core Idea
A defective condition in the periphery can be removed to validate a sale; a defect in the core cannot.

This lesson examines a disputed case in Hanafi fiqh: a sale made with an uncertain deferred payment term (e.g., 'when the pilgrims arrive') is initially fasid due to potential dispute. What happens if both parties cancel the term before it matures? Abu Hanifa and his student Zufar differ on whether the sale becomes valid. Understanding their arguments illuminates the Hanafi approach to curing contractual defects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract defect
The sale has an uncertain deferred payment term (ajal majhul) such as 'when the harvest comes'. This creates jahalah (ignorance) that could lead to dispute, making the sale fasid initially.
The defect is in an additional condition (the term), not in the core of the contract (price and commodity).
2
Understand Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Abu Hanifa argues that the invalidity is due to the potential for dispute, which is removed by cancelling the term before it materializes. Since the defect is in a peripheral condition, it can be dropped, and the sale becomes valid.
His argument is based on the removal of the cause of invalidity before it takes effect.
3
Understand Zufar's objection
Zufar argues that once a contract is concluded as fasid, it cannot become valid by removing the defect. He analogizes to mut'ah marriage (temporary marriage) where cancelling the term does not make it a valid nikah, and to selling one dirham for two where cancelling the extra dirham does not validate the riba contract.
Zufar uses qiyas (analogical reasoning) to support his position.
4
Trace the Hanafi response to Zufar
The Hanafi response distinguishes: in mut'ah, the contract itself is a different type (temporary marriage), not a valid marriage with a defect; in the riba case, the defect is in the core (one of the two prices), so removal does not change the initial invalid formation. In our case, the defect is peripheral and the contract remains a sale, so removal can cure it.
This distinction between core (asl) and peripheral (zā'id) defects is key.
5
Apply the ruling
The mufta bihi (relied upon) position is Abu Hanifa's: if both parties agree to cancel the uncertain term before it arrives, the sale becomes valid. The term is the right of the one who benefits from it, so he can waive it alone.
The ruling is limited to defects in additional conditions, not defects in the essence of the contract.

مذکورہ اشیاء کو آجال ٹھہرایا پھر اجل ساقط کر دیا، حکم
ولو باع الى هذه الاجال ثم تراضيا باسقاط الاجل قبل ان ياخذ الناس فى الحصادو الدياس وقبل قدوم الحاج جاز البيع ايضا وقال زفر لا يجوز لا نه وقع فاسد ا فلا ينقلب جائز او صار كاسقاط الاجل في النكاح الى اجل ولنا ان الفساد للمنازعة وقد ارتفع قبل تقرره وهذه الجهالة فى شرط زائد لا في صلب العقد فيمكن اسقاطه بخلاف ما اذا باع الدرهم بالدر همين ثم اسقط الدرهم الزائد لان الفساد في صلب العقدو بخلاف النكاح الى اجل لانه متعة وهو عقد غير عقد النكاح وقوله فى الكتاب ثم تراضيا خرج وفاقالان من له الاجل يستبد باسقاطه لانه خالص حقه

ترجمہ اور اگر ان اوقات تک بیع کی پھر بائع اور مشتری لوگوں کے کھیتیاں کاٹنے اور گانے اور حاجیوں کے آنے سے پہلے میعاد ساقط کرنے پر راضی ہو گئے تو بیع جائز ہے اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ بیچ فاسد ہو کر واقع ہوتی تھی لہذا بدل کر جائز نہ ہوگی اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے میعادی نکاح میں میعاد کو ساقط کرنا اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ بیع فاسد ہونا جھگڑے کی وجہ سے تھا حالانکہ وہ تقریر سے پہلے رآ گیا اور یہ جہالت ایک زائد شرط میں تھی نہ کہ نفس عقد میں اس لئے اس کا ساقط کرناممکن ہے اس کے برخلاف اگر ایک درہم دو درہم کے عوض بیچا پھر دونوں نے زائد درہم کو ساقط کر دیا کیونکہ نفس عقد میں فساد ہے اور برخلاف میعادی نکاح کے کیونکہ یہ متعہ ہے اور متعہ عقد نکاح کے علاوہ دوسرا اعقد ہوتا ہے اور مصنف کا قول ثم تراضیا یہ کلام اتفاقی ہے۔ کیونکہ تنہاوہ شخص جسکے واسطے میعاد ہے اس کو ساقط کر سکتا ہے کیونکہ میعاد خالص اس کا حق ہے۔

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے مذکورہ اوقات میں سے کسی ایک وقت کو میعاد بنا کر کوئی سامان فروخت کیا مثلاً اس شرط کے ساتھ فروخت کیا کہ ثمن نوروز کے دن یا حاجیوں کے آنے کے وقت ادا کر دینا مشتری نے اس کو منظور کر لیا پھر اس مشروط وقت کے آنے سے پہلے بائع اور مشتری دونوں اس مشروط میعاد کو ساقط کرنے پر راضی ہو گئے تو یہ بیع جائز ہوگئی ۔ لیکن حضرت امام زفر کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہوئی۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جو عقد ایک مرتبہ فاسد ہو کر منعقد ہوتا ہے وہ بدل کر جائز نہیں ہوتا پس جب شرط فاسد کی وجہ سے بیع فاسد ہوگئی تو اب عقد بدل کر جائز نہ ہوگا اگر چہ اس شرط فاسد کو ساقط کر دیا گیا جیسا کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک اگر ایک مدت کے لئے نکاح کیا گیا پھر اس مدت کو ساقط کر دیا تو یہ نکاح بدل کر جائز نہیں ہوتا اور جیسے اگر بغیر گواہوں کے نکاح کیا اور پھر گواہ مقرر کر لئے تو یہ نکاح بھی چونکہ فاسد ہوکر منعقد ہوا تھا اسلئے بدل کر جائز نہیں ہوسکتا اور جیسے اگر ایک درہم کو دو درہم کے عوض فروخت کیا پھر ایک درہم کو ساقط کر دیا تو یہ عقد بھی بدل کر جائز نہیں ہوتا اسی طرح میعاد مجہول کی وجہ سے جب عقد بیع فاسد ہو کر منعقد ہوا تو میعاد مجہول ساقط کرنے سے بدل کر یہ عقد جائز نہ ہوگا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ میعاد مجہول ہونے کی صورت میں بیچ اس لئے فاسد ہوتی ہے کہ اس کی وجہ سے بائع اور مشتری کے درمیان جھگڑا پیدا ہونے کا امکان ہے اور جھگڑا اس وقت پیدا ہو گا جبکہ میعاد پوری ہونے کا وقت آئے گا مگر جب دونوں نے میعاد مجہول کو ساقط کر دیا تو مفسد بیج ثابت ہونے سے پہلے ہی دور ہو گیا اور جب مفسد دور ہو گیا تو بیع جائز ہو جائے گی۔ سوال رہا یہ سوال کہ جہالت اور فساد جب ابتدائے عقد میں ثابت ہو گیا تو اس کو ساقط کرنا مفید نہ ہونا چاہئے جیسا کہ جب ایک درہم کو دو درہم کے عوض بیچا پھر دونوں نے ایک درہم کو ساقط کر دیا تو یہ درہم زائد کو ساقط کرنا مفید نہیں ہے چنانچہ اس صورت میں بیع بدل کر جائز نہیں ہوتی۔ جواب ... اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ میعاد مجہول ہونے کی صورت میں جہالت شرط زائد میں ہے اس لئے اس کو ساقط کرناممکن اور مفید ہے اور بیع الدرہم بالدر ہمین کی صورت میں فساد صلب عقد یعنی احد البد لین میں ہے اس لئے اس کو ساقط کرنا ناممکن ہے۔ امام زفر کے قیاس کا جواب ... وبخلاف النكاح الى اجل .. الخ سے امام زفر کے قیاس کا جواب ہے جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ مفسد کے ثابت ہونے سے پہلے عقد فاسد بدل کر جائز ہو سکتا ہے لیکن ایک عقد بدل کر دوسرا عقد نہیں ہو سکتا اور مدت معینہ تک نکاح کرنا متعہ ہے اور متعہ ، نکاح کے علاوہ ایک عقد ہے پس متعہ بدل کر نکاح نہیں ہو سکتا اور میعاد مجہول کی صورت میں مفسد کو ساقط کرنے سے پہلے بھی وہ عقد بیع تھا اور مفسد کو ساقط کرنے کے بعد بھی عقد بیج ہے صرف اتنا فرق ہے کہ پہلے عقد فاسد تھا اور مفسد ساقط کر کے جائز ہو گیا
He made these items as terms, then cancelled the term. Ruling: 'If he sells with these terms, then they both agree to cancel the term before people start harvesting and threshing and before the arrival of the pilgrims, the sale is also valid. Zufar said: It is not valid because it occurred as invalid, so it does not become valid, or it is like cancelling the term in a marriage with a term. Our evidence is that the invalidity is due to potential dispute, and it was removed before it was established, and this ignorance is in an additional condition, not in the core of the contract, so its cancellation is possible. Unlike the case where he sells a dirham for two dirhams then cancels the extra dirham, because the invalidity is in the core of the contract. And unlike a marriage with a term, because it is mut'ah, which is a different contract from marriage. And his statement in the book 'then they both agree' is a matter of agreement, because the one who has the term may cancel it alone because it is exclusively his right.' Translation: And if he sells with these terms, then the seller and buyer agree to cancel the term before people harvest and thresh and before the pilgrims arrive, the sale is valid. Imam Zufar said: It is not valid because this sale occurred as invalid, so it does not become valid, and it becomes like cancelling the term in a time-limited marriage. And our evidence is that the sale was invalid due to the possibility of dispute, and that was removed before it was established, and this ignorance is in an additional condition, not in the essence of the contract, so its cancellation is possible. Contrary to if he sold a dirham for two dirhams then they cancelled the extra dirham, because the invalidity is in the essence of the contract. And contrary to a time-limited marriage, because it is mut'ah, and mut'ah is a different contract from marriage. And the author's statement 'then they both agree' is a matter of agreement, because the one who has the term may cancel it alone, because it is exclusively his right. Explanation: The scenario is that a person sold an item with one of these times as a term, e.g., with the condition that the price be paid on Nowruz or when the pilgrims arrive. The buyer accepted. Then before that time arrives, both seller and buyer agree to cancel the term, so the sale becomes valid. But according to Imam Zufar, it does not become valid. Zufar's evidence is that a contract that once occurs as invalid does not become valid by change. So when the sale became invalid due to an invalid condition, it does not become valid even if the condition is cancelled. Like if a marriage is made for a fixed term then the term is cancelled, it does not become a valid marriage. And like a marriage without witnesses then witnesses are produced, it remains invalid. And like selling one dirham for two then cancelling the extra dirham, it does not become valid. So similarly, when the sale became invalid due to unknown term, cancelling the term does not make it valid. Our evidence is that the sale is invalid due to the potential for dispute, which would only occur when the term arrives. When both cancelled the term before that, the defect was removed before it was established, so the sale becomes valid. A question arises: If ignorance and invalidity are established at the beginning of the contract, cancelling them should not help, like in the case of selling one dirham for two. Answer: In the case of unknown term, the ignorance is in an additional condition, so its cancellation is possible and beneficial. In the case of selling dirham for two, the invalidity is in the core of the contract (one of the two prices), so cancelling is impossible. Response to Zufar's analogy: 'And contrary to marriage with a term' is the response. The gist is that before the defect is established, an invalid contract can become valid, but one contract cannot change into another. So marriage with a term is mut'ah, which is a different contract from marriage, so mut'ah cannot become marriage. In the case of unknown term, before cancelling the defect, it was still a sale, and after cancelling, it is still a sale, only the defect is removed and it becomes valid.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage discusses a specific case: a sale made with a deferred payment term that is uncertain (e.g., 'when the pilgrims arrive'). The sale is initially invalid due to this uncertainty (jahalah) because it could lead to dispute. However, if before the term arrives, both the buyer and seller agree to cancel the term, the sale becomes valid according to Imam Abu Hanifa and the majority. Imam Zufar disagrees, arguing that once a contract is invalid, it cannot become valid by removing the defect; he draws an analogy to a marriage with a fixed term (mut'ah) which cannot be converted into a valid marriage by removing the term. The Hanafi response is that the invalidity here is due to an external reason (potential dispute) that is removed before it materializes, and the ignorance is in an additional condition (the term) not in the essence of the contract (the price and commodity). This distinguishes it from cases like selling one dirham for two (riba) where the defect is in the core, or mut'ah marriage which is a different type of contract altogether. The text concludes that cancelling the term is allowed because it is the right of the one whose term it is.

Key Terms
اجل (ajal): A fixed term or deadline for payment in a sale contract.
فساد (fasad): Invalidity that is curable; a contract that is essentially valid but has a defect that can be corrected.
متعہ (mut'ah): Temporary marriage for a fixed period, considered a separate contract from permanent marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what happens to a sale made with an uncertain deferred term if both parties cancel the term before it arrives?
A) The sale remains invalid.
B) The sale becomes valid.
C) The sale becomes a valid gift.
D) The sale is void from the beginning.

Key Takeaway
A fasid sale can become valid if the defect is in an additional condition and is removed before it causes dispute; defects in the core cannot be cured.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
12 min
Cancelling Unknown Future Time in Sale: Abu Hanifa vs Zufar
Explains ruling on cancelling unknown future time condition in sale and dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on cancelling an unknown future time condition in a sale and explain the distinction between defects in extra conditions and defects in the contract core.

Core Idea
An extra condition in a sale can be cancelled; a core defect cannot.

In a sale contract, specifying an unknown future time for payment or delivery renders the sale invalid due to potential dispute. However, the Hanafi school led by Imam Abu Hanifa holds that this defect can be rectified if the condition is cancelled before the time arrives. This lesson examines the reasoning behind this view and the counter-argument of Imam Zufar, focusing on the distinction between defects in accessory conditions and defects in the contract core.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on cancelling the condition
According to Imam Abu Hanifa and the majority, if both parties cancel the unknown time condition before it arrives, the sale becomes valid. The defect is in an extra condition (shart za'id), not in the contract itself.
The cancellation must occur before the time, not after.
2
Identify Imam Zufar's opposing view and his analogical evidence
Imam Zufar argues that a contract once concluded invalidly cannot become valid by later change. He analogizes to: (1) marriage for a term (mut'ah), (2) marriage without witnesses, and (3) selling one dirham for two dirhams. In all these, cancellation does not cure the invalidity.
Zufar's analogies are based on the principle that initial invalidity is permanent.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response to each analogy
The Hanafi response distinguishes: in mut'ah, the contract is a different type (temporary marriage), not a regular marriage; in dirham sale, the defect is in the core (one of the countervalues); in witnessless marriage, the condition of witnesses is strong, like a core element. In the unknown time case, the defect is only an accessory condition that can be removed before it causes harm.
The key is that the ignorance (jahalah) is in an extra condition, so removal is possible and effective.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
Practical difference: According to Abu Hanifa, the sale becomes valid after cancellation; according to Zufar, it remains invalid. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa, as stated in the Hidayah commentary.
The passage also clarifies that only the party benefiting from the time (usually the buyer) can cancel it unilaterally.
