امام زفر کے قیاس کا جواب ہے جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ مفسد کے ثابت ہونے سے پہلے عقد فاسد بدل کر جائز ہو سکتا ہے لیکن ایک عقد بدل کر دوسرا عقد نہیں ہو سکتا اور مدت معینہ تک نکاح کرنا متعہ ہے اور متعہ ، نکاح کے علاوہ ایک عقد ہے پس متعہ بدل کر نکاح نہیں ہو سکتا اور میعاد مجہول کی صورت میں مفسد کو ساقط کرنے سے پہلے بھی وہ عقد بیع تھا اور مفسد کو ساقط کرنے کے بعد بھی عقد بیج ہے صرف اتنا فرق ہے کہ پہلے عقد فاسد تھا اور مفسد ساقط کر کے جائز ہو گیا اپس میعاد مجہول ہونے کی صورت کو نکاح الی اجل پر قیاس کرنا درست نہیں ہے۔ سوال اور رہا یہ سوال کہ جب بغیر گواہ کے نکاح کیا پھر نکاح کے بعد گواہ مقر کر لئے تو یہ نکات بدل کر جائز نہیں ہوتا۔ حالانکہ فسا، حساب عقد میں نہیں ہے۔ جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہاں فساد شرط نکاح نہ پائے جانے کی وجہ سے ہے اور یہ فساد قوی ہے اور یہ ایسا ہے جیسا کہ صلب عقد میں ہو اس لئے اس کا دور کرناممکن اور مفید نہ ہوگا اسکی مثال ایسی ہے جیسے کسی نے بغیر وضو نماز ادا کی پھر وضو کیا تو یہ نماز چونکہ عدم شرط کی وجہ سے فاسد ہوئی ہے اس لئے بدل کر جائز نہ ہوگی۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قدوری کا قول ثم تراضيا اتفاقی ہے۔ یعنی میعاد کو ساقط کرنے کے لئے بائع اور مشتری دونوں کی رضامندی شرط نہیں ہے بلکہ جس کے لئے میعاد ہے وہ تنے تنہا اس کو ساقط کر سکتا ہے کیونکہ میعاد خالص اس کا حق ہے لہذا ساقط کرنے کا حق بھی اس کو ہو گا۔
And this ignorance was in an extra condition, not in the contract itself, therefore it is possible to cancel it. In contrast, if one dirham was sold for two dirhams and then both cancel the extra dirham, (it is not possible) because the defect is in the contract itself. And in contrast to a time-limited marriage because it is temporary marriage (mut'ah), and temporary marriage is a different contract besides marriage. The author's statement 'thumma taradaya' is coincidental. Because only the person for whom the time period is set can cancel it, because the time period is purely his right. Explanation: The scenario is that a person sold some goods with a specified time from the mentioned times, e.g., sold with the condition that the price be paid on Nowruz or at the time of pilgrims' arrival. The buyer accepted. Then before the appointed time, both seller and buyer agreed to cancel the stipulated time. Then this sale becomes valid. But according to Imam Zufar, it did not become valid. Imam Zufar's evidence is that a contract which is once concluded invalidly does not become valid by change. So when the sale became invalid due to an invalid condition, it will not become valid by change even if the invalid condition is cancelled. As in Imam Abu Hanifa's view, if marriage was contracted for a term and then the term is cancelled, this marriage does not become valid by change. And like if marriage was contracted without witnesses and then witnesses were appointed, this marriage, since it was concluded invalidly, cannot become valid by change. And like if one dirham was sold for two dirhams and then one dirham is cancelled, this contract also does not become valid by change. Similarly, when the sale contract was concluded invalidly due to an unknown time, it will not become valid by cancelling the unknown time. Our evidence is: In the case of an unknown time, the sale is invalid because there is a possibility of dispute between seller and buyer, and the dispute will arise when the time arrives. But when both cancel the unknown time, the corrupting factor is removed before it is established, so when the corrupting factor is removed, the sale becomes valid. Then there is the question: When ignorance and corruption are established at the inception of the contract, cancelling it should not be effective, like when one dirham is sold for two dirhams and then both cancel one dirham, this cancellation of the extra dirham is not effective; thus in that case the sale does not become valid by change. The answer: In the case of unknown time, the ignorance is in an extra condition, so its cancellation is possible and effective. In the case of selling a dirham for two dirhams, the corruption is in the core of the contract, i.e., one of the two countervalues, so its cancellation is impossible. The response to Imam Zufar's analogy: 'And in contrast to marriage for a term...' is the response to Imam Zufar's analogy. The gist is: Before the corrupting factor is established, an invalid contract can become valid by change, but one contract cannot change into another contract. Marriage for a specified term is temporary marriage (mut'ah), and mut'ah is a contract different from marriage. So mut'ah cannot become marriage by change. In the case of unknown time, before cancelling the corrupting factor, it was a sale contract, and after cancelling the corrupting factor it is still a sale contract; the only difference is that earlier it was invalid and after removing the corrupting factor it became valid. So analogizing the case of unknown time to marriage for a term is incorrect. Another question: When marriage is contracted without witnesses and then witnesses are appointed after the contract, this marriage does not become valid by change, even though the corruption is not in the contract itself. The answer: The corruption here is due to the absence of the condition for marriage (witnesses), and this corruption is strong, like it is in the core of the contract. Therefore, removing it is impossible and ineffective. An example of this is: If someone prayed without ablution and then performed ablution, this prayer, because it was invalid due to absence of condition, will not become valid by change. The author of Hidayah says that Al-Quduri's statement 'thumma taradaya' is coincidental, meaning that for cancelling the time, the consent of both seller and buyer is not required; rather, the person for whom the time is set can alone cancel it because the time is purely his right, so he also has the right to cancel it.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage deals with a sale contract where the parties agree on an unknown future time for payment (e.g., at Nowruz or when pilgrims arrive). Such a sale is initially invalid (fasid) because the unknown time leads to potential dispute. However, the Hanafi position, as stated by Imam Abu Hanifa and supported by the author of Hidayah, is that if both parties cancel this condition before the time arrives, the sale becomes valid. The reason is that the defect is in an extra condition, not in the contract itself. Therefore, removing the condition is possible and effective. Imam Zufar disagreed, arguing that once a contract is concluded invalidly, it cannot be rectified by later change. He compared it to selling one dirham for two (where the price increase is part of the contract) and to time-limited marriage (mut'ah) which is a different contract. The Hanafi response distinguishes: in the unknown time case, the ignorance is in an accessory condition, not the core of the contract. Hence it can be removed. In contrast, the sale of one dirham for two has corruption in the contract core (one of the countervalues is excess), and mut'ah is an entirely different contract (temporary marriage) that cannot become valid marriage. Another objection about marriage without witnesses is answered: the absence of witnesses is a strong corruption like one in the contract core, so it cannot be removed. Finally, the passage clarifies that the consent of both parties for cancellation is not necessary; only the person benefiting from the time (usually the buyer) can cancel it alone, as emphasized by Al-Quduri's statement 'thumma taradaya' which is explained as coincidental and not a condition.

Key Terms
میعاد مجہول (mi'ad majhul): An unknown or unspecified future time for payment or delivery in a sale contract, e.g., 'at Nowruz' or 'when pilgrims arrive'.
شرط زائد (shart za'id): An extra condition added to a contract that is not part of the core contract terms.
متعہ (mut'ah): Temporary marriage contracted for a fixed period, considered a separate and invalid contract in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a sale with an unknown future time, if both parties cancel the time condition before it arrives, what is the ruling according to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) The sale remains invalid because it was invalid from the start.
B) The sale becomes valid because the defect was in an extra condition and was removed before causing harm.
C) The sale becomes valid but only if the buyer alone cancels the time.
D) The sale becomes invalid because the time condition is an integral part of the contract.

Key Takeaway
A sale with an unknown future time condition becomes valid if the condition is cancelled before its arrival, because the defect is in an extra condition, not in the contract core.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Combining Invalid and Valid Items in One Sale
Rulings on combining a free person with a slave or a slaughtered animal with a dead animal in one sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and Imam Zufar on combining a free person with a slave in a single sale, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
When a free person and slave are sold together, Abu Hanifa invalidates the whole; the Sahibayn permit the slave's sale if prices are named.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about mixing a non-saleable item (like a free person) with a saleable one (like a slave) in one contract. At stake is whether the invalid element infects the entire sale or only its own part. The disagreement between Abu Hanifa, the two Sahibayn, and Imam Zufar turns on different understandings of contract unity and the principle that corruption is limited to its cause.

Guided Path
1
State Abu Hanifa's position
Identify what Abu Hanifa rules when a free person and a slave are sold together, both without and with separate prices. Note his rationale: the free person is not property and cannot enter the contract, so the whole sale is invalid.
Abu Hanifa treats the sale as a single transaction (safqah wahidah) and the inclusion of the free person as an invalid condition.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's counter-position
Find what Abu Yusuf and Muhammad rule. They distinguish: if each item has a named price, the sale of the slave (or slaughtered animal) is valid. They apply the maxim 'al-fasad bi qadr al-mufsid' (corruption is according to the corrupting factor).
They also analogize to marriage with a non-mahram woman and her sister: only the invalid part is affected.
3
Analyze the third position of Imam Zufar
Imam Zufar invalidates the entire sale even when prices are named, arguing by analogy to the first case that the capacity for sale is negated with respect to the whole.
His view is not relied upon (marjuh).
4
Examine the extended cases (mudabbar, mukatab, etc.)
The passage extends the discussion to combining a slave with a mudabbar, mukatab, umm walad, or another's slave. Here the three scholars (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree that the slave's sale is valid because these entities have monetary value. The sale is suspended (mawquf) pending permissions.
Imam Zufar again invalidates the whole even here.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Identify the practical consequence: if a seller combines a free person with a slave and names prices, the transfer of the slave is valid only according to the Sahibayn; this is the relied-upon fatwa. Without named prices, all agree the whole is invalid. For mudabbar etc., the three scholars' view is operative.
This affects contract enforceability and risk for buyers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن جمع بين حر وعبد اوشاة ذكية وميتة بطل البيع فيهما وهذا عند ابي حنيفة وقال ابو يوسف و محمد ان سمى لكل واحد منهما ثمنا جاز فى العبد والشاة الذكية وان جمع بين عبد ومد براوبين عبده وعبد غيره صح البيع في العبد بحصة من الثمن عند علمائنا الثلثة وقال زفر فسد فيهما ومتروك التسمية عامدا كالميتة والمكاتب وام الولد كالمدبر له الاعتبار بالفصل الاول المحلية البيع منتفية بالاضافة الى الكل ولهما ان الفساد بقدر المفسد فلا يتعدى الى القن كمن جمع بين الاجنبية واخته في النكاح بخلاف ما اذا لم يسم ثمن كل واحد لانه مجهول ولا بى حنيفة وهو الفرق بين الفصلين ان الحر لا يدخل تحت العقد اصلا لانه ليس بمال والبيع صفقة واحدة فكان القبول فى الحر شرطا للبيع في العبد وهذا شرط فاسد بخلاف النكاح لانه لا يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة واما البيع فى هولاء موقوف وقد دخلوا تحت العقد لقيه المالية ولهذا ينعقد فى عبد الغير باجازته وفى المكاتب برضاه في الاصح وفي المدير بقضاء القاضي وكذافى ام الولد عند ابي حنيفة وابى يوسف الا ان المالك باستحقاقه المبيع وهولاء باستحقاقهم انفسهم ردوا البيع فكان هذا اشارة الى البقاء كما اذا اشتری عبدین و هلک احدهما قبل القبض وهذا لا يكون شرطا للقبول فى غير المبيع ولا بيعا بالحصة ابتداء ولهذا لا يشترط بيان ثمن كل واحد فيه ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے آزاد اور غلام کو ملا کر بیچا یا ذبح کی ہوئی بکری اور مردار بکری کو ملا کر بیچا تو دونوں کی بیع باطل ہے اور یہ تم ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے اور ابو یوسف اور امام محمد نے فرمایا اگر ہر ایک کا شمن بیان کیا تو غلام اور ذبح کی ہوئی بکری کی بیع جائز ہے۔ او را گر اس نے غلام اور مدبر کو جمع کیا یا اپنے غلام اور دوسرے کے غلام کو جمع کیا تو ہمارے علماء ثلاثہ کے نزدیک غلام کی بیع اس کے حصہ ثمن سے عوض جائز ہے اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ دونوں کی بیع فاسد ہے اور جس ذبیحہ پراللہ کا نام قصداً چھوڑا گیا ہو وہ مردار کے مانند ہے اور ، ماتب اور ام ولد مدبر کے مانند ہے امام زفر کی دلیل پہلے مسئلہ پر قیاس ہے کیونکہ تمام کی طرف نسبت کرتے ہوئے بیچ کا محل منکی ہے اور ساحین
He said: Whoever combines a free person and a slave, or a slaughtered sheep and a dead one, the sale of both is invalid. This is according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: If he specified a price for each one, the sale is permissible for the slave and the slaughtered sheep. If he combines a slave and a mudabbar (one whose freedom is deferred upon death), or his own slave and another's slave, the sale of the slave is valid for a portion of the price according to our three scholars (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). Zufar said: Both are invalid. And the one who intentionally omits the name (tasmiyah) [of Allah?] is like the dead animal. The mukatab (slave contracted for freedom) and umm walad (mother of a child) are like the mudabbar. The consideration is the first section: the capacity for sale is negated in relation to the whole. For them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) [they say]: corruption is according to the corrupting factor, so it does not extend to the qinn (regular slave). Like one who combines a non-mahram woman and her sister in marriage. In contrast to when he does not name the price for each, because it is unknown. And Abu Hanifa's (explanation) is the difference between the two sections: the free person does not enter into the contract at all because he is not property, and the sale is one transaction, so the acceptance in the free person is a condition for the sale of the slave, and this condition is invalid. In contrast to marriage, because it is not invalidated by invalid conditions. As for the sale of these (mudabbar, mukatab, umm walad, another's slave): it is suspended. They have entered into the contract because of the presence of monetary value. For this reason, it is concluded regarding another's slave by his permission, and regarding the mukatab with his consent in the more correct view, and regarding the mudabbar by the judge's decree, and similarly for the umm walad according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, except that the owner, by claiming ownership of the sold item, and these, by claiming themselves, reject the sale. So this indicates the remaining [of the contract] as if he bought two slaves and one perished before possession. And this is not a condition for acceptance in the non-sold item, nor is it a sale by portion initially, and for this reason it is not required to state the price of each one. Translation: And the person who sold together a free person and a slave, or a slaughtered sheep and a dead sheep, the sale of both is invalid, and this is according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad said: If the price of each was stated, then the sale of the slave and the slaughtered sheep is permissible. And if he combined a slave and a mudabbar, or his own slave and another's slave, then according to our three scholars, the sale of the slave is valid for a portion of the price. Imam Zufar said: The sale of both is invalid. And the slaughtered animal on which the name of Allah was intentionally omitted is like the dead animal. The mukatab and umm walad are like the mudabbar. Imam Zufar's evidence is analogy to the first issue, because in relation to the whole, the capacity for sale is negated. And the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) [argue]...
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on combining two items in a single sale when one item cannot be sold (e.g., a free person) or is impure (dead animal). According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a free person and a slave are sold together in one transaction without specifying individual prices, the entire sale is invalid because the free person is not property and cannot be part of a sale; the sale is a single transaction, and the acceptance of the free person's inclusion is an invalid condition that corrupts the whole. Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad differ: if a price is stated for each item separately, the sale is valid for the slave (or slaughtered sheep) because the corruption is limited to the free person (or dead animal) and does not extend to the valid item. They rely on the principle 'al-fasad bi qadr al-mufsid' (corruption is according to the corrupting factor). Imam Zufar goes further, declaring the entire sale invalid even if prices are stated, using analogy to the first case. The passage also covers cases of combining a slave with a mudabbar, mukatab, umm walad, or another's slave. Here, the three scholars (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree that the sale of the slave is valid for a portion of the price because these individuals do have monetary value and are capable of being sold. The sale is suspended (mawquf) pending permission or consent. Imam Zufar again invalidates the whole. The relied-upon position is that of the three scholars, with explicit mention that for the mudabbar and umm walad, specific rules apply (e.g., need for judge's decree). The text also clarifies that intentionally omitting tasmiyah (saying 'Bismillah' during slaughter) renders the animal like carrion, invalid for sale.

Key Terms
حر (hurr): A free person, not a slave. In this context, a free person cannot be sold because he is not property (mal).
شاة ذكية (shah dhakiyyah): A sheep that has been slaughtered according to Islamic rites (tadhkiyah), thus permissible to eat and sell.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose master has declared that he will be free upon the master's death (tadbir). He has monetary value but his freedom is contingent.
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has contracted with his master for manumission by paying a sum (kitabah). He has limited ownership rights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position, what is the ruling if a seller combines a free person and a slave in one contract and does NOT specify individual prices?
A) The sale of the slave is valid.
B) The entire sale is invalid.
C) The sale is suspended pending agreement.
D) The buyer may choose to enforce the sale of the slave.

Key Takeaway
When a valid item is sold together with an invalid one, the relied-upon Hanafi position is that the valid item's sale is still valid if its price is separately stated, in line with the principle that corruption is limited to its cause.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
advanced
10 min
Combining Non-Saleable and Saleable Items in a Single Sale
Rulings on combining non-saleable items with saleable ones in one sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on combining a free person with a slave (or dead animal with slaughtered) in one sale, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the principle of fasad bi qadr al-mufsid to distinguish valid from void parts of a transaction.

Core Idea
A free person cannot be sold; including him corrupts the entire sale unless price is specified for the saleable item.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah examines a critical question in sale contracts: what happens when you combine an item that cannot be sold (like a free person or a dead animal) with a saleable item in a single transaction? The Hanafi school contains an important internal dispute on this issue between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two leading students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. By studying this passage, you will learn how the principle that 'corruption is limited to the corrupting element' (fasad bi qadr al-mufsid) can salvage part of a transaction, and where it fails. The passage also covers combining a slave with a mudabbar or another's slave, and the ruling on an animal slaughtered without mentioning Allah's name.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Main Cases
The passage presents two distinct scenarios: (1) combining a free person with a slave, or a dead animal with a slaughtered animal; (2) combining a slave with a mudabbar (a slave whose emancipation is deferred), or one's own slave with another's slave. Note the ruling for each.
The first case involves items with no monetary value; the second involves items that have monetary value but are not fully owned or are restricted.
2
Analyze the Dispute in the First Case
Abu Hanifa rules the entire sale void (batil) regardless of price specification. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rule that if the price for each is specified, the sale of the slave (or slaughtered animal) is valid. Identify their respective evidences.
The key evidence: Abu Hanifa argues that the free person cannot enter the contract at all, so accepting his inclusion is a corrupt condition that voids the whole. The Sahibayn argue that corruption is limited to the corrupt element, using the analogy of marrying a strange woman and one's sister together.
3
Examine the Second Case and Zufar's Opposition
The three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree that the owned slave's sale is valid for its share of the price, while the mudabbar or other's slave is fasid. Zufar holds the entire sale void. Understand why the three imams distinguish this case from the first: these items have monetary value and enter the contract as suspended sales.
The owned slave's sale is valid because the corrupt element is separate, and the sale is by share. Zufar applies the same logic as Abu Hanifa in the first case.
4
Clarify the Ruling on Tark al-Tasmiyah
The author equates an animal slaughtered without mentioning Allah's name intentionally (matruk al-tasmiyah amdan) with a dead animal, so combining it with a slaughtered sheep voids the whole sale. The passage includes a question-answer affirming that this is not a valid ikhtilaf; the Shafi'i view allowing it is deemed an error against the Quran.
This confirms that the Hanafi ruling is decisive despite external disagreement.
5
Synthesize the Practical Consequences
For the first case, the practical difference: if price is specified, the Sahibayn allow the buyer to take the slave, while Abu Hanifa does not. For the second case, the owned slave is valid, but the mudabbar requires permission. For tark al-tasmiyah, the sale is void like dead animal.
The mufta bihi in later practice often follows the Sahibayn in the first case when price is specified.

آزاد اور غلام کی شاة مذبوحہ اور میتہ کی بیع باطل ہے
قال ومن جمع بين حر وعبد أو شاة ذكية وميتة بطل البيع فيهما وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد إن سمى لكل واحد منهما ثمنا جاز في العبد والشاة الذكية وإن جمع بين عبد ومدبر وبين عبده وعبد غيره صح البيع في العبد بحصة من الثمن عند علمائنا الثلاثة وقال زفر فسد فيهما ومتروك التسمية عامدا كالميتة والمكاتب وأم الولد كالمدبر له الاعتبار بالفصل الأول المحلية البيع منتفية بالإضافة إلى الكل ولهما أن الفساد بقدر المفسد فلا يتعدى إلى القن كمن جمع بين الأجنبية وأخته في النكاح بخلاف ما إذا لم يسم ثمن كل واحد لأنه مجهول ولأبي حنيفة وهو الفرق بين الفصلين أن الحر لا يدخل تحت العقد أصلا لأنه ليس بمال والبيع صفقة واحدة فكان القبول في الحر شرطا للبيع في العبد وهذا شرط فاسد بخلاف النكاح لأنه لا يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة وأما البيع في هؤلاء موقوف وقد دخلوا تحت العقل لقيام المالية ولهذا ينعقد في عبد الغير بإجازته وفي المكاتب برضاه في الأصح وفي المدبر بقضاء القاضي وكذا في أم الولد عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف إلا أن المالك باستحقاقه المبيع وهؤلاء باستحقاقهم أنفسهم ردوا البيع فكان هذا إشارة إلى البقاء كما إذا اشترى عبدين وهلك أحدهما قبل القبض وهذا لا يكون شرطا للقبول في غير المبيع ولا بيعا بالحصة ابتداء ولهذا لا يشترط بيان ثمن كل واحد فيه
ترجمہ: اور جس شخص نے آزاد اور غلام کو ملا کر بیچا یا ذبح کی ہوئی بکری اور مردار بکری کو ملا کر بیچا تو دونوں کی بیع باطل ہے اور یہ ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف اور امام محمد نے فرمایا اگر ہر ایک کا ثمن بیان کیا تو غلام اور ذبح کی ہوئی بکری کی بیع جائز ہے۔ اور اگر اس نے غلام اور مدبر کو جمع کیا یا اپنے غلام اور دوسرے کے غلام کو جمع کیا تو ہمارے علماء ثلاثہ کے نزدیک غلام کی بیع اس کے حصہ ثمن سے عوض جائز ہے اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ دونوں کی بیع فاسد ہے۔ اور جس ذبیحہ پر اللہ کا نام قصداً چھوڑا گیا ہو وہ مردار کے مانند ہے۔ اور مكاتب اور أم ولد مدبر کے مانند ہے۔ امام زفر کی دلیل پہلے مسئلہ پر قیاس ہے کیونکہ تمام کی طرف نسبت کرتے ہوئے بیع کا محل منتفی ہے۔ اور صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ فساد بقدر مفسد ہوتا ہے، اس لئے یہ فساد غلام کی طرف متعدی نہ ہوگا جیسے کسی نے اجنبیہ عورت اور اپنی بہن کو نکاح میں جمع کیا، برخلاف اس کے جب کہ ہر ایک کا ثمن بیان نہ کیا ہو کیونکہ ثمن مجہول ہے۔ اور ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے اور یہی دونوں مسئلوں میں فرق ہے کہ آزاد عقد کے تحت بالکل داخل نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ آزاد مال نہیں ہے اور بیع صفقة واحدہ ہے، پس غلام کی بیع قبول کرنے کے واسطے آزاد کی بیع قبول کرنا شرط ہوا حالانکہ یہ شرط فاسد ہے، برخلاف نکاح کے کیونکہ نکاح شروط فاسدہ سے باطل نہیں ہوتا۔ اور رہی ان کی بیع تو وہ موقوف ہے اور مالیت کے موجود ہونے کی وجہ سے یہ بیع کے تحت داخل ہو گئے، اسی لئے دوسرے کے غلام کی بیع اس کی اجازت سے نافذ ہو جائے گی، اور مکاتب کی بیع اس کی رضامندی سے اصح قول کے مطابق نافذ ہو جائے گی، اور مدبر کی بیع بحکم قاضی نافذ ہو جائے گی۔ اور اسی طرح مشائخ کے نزدیک أم ولد کی بیع، مگر یہ کہ مالک نے مبیع کے مستحق ہونے کی وجہ سے اور مدبر وغیرہ نے خود اپنی ذات کا مستحق ہونے کی وجہ سے بیع کو رد کر دیا، پس یہ بقاء کی طرف اشارہ ہے جیسے کسی نے دو غلام خریدے اور قبضہ سے پہلے ان دونوں میں سے ایک ہلاک ہو گیا، اور یہ غیر مبیع میں قبول کرنے کی شرط نہ ہو اور نہ بیع بالحصہ ابتداء ہوا، اسی لئے اس میں ہر ایک کا ثمن بیان کرنا شرط نہیں ہے۔
تشریح: صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے آزاد آدمی اور اپنے غلام کو ملا کر فروخت کیا یا مذبوحہ بکری اور مردار بکری کو ملا کر فروخت کیا تو حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک دونوں صورتوں میں دونوں کی بیع باطل ہے خواہ دونوں کا ثمن علیحدہ علیحدہ بیان کیا ہو یا علیحدہ علیحدہ بیان نہ کیا ہو، اسی کے قائل امام مالک ہیں، یہی ایک قول امام شافعی کا ہے، اور امام احمد کی ایک روایت بھی یہی ہے۔ اور صاحبین نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر دونوں کا ثمن علیحدہ علیحدہ بیان کیا ہو مثلاً یہ کہا کہ میں نے آزاد اور غلام یا مذبوحہ بکری اور مردار بکری کو ایک ہزار روپیہ کے عوض خریدا اور ان میں سے ہر ایک کا ثمن پانچ سو روپیہ ہے تو اس صورت میں غلام اور مذبوحہ بکری کی بیع جائز ہو جائے گی اور آزاد اور مردار بکری کی بیع باطل ہو جائے گی، اور اگر دونوں کا ثمن علیحدہ علیحدہ بیان نہ کیا ہو تو دونوں کی بیع باطل ہو جائے گی جیسا کہ حضرت امام اعظم کا مذہب ہے، حضرت امام شافعی کا ایک قول بھی یہی ہے، اور امام احمد کی ایک روایت بھی یہی ہے۔ اور اگر غلام اور مدبر کو ملا کر فروخت کیا یا اپنے مملوک غلام اور دوسرے کے غلام کو ملا کر فروخت کیا تو حضرت امام ابوحنیفہ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک غلام مملوک کی بیع اس کے حصہ ثمن کے عوض جائز ہے اور مدبر یا غیر مملوک غلام کی بیع فاسد ہے، اور امام زفر کے نزدیک غلام اور مدبر اور اپنے غلام اور دوسرے کے غلام دونوں کی بیع فاسد ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جس ذبیحہ پر اللہ کا نام عمداً چھوڑا گیا ہو وہ مردار کے مانند ہے، چنانچہ اگر مذبوحہ بکری کو اس کے ساتھ ملا کر فروخت کیا گیا تو دونوں کی بیع باطل ہے جیسا کہ ذبیحہ بکری اور مردار بکری کو ملا کر فروخت کرنے کی صورت میں دونوں کی بیع باطل ہوتی ہے۔
سوال: یہاں ایک سوال ہے وہ یہ کہ متروک التسمیہ عامداً مختلف فیہ ہے، احناف کے نزدیک اگرچہ اس کا کھانا ناجائز ہے لیکن شوافع کے نزدیک جائز ہے، پس اختلاف ائمہ کی وجہ سے اس کی حرمت چونکہ خفیف ہو گئی ہے اس لئے اس کا حکم مدبر کے مانند ہوگا، اور غلام اور مدبر کو ملا کر فروخت کرنے کی صورت میں چونکہ غلام کی بیع جائز ہوتی ہے، لہذا مذبوحہ بکری اور متروک التسمیہ عامداً کو ملا کر فروخت کرنے کی صورت میں بھی مذبوحہ بکری کی بیع جائز ہونی چاہئے تھی۔
جواب یہ ہے کہ متروک التسمیہ عامداً مختلف فیہ نہیں ہے بلکہ دلیل ظاہر یعنی قول باری تعالیٰ {وَلا تَأْكُلُوا مِمَّا لَمْ يُذْكَرِ اسْمُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِ} کی مخالفت کرنے کی وجہ سے شوافع کی کھلی ہوئی غلطی ہے، یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر قاضی متروک التسمیہ عامداً کے حلال ہونے کا فیصلہ کرے تو اس کا فیصلہ نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ پس متروک التسمیہ عامداً مدبر کے مرتبہ میں نہ ہوگا بلکہ متروک التسمیہ عامداً اور ذبیحہ بکری کو ملا کر بیچنا ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ مردار اور ذبیحہ کو ملا کر بیچنا۔
The sale of a free person and a slave, or a slaughtered sheep and a dead sheep, is void. This is according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: If he specifies a price for each, the sale of the slave and the slaughtered sheep is valid. If he combines a slave and a mudabbar, or his own slave and another's slave, the sale of the slave is valid for its share of the price according to our three imams. Zufar said: Both are void. The intentionally unnamed slaughtered animal is like a dead one. The mukatab and umm walad are like the mudabbar. The consideration is of the first case: the capacity for sale is negated in relation to the whole. Their (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's) evidence is that corruption is proportionate to the corrupting element, so it does not extend to the slave, like one who combines a strange woman and his sister in marriage. Contrary to when he does not specify the price of each, because it is unknown. Abu Hanifa's evidence, and this is the distinction between the two cases, is that the free person does not enter the contract at all because he is not property, and the sale is a single transaction, so acceptance in the free person is a condition for the sale of the slave, and this is a corrupt condition, unlike marriage because marriage is not invalidated by corrupt conditions. As for the sale of these (mudabbar, etc.), it is suspended, and they have entered the contract due to the existence of monetary value, and for this reason it is concluded in another's slave with his permission, in the mukatab with his consent according to the soundest opinion, in the mudabbar by the judge's decree, and similarly in the umm walad according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, except that the owner, due to his entitlement to the sold item, and these due to their entitlement to themselves, have rejected the sale, so this indicates continuity, like when one buys two slaves and one dies before delivery, and this (the death) is not a condition for acceptance in the non-sold item, nor is it an initial sale by share, and for this reason specifying the price of each is not required therein.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents a detailed ruling on combining non-saleable items (such as a free person or a dead animal) with saleable items (such as a slave or slaughtered animal) in a single sale. The passage begins by stating the ruling on combining a free person with a slave or a slaughtered sheep with a dead sheep: according to Abu Hanifa, the sale is void (batil) for both items, regardless of whether the price is specified separately or not. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that if the price of each is specified separately, the sale of the slave and the slaughtered sheep is valid, while the free person and dead sheep remain void. If the price is not specified, all are void. The passage then addresses a second case: combining a slave with a mudabbar (a slave whose emancipation is deferred after the master's death) or one's own slave with another's slave. Here, the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree that the sale of the owned slave is valid for its share of the price, while the mudabbar or other's slave is sold invalidly (fasid). Zufar differs, holding the entire sale void. The author also adds that an animal on which Allah's name was intentionally omitted (tark al-tasmiyah amdan) is treated like a dead animal, so combining it with a slaughtered one makes the whole sale void. A subsequent question and answer clarify that tark al-tasmiyah amdan is not truly disputed among schools; the Shafi'i view allowing it is deemed a clear error against the Qur'anic verse (6:121), so its ruling remains as a dead animal. The commentary provides the legal reasoning: Abu Hanifa argues that the free person cannot be the subject of sale at all, so including him makes the entire contract a single transaction with a corrupt condition (accepting the free person's sale as a condition for the slave's sale). The Sahibayn argue that the corruption is confined to the corrupt element (the free person) and does not extend to the saleable item (the slave) when the price is specified, analogous to marrying a strange woman and one's sister together where the marriage to the sister is valid. Zufar extends the analogy to the second case, but the majority restrict it. The key principle is that a free person does not enter the contract, while a mudabbar or another's slave does enter but the sale is suspended (mawquf) pending approval, hence the difference in ruling.

Key Terms
صفقة واحدة (safqah wahidah): A single transaction where all items are sold together as one unit, not divisible.
فساد بقدر المفسد (fasad bi qadr al-mufsid): The corruption is limited to the extent of the corrupting element and does not spread to the valid part.
متروك التسمية عامداً (matruk al-tasmiyah amdan): An animal slaughtered without mentioning Allah's name intentionally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling if a free person and a slave are sold together without specifying each price?
A) The sale of the slave is valid; the free person is void.
B) The entire sale is void (batil).
C) The sale is suspended pending the free person's consent.
D) The sale is valid if the price is fair.

Key Takeaway
When combining non-saleable items with saleable ones in one sale, the ruling hinges on whether the non-saleable item has any monetary value and whether the price is specified—Abu Hanifa voids the whole, while the Sahibayn salvage the saleable part if the price is apportioned.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
Selling a Free Person and a Slave Together: The Hanafi Ikhtilaf
States the ruling and ikhtilaf on mixing free and slave in one sale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the sale of a free person with a slave in a single contract, and identify the condition under which the Sahibayn validate the slave's sale.

Core Idea
Mixing a non-saleable item with a saleable one in one contract: Abu Hanifa invalidates all; Sahibayn save the saleable if prices are separate.

In this lesson, we examine a foundational Hanafi dispute regarding the sale of a free person (who cannot be sold) together with a slave (who can) in a single transaction. The ruling hinges on whether the mixed contract is treated as one undivided unit or as separate sales. We will trace the arguments of Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and see how their positions shape practical transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Two items are sold together: one valid (slave/slaughtered goat) and one invalid (free man/carrion).
The invalid item is not legally owned or saleable (e.g., a free person is not property).
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling
He considers the entire contract invalid (fasid) regardless of whether prices are stated separately because the invalid item cannot be sold, making the whole transaction corrupt.
The contract is a single safqah (transaction); mixing a non-property item spoils the whole.
3
State the Sahibayn's ruling
They distinguish: if separate prices are declared, the valid item's sale is valid (sahih) and the invalid item's sale is void (batil). If no separate prices, both are invalid due to ambiguity (jahalah) in the price of the valid item.
The key condition is separate pricing; without it, the entire contract fails.
4
Note cross-madhhab agreement
Imam Malik, one view of al-Shafi'i, and one transmission from Ahmad agree with Abu Hanifa that both sales are invalid even with separate prices.
This ikhtilaf is a legitimate scholarly difference.
5
Apply the principle
Understand that the thaman (price) ambiguity is the decisive factor for the Sahibayn; separate pricing preserves the valid part of the contract.
In practice, always state individual prices when mixing valid and potentially invalid items.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے آزاد آدمی اور اپنے غلام کو ملا کر فروخت کیا باند بوحہ بکری اور مردار بکری کو ملا کر فروخت کیا تو حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک دونوں صورتوں میں دونوں کی بیع باطل ہے خواہ دونوں کا شمن علیحدہ علیحدہ بیان کیا ہو یا علیحدہ علیحدہ بیان نہ کیا ہو اسی کے قائل امام مالک ہیں یہی ایک قول امام شافعی کا ہے اور امام احمد کی ایک روایت بھی یہی ہے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر دونوں کا شمن علیحدہ علیحدہ بیان کیا ہو مثلاً یہ کہا کہ میں نے آزاد اور غلام باند بوحہ بکری اور مردار بکری کو ایک ہزار روپیہ کے عوض خریدا اور ان میں سے ہر ایک کا شمن پانچ سو روپیہ ہے تو اس صورت میں غلام اور مذبوحہ بکری کی بیع جائز ہو جائے گی اور آزاد اور مردار بکری کی بیع باطل ہو جائے گی اور اگر دونوں کا شمن علیحدہ علیحدہ بیان نہ کیا ہو تو دونوں کی بیع باطل ہو جائے گی جیسا کہ حضرت امام اعظم کا مذہب ہے حضرت امام شافعی کا ایک قول بھی یہی ہے اور امام احمد کی ایک روایت بھی یہی ہے
Explanation of the case: If someone sold a free man and his own slave together, or a slaughtered goat and a dead goat together, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, in both cases the sale of both is invalid, whether their prices were stated separately or not stated separately. Imam Malik holds the same view, and it is one of the sayings of Imam al-Shafi'i, and one transmission from Imam Ahmad is also this. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: If their prices were stated separately, for example, he said, "I bought the free man and the slave, or the slaughtered goat and the dead goat, for one thousand rupees, and the price of each is five hundred rupees," then in this case the sale of the slave and the slaughtered goat is valid, and the sale of the free man and the dead goat is invalid. But if their prices were not stated separately, then the sale of both is invalid, as is the madhhab of Imam A'zam. One saying of Imam al-Shafi'i is also this, and one transmission from Imam Ahmad is also this.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a memorization anchor presenting the initial Hanafi ikhtilaf on the ruling when a valid object (slave, slaughtered goat) is mixed with an invalid object (free man, carrion) in a single sale contract. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that in such a mixed sale, the entire contract is invalid regardless of whether the prices are stated separately. This is because the free man is not property (mal) and cannot be the subject of a sale; the inclusion of a non-property item renders the entire contract invalid. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) distinguish: if the prices are declared separately, then the sale of the valid item (slave, slaughtered goat) is valid, while the invalid item's sale is void. If no separate prices are stated, then the entire sale is invalid due to ambiguity (jahalah) in the price of the valid item. The passage also notes that Imam Malik, one view of al-Shafi'i, and one transmission from Ahmad agree with Abu Hanifa. This is a core ruling in Hanafi fiqh concerning the impact of mixing a valid and invalid object in one sale transaction.

Key Terms
صفقة واحدة (safqah wahidah): A single transaction or contract in which multiple items are sold together as a unit.
ثمن (thaman): The price or consideration in a sale contract.
فساد (fasad): Invalidity or corruption of a contract that is not fundamentally void (batil) but can be corrected.

A) Only if the buyer agrees to accept both

When a valid and invalid item are sold together, Abu Hanifa invalidates the entire contract; the Sahibayn allow the valid item's sale if prices are designated separately.

Intentional Omission of Tasmiyah: Ruling and Hanafi Defense
Ruling with proof and defense against Shafi'i objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an animal intentionally slaughtered without tasmiyah and evaluate the Shafi'i counterargument using the Quranic dalil.

Core Idea
An animal intentionally slaughtered without tasmiyah is carrion – its sale invalidates the entire mixed transaction.

This lesson examines a key ruling from Al-Hidayah regarding the status of an animal slaughtered without pronouncing Allah's name intentionally. The Hanafi school considers such meat impermissible and treats the animal as carrion, affecting sales. We will explore the Quranic proof and the school's response to a valid objection from the Shafi'i perspective.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The passage rules that an animal slaughtered without tasmiyah intentionally is like carrion. Determine the act (tasmiyah omission) and the hukm (haram consumption, invalid sale).
The animal is not just prohibited; it is legally carrion.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: the Quranic verse from Surah al-An'am (6:121). Identify its type (Quran, qat'i al-thubut).
The verse is quoted in the answer to the objection.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the verse proves the ruling: the absolute prohibition (لا تأكلوا) indicates any intentional omission makes the meat haram, regardless of the slaughterer's faith.
The Hanafi usul principle: al-amr (or prohibition here) on a general cause is general until specified.
4
Consider the Shafi'i objection
The objector argues that since there is ikhtilaf (Shafi'is allow it), the prohibition is weakened, likening it to a mudabbir. Identify this argument.
The objection is that the animal's status is ambiguous like a mudabbir, so sale with a valid animal should be partially valid.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The response rejects the Shafi'i view as a clear mistake (khalil ghalat) because the Quranic text is manifest. The Hanafi ruling is definitive, and if a judge rules otherwise, his ruling is not enforceable.
The mudabbir analogy fails because the untasmiyah animal is not disputed; it is clearly carrion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جس ذبیحہ پر اللہ کا نام عمداً چھوڑا گیا ہو وہ مردار کے مانند ہے چنانچہ اگر مذبوحہ بکری کو ملا کر فروخت کیا گیا تو دونوں کی بیع باطل ہے جیسا کہ ذبیحہ بکری اور مردار بکری کو ملا کر فروخت کرنے کی صورت میں دونوں کی بیع باطل ہوتی ہے۔ سوال .... یہاں ایک سوال ہے وہ یہ کہ متروک التسمیہ عامداً مختلف فیہ ہے۔ احناف کے نزدیک اگر چہ اس کا کھانا نا جائز ہے لیکن شوافع کے نزدیک جائز ہے پس اختلاف ائمہ کی وجہ سے اس کی حرمت چونکہ خفیف ہو گئی ہے اس لئے اس کا حکم مدبر کے مانند ہوگا اور غلام اور مد بر کو ملا کر فروخت کرنے کی صورت میں چونکہ غلام کی بیع جائز ہوتی ہے لہذاند بوحہ بکری اور متروک التسمیہ عامداً کو ملا کر فروخت کرنے کی صورت میں بھی مذبوحہ بکری کی بیع جائز ہونی چاہئے تھی۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ متروک التسمیہ عامد امختلف فیہ نہیں ہے بلکہ دلیل ظاہر یعنی قول باری تعالی ولاتا كلو امما لم يذكر اسم الله علیہ کی مخالفت کرنے کی وجہ سے شوافع کی کھلی ہوئی غلطی ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر قاضی متروک التسمیہ عامد احلال ہونے کا فیصلہ کرے تو اس کا فیصلہ نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ پس متروک القسمیہ عامد امد بر کے مرتبہ میں نہ ہوگا بلکہ متروک التسمیہ عامداً اور ذبیحہ بکری کو ملا کر بیچنا ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ آزاد اور غلام کو ملا کر بیچنا بہر حال یہ ثابت ہو گیا کہ متروک التسمیہ عامد امردار کے حکم میں ہے
The author of Al-Hidayah says: The animal upon which the name of Allah was intentionally omitted is like carrion. Thus, if it is sold mixed with a slaughtered goat, then the sale of both is invalid, just as when a slaughtered goat and a carrion goat are sold together, the sale of both is invalid. Question: There is a question: The animal on which tasmiyah was intentionally omitted is disputed. According to the Hanafis, its consumption is impermissible, but according to the Shafi'is, it is permissible. Therefore, due to the difference of the imams, its prohibition is lightened, so its ruling should be like that of a mudabbir (who is partially free). And in the case of selling a slave with a mudabbir, the sale of the slave is valid. Likewise, when a slaughtered goat and an intentionally untasmiyah goat are sold together, the sale of the slaughtered goat should have been valid. The answer is that the intentionally untasmiyah animal is not disputed; rather, it is a clear mistake of the Shafi'is because they oppose the manifest evidence, namely the saying of Allah Most High: 'Do not eat of that over which the name of Allah has not been mentioned.' For this reason, if a judge rules that the intentionally untasmiyah animal is lawful, his ruling is not enforceable. So the intentionally untasmiyah animal is not on the level of a mudabbir; rather, selling it with a slaughtered goat is like selling a free person with a slave. In any case, it is established that the intentionally untasmiyah animal is in the ruling of carrion.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe by the commentator, addressing a specific objection regarding the ruling on an animal intentionally slaughtered without tasmiyah (declaration of Allah's name). The author of Hidayah rules that such an animal is equivalent to carrion, so selling it mixed with a validly slaughtered goat invalidates the entire sale. An objection is raised: since there is ikhtilaf between the Hanafis and Shafi'is on the permissibility of eating such meat (Hanafis: haram, Shafi'is: halal), its prohibition is weakened, so it should be treated like a mudabbir (whose status is ambiguous, not fully property). In the case of selling a slave with a mudabbir, the slave's sale remains valid. Hence, selling a slaughtered goat with an untasmiyah goat should also leave the slaughtered goat's sale valid. The commentary refutes this: the untasmiyah animal is not actually disputed; the Shafi'i view is a clear error because it contradicts the Qur'anic verse (al-An'am 6:121). Therefore, it is like carrion, not a mudabbir. The analogy is with the free person and slave case: just as selling a free and slave together invalidates the slave's sale (according to Abu Hanifa), here too both are invalid. The ruling confirms that the untasmiyah animal is carrion in this context, and its inclusion in a mixed sale nullifies the whole transaction.

Key Terms
متروک التسمیہ عامداً (mutaraku al-tasmiyah 'amdan): An animal slaughtered with the intentional omission of declaring Allah's name.
مدبر (mudabbir): A slave who is promised freedom upon the master's death.

B) Because it contradicts the explicit Quranic verse
C) Because the animal is a mudabbir
D) Because the majority of scholars agree

Key Takeaway
An animal intentionally slaughtered without tasmiyah is treated as carrion, and its inclusion in a sale invalidates the entire transaction, based on the clear Quranic prohibition.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Sale of Slave with Mudabbir
Presents intra-Hanafi dispute on mixed sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and Imam Zufar on the sale of a slave mixed with a mudabbir, and explain the reasoning (qiyas vs. confinement of corruption) that leads to their differing rulings.

Core Idea
Corruption is confined to its cause: the Sahibayn limit fasad to the invalid item; Imam Zufar extends it via qiyas.

This passage delves into an intra-Hanafi disagreement over whether mixing a slave with a mudabbir (or another's slave) in a single sale invalidates the entire transaction or only the mudabbir's portion. Imam Zufar analogizes to the sale of a free person with a slave, where both are invalid. The Sahibayn and Abu Hanifa distinguish the cases based on the nature of property and the confinement of corruption. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply qiyas and recognize when analogies fail.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three Hanafi positions
List the rulings of Imam Zufar, the Sahibayn, and Abu Hanifa regarding the sale of a slave and a mudabbir together. Note that for Imam Zufar both sales are fasid, while for the Sahibayn and Abu Hanifa the slave's sale is valid and the mudabbir's is fasid (except when prices are not stated separately).
2
Examine Imam Zufar's qiyas
Determine the original case (asl): sale of a free person with a slave. Identify the new case (far'): sale of a slave with a mudabbir. Find the common cause ('illah) he uses: all are not proper subjects of sale (mahall bay'). Observe his conclusion that both are fasid.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's objection
Understand their principle: corruption is confined to the element that causes it (al-fasad biqadr al-mufsid). The mudabbir is still property, unlike a free person, so the corrupting element is only the mudabbir; thus fasad does not extend to the slave. Note their analogy to marriage (sister invalid, stranger valid).
4
Understand Abu Hanifa's additional reasoning
Abu Hanifa distinguishes the free+slave case from slave+mudabbir. In the free+slave case, the contract is a single transaction (safqah wahidah) because the buyer cannot accept only part. Including a non-property item imposes a fasid condition, invalidating the entire sale. For the mudabbir, no such condition exists because both are property, so the slave's sale remains valid.
5
Apply the principle to practical cases
Consider the separate price declaration exception: if prices are stated separately, the slave's sale is valid even in the free+slave case. For slave+mudabbir, the default ruling (Sahibayn) is slave valid, mudabbir fasid. Use this to answer hypotheticals.

And the mukatab and umm walad are like the mudabbir. Thus, if a mukatab or umm walad is sold mixed with a slave, the sale of the slave is valid for his portion of the price. Imam Zufar's proof is qiyas: He analogized the sale of a slave with a mudabbir, or one's own slave with another's slave, to the first case of selling a free person with a slave. Just as in the sale of a free person and a slave, the sale of both is invalid, similarly in the sale of a slave and a mudabbir, the sale of both becomes fasid. The common cause (illah) is that the free person, carrion, mudabbir, and another's slave are not proper subjects of sale. So the same ruling applies. The proof of the Sahibayn is: corruption is confined to the corrupting element. The corruptor exists only in the free man and carrion because they are not property, so they are not proper subjects of sale. Thus corruption is confined to them and does not extend to the slave or slaughtered goat, just as in selling a slave and a mudabbir, the corruption remains with the mudabbir and does not extend to the slave. This is like when someone marries a stranger and his own sister together: the sister's marriage is invalid, but the stranger's is valid. However, if a free person and a slave are sold together and their prices are not stated separately, both sales are fasid because the price of the slave is unknown, and the unknown price is a corrupting factor. But when the prices are stated separately, the slave's sale is valid due to the absence of price ignorance. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa: And this is the difference between the two issues (the sale of free+slave and the sale of slave+mudabbir): that a free person and a carrion animal are not at all included under the contract of sale because they are not property, and non-property is not included under a sale contract. And the sale of a free person and a slave, or a slaughtered goat and carrion, is a single transaction (safqah wahidah). The proof of this is that if the buyer wants to accept the sale of only the slave or only the slaughtered goat, he has no such option; he must accept or reject both. Therefore, the lack of choice to accept only one part proves it is a single transaction. So selling a free person with a slave is a single transaction. Since the free person is not included in the sale because he is not property, he becomes a non-sold item (ghayr mabi'). The slave is the sold item. Thus, the seller has placed a condition that to accept the sale of the slave (the sold item), the buyer must also accept the sale of the free person (the non-sold item). This is a fasid condition, and a fasid condition invalidates the sale, so the sale of the slave also becomes fasid.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe that presents the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sale of a slave mixed with a mudabbir or another's slave. The text opens by stating that the ruling for a mukatab (slave contractually purchasing freedom) and umm walad (female slave who bore her master's child) is the same as for a mudabbir (slave promised freedom after master's death): if sold with a slave, the slave's sale is valid for his share. Then the views of Imam Zufar, the Sahibayn, and Abu Hanifa are given. Imam Zufar applies qiyas (analogy) to the earlier case of selling a free person with a slave: since the free person is not a proper subject of sale, the entire transaction is invalid. He extends this to the mudabbir and another's slave, arguing that they too are problematic subjects, so both sales are invalid. The Sahibayn reject this, arguing that fasad (corruption) is confined to the element that causes it. The corruptor here is the free person or carrion because they are not property; similarly, the mudabbir or another's slave are not fully owned by the seller, but the slave is fully owned, so corruption remains with the non-proper subject and does not extend to the slave. They analogize to marriage: marrying a stranger and one's sister results in the sister's marriage being invalid but the stranger's valid. However, if prices are not declared separately, the slave's price is unknown, which causes fasad in that sale as well. Abu Hanifa's reasoning focuses on the nature of the contract as a single transaction (safqah wahidah). Since the buyer cannot choose to accept only part, the inclusion of a non-property item (free person) imposes a condition on the slave's sale that is fasid, thus invalidating the entire sale. This reasoning applies to the free+slave case, but he distinguishes the slave+mudabbir case where the mudabbir is still property (though with limited ownership), so the condition argument does not apply.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract of kitabah to purchase his freedom over time.
ام ولد (umm walad): A female slave who has borne a child to her master, becoming entitled to freedom upon his death.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning used to extend a ruling from a known case to a new case based on a shared effective cause.
صفقة واحدة (safqah wahidah): A single transaction or bargain involving multiple items in one contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, why does the corruption (fasad) in the sale of a slave with a mudabbir not extend to the slave?
A) Because the slave is sold separately
B) Because the mudabbir is still property
C) Because the corruption is confined to the invalid item only
D) Because the buyer has a choice

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school, through the Sahibayn and Abu Hanifa, holds that when a slave is sold together with a mudabbir, the slave's sale remains valid because corruption is confined to the invalid part; Imam Zufar's broader analogy is rejected.

Sale of a Free Person with a Slave: Dispute and Proof
Analyzes rulings and proofs for selling a free man with a slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Imam Abu Hanifa rules that the sale of a slave is void when sold with a free person in a single transaction, and evaluate the opposing views of Sahibayn and Imam Zufar.

Core Idea
A single contract cannot mix a saleable item with a non-saleable one; the invalid condition voids the entire sale.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a critical dispute within the Hanafi school regarding the sale of a free person together with a slave. While all Hanafis agree that the free person cannot be sold, they differ on whether the invalidity extends to the slave. Imam Abu Hanifa argues that the sale is a single transaction and the condition to accept the free person is an invalid condition (shart fasid) that benefits the seller, thus voiding the entire contract. The Sahibayn and Imam Zufar offer alternative views. Understanding this dispute illuminates the Hanafi principles of contract unity and the effect of invalid conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the different rulings
First, recognize that the act in question is selling a free person and a slave together in a single contract. Note that Imam Abu Hanifa holds the entire sale void, Sahibayn hold the slave's sale valid (if prices are specified), and Imam Zufar holds both void.
2
Understand Imam Abu Hanifa's proof
Focus on his reasoning: the sale is a single transaction (safqah wahidah) because the buyer cannot accept the slave alone. The free person is non-property, so the condition to accept it is invalid (shart fasid), which provides benefit to the seller (extra price without consideration, i.e., riba), thus voiding the entire sale.
Note the concept of 'shart fasid' and its effect on contracts.
3
Analyze the opposing proofs: Sahibayn and Zufar
Sahibayn argue that invalidity is confined to the free person only, analogous to marriage contracts. Imam Zufar uses qiyas to the case of a mudabbar, claiming the same illa (non-saleable item) applies.
The text provides detailed rebuttals to both.
4
Examine the two objections to Abu Hanifa and their rebuttals
Two objections are raised: (1) specifying separate prices makes the transaction multiple, so no condition applies; (2) the condition does not benefit anyone, so it is not invalid. Abu Hanifa's rebuttals: contract speech unity determines single transaction, and the condition does benefit the seller (extra price without consideration).
Pay attention to the linguistic and economic arguments.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, the buyer can return both and get full refund; under Sahibayn, the slave's sale is valid, and only the free person's part is refunded (if prices specified). This affects the rights of parties.

Kitab al-Buyu' page 213. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya volume eight. That selling a free person and a slave together has been established in any case, that the omitted name (the free person) is in the ruling of a dead animal, and the mukatab and umm walad are like the mudabbar. Thus, if a mukatab or umm walad is sold together with a slave, the sale of the slave is valid for its portion of the price. Imam Zufar's proof is analogy (qiyas): he analogizes selling a slave and a mudabbar, or his own slave and another's slave, to the first issue of selling a free and a slave. Just as in the sale of a free and a slave, both sales are void, similarly in the sale of a slave and a mudabbar, both sales become invalid. The common cause is that the free, dead animal, mudabbar, and another's slave are problematic as objects of sale. Just as in the first issue, the free and dead animal are not objects of sale, similarly in the second issue, the mudabbar and another's slave are not objects of sale. So the same ruling applies. The Sahibayn's proof is that the invalidating factor extends only as far as it exists. The invalidating factor is only in the free and dead animal because they are not property, thus invalidity is specific to them and does not affect the slave or the slaughtered goat, just as the invalidity in the sale of a slave and a mudabbar remains specific to the mudabbar. This is like a marriage contract combining a stranger woman and one's sister: the sister's marriage is void, the stranger's is valid. However, if a free and slave are sold together without specifying individual prices, both sales are invalid due to ignorance of the slave's price. But if prices are specified separately, the slave's sale becomes valid due to absence of price ignorance. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa — and this is the difference between the two issues — is that a free man and a dead animal are not included in a sale contract at all because they are not property, and non-property is not included. The sale of a free and a slave, or a slaughtered goat and a dead animal, is a single transaction. The evidence is that if the buyer wishes to accept only the slave or the goat, he does not have that option; he must accept both or reject both. Thus not having the option to accept a single item proves it is a single transaction. So selling a free and a slave together is a single transaction. Since the free person is not included in the sale, he is a non-sold item, and the slave is the sold item. So the seller puts a condition that for accepting the sale of the sold item (the slave), the buyer must also accept the non-sold item (the free person). This is an invalid condition (shart fasid), and an invalid condition voids the sale, so the sale of the slave is also void. There are two objections to Imam A'zam's proof. First objection: when the prices of both are specified separately, the transaction ceases to be a single transaction; it becomes multiple transactions, so the condition of accepting the free is not necessary. Second objection: an invalid condition is only one that gives benefit to the seller, buyer, or the object of contract; this condition gives no benefit, so it is not invalid. [PAGE_214] Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya volume eight. If there is no benefit, this condition is not invalid. FIF Kitab al-Buyu'. Answer to first objection: even if the prices are specified separately, the transaction remains one because the word of sale is not repeated; unless the word 'sold' or 'bought' is repeated, the transaction is not multiple. Answer to second objection: the condition of accepting the free person benefits the seller. For example, he sells the free and slave for one thousand rupees, but the free is not property, so no price is in exchange for it, making it as if he said: I sell this slave for five hundred on condition that you give an additional five hundred. So the seller benefits from five hundred without consideration, which is riba. Thus the condition becomes invalid and voids the slave's sale. Another point: selling free and slave in one transaction is invalid because it is a sale of a share (bay' bi al-hissah) at the outset, so both sales are invalid. As for the Sahibayn's analogy to marriage, the answer is that analogizing sale to marriage is incorrect because marriage is not voided by invalid conditions, but sale is voided by them. So how can analogy be valid when there is a difference?
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the ruling on selling a free person together with a slave. The text presents the views of Imam Zufar, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), and Imam Abu Hanifa, along with proofs and responses to objections. The core issue is whether the invalidity due to including a non-property item extends to the slave. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that it does, because the sale is a single transaction and the condition to accept the free person is invalid, benefitting the seller. The Sahibayn argue that the invalidating factor is confined to the free person only. Imam Zufar analogizes to the case of a mudabbar, but the text refutes this by explaining the difference. The passage also addresses two objections to Abu Hanifa's proof and provides rebuttals, concluding that the sale of the slave is nonetheless void due to the invalid condition or because it constitutes a sale of a share at the outset.

Key Terms
صفقہ واحدہ (safqah wahidah): A single transaction where acceptance and rejection are indivisible; one cannot accept part and reject part.
شرط فاسد (shart fasid): A condition that is invalid and voids the contract because it provides benefit to one party or contradicts the nature of the contract.
غیر مبیع (ghayr mabi'): An item that is not the object of sale, but included in the contract as a condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is the sale of the slave void when sold with a free person in a single transaction?
A) Because the slave is not property
B) Because the condition to accept the free person is an invalid condition that benefits the seller
C) Because the price of the slave is unknown
D) Because the free person is a dead animal

Key Takeaway
The sale of a free person with a slave in a single transaction is void because it imposes an invalid condition that benefits the seller, a principle upheld by Imam Abu Hanifa.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Validity of Selling a Regular Slave with a Suspended-Sale Slave
Explains why selling a mudabbar, mukatab, etc. with a regular slave is valid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that selling a regular slave together with a mudabbar, mukatab, umm walad, or another's slave is valid, and identify the key condition that prevents invalidation.

Core Idea
A slave's sale remains valid when combined with a suspended-sale slave because both possess slave status and monetary value, so no invalidating condition arises.

In this lesson, we explore a specific ruling from the Hanafi school on the validity of selling a regular slave alongside a slave whose own sale is suspended (mawquf). The key distinction from the case of a free person is that these slaves are valid property (mal mutaqawwim). Understanding this nuance clarifies when a combined sale is permissible and when it is not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is selling a regular slave together with a mudabbar, mukatab, umm walad, or another's slave in one contract. The ruling is that the regular slave's sale is valid (sahih).
The sale of the other slaves themselves is suspended, not invalid.
2
Analyze the condition for a valid object of sale
A sale object must be mal mutaqawwim (valuable property). Determine whether each type of slave qualifies. Check riqq (slave status) and taqawwum (monetary value).
Free persons and dead animals lack taqawwum and thus cannot be sold.
3
Understand the suspended sale mechanism
Recognize that the mudabbar, mukatab, etc. can be sold, but their sale is suspended (mawquf) until a condition (e.g., owner's permission, qadi's order) is met. The contract is concluded but not immediately effective.
This is distinct from fasid (invalid) or batil (void) sales.
4
Trace the reasoning that rejection implies existence
When the mudabbar or owner rejects the sale, that rejection presupposes a valid contract. Thus the contract existed, making the slaves 'sold items' at the time of contract.
This prevents the need for a condition to accept a non-saleable item.
5
Apply the analogy of two slaves where one dies
The passage uses the analogy: if two slaves are sold and one dies before possession, the other's sale is valid for its portion. This illustrates that partial loss or suspension does not invalidate the whole.
This is called bay' bi al-hissah baqa' (sale of a share after the fact).

مدبر ، مکاتب اور ام ولد نے خود اپنی ذات کے مستحق ہونے کی وجہ سے بیع کو رد کر دیا اس لئے ان کے اندر بیع رد ہو گئی ہے اور بیع کا رد کرنا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ ان کے اندربیع موجود تھی اور جب مدبر وغیرہ میں بیع متحقق ہوگئی تو مدبر ، مکاتب، ام ولد اور عبد غیر بھی مبیع ہوئے اور جو غلام ان کے ساتھ ملا کر فروخت کیا گیا وہ بھی طبع ہے۔ تو ان صورتوں میں مبیع کے اندر بیع قبول کرنے کیلئے غیر مبیع کے اندر بیع قبول کرنے کی شرط لگا نا لازم نہیں آیا اور جب یہ شرط لگانا لازم نہیں آیا تو غلام کی بیچ بھی فاسد نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ مفسد بیع یہی شرط تھی ۔ اور بیع بالحصہ ابتداء بھی لازم نہیں آیا کیونکہ مد بر وغیرہ جب بیچ کے تحت داخل ہو گئے تو ابتدائے عقد میں غلام اور مدبر وغیرہ پر من تقسیم کرنے کی نوبت بھی نہیں آئے گی بلکہ یہ نوبت بیچ کے بعد قبضہ کے وقت آئے گی اور اس کو بیع بالحصہ بقائے کہا جاتا ہے اور بیع بالحصہ بقاء جائز ہے اسلئے ان صورتوں میں غلام کی بیع درست ہو جائے گی۔ اسی وجہ سے غلام اور مدبر میں سے ہر ایک کا شمن بیان کرنا شرط نہیں ہے اور یہ ایسا ہے جیسے کسی نے دو غلام فروخت کیلئے اور مشتری کے قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے ایک ہلاک ہو گیا تو دوسرے غلام کی بیع اس کے حصہ ثمن کے عوض جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ اس میں نہ تو غیر مبیع کو قبول کرنے
As for the second issue, the mudabbar, mukatab, umm walad, and the slave of another are included in a sale contract because their value remains. Value remains because a slave's value is established by slave status (riqq) and being valuable (taqawwum). The mudabbar, mukatab, umm walad, and another's slave have both slave status and being valuable. So when both aspects exist, their value remains, and when value remains, their being objects of sale is established. However, their sale is suspended: the sale of a mudabbar is suspended upon the qadi's decision, the sale of a mukatab is suspended upon the mukatab's consent, the sale of an umm walad is suspended upon the qadi's decision according to the Shaykhayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and the sale of another's slave is suspended upon the owner's permission. For this reason, the sale of another's slave becomes effective with the owner's permission, the sale of a mukatab becomes effective with his consent, the sale of a mudabbar becomes effective with the qadi's order, and similarly the sale of an umm walad becomes effective with the qadi's order according to the Shaykhayn. In any case, the sale of mudabbar etc. is suspended. But because in the case of another's slave, the owner (other) has rejected the sale by virtue of being entitled to his slave, and the mudabbar, mukatab, and umm walad have rejected the sale by virtue of being entitled to themselves, thus rejection of the sale occurred. Rejection of the sale is evidence that the sale existed (i.e., the contract took place but was rejected). And when the sale is realized in mudabbar etc., they became sold items. And the slave that was sold together with them is also sold. So in these cases, it is not necessary to impose a condition of accepting the non-sold item in order to accept the sold item. And when it is not necessary to impose such a condition, the slave's sale is not invalid, because the invalidating factor was that condition. Also, the sale of a share at the outset is not necessary because when mudabbar etc. are included in the contract, there is no need to divide the price at the time of contracting; that need arises at the time of possession, which is called bay' bi al-hissah baqa', and that is permissible. Therefore, in these cases the slave's sale is valid. For this reason, it is not required to specify the price of each. This is like a person selling two slaves, and before the buyer takes possession, one dies; the sale of the other slave is valid for its portion of the price, because there is no acceptance of a non-sold item.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining why selling a mudabbar, mukatab, umm walad, or another's slave together with a regular slave does not invalidate the slave's sale. The key distinction from the free person case is that these individuals are property with monetary value (maliyyah) due to their slave status (riqq) and being considered valuable (taqawwum). They can be objects of sale, though their sale is suspended (mawquf) upon fulfillment of certain conditions. Because they are valid subjects of sale, the transaction does not require a condition to accept a non-saleable item, unlike the free person case. Thus the invalidating factor is absent, and the slave's sale is valid. The text also clarifies that specifying individual prices is not necessary, and gives an analogy of two slaves where one dies before possession, which is also valid.

Key Terms
موقوف (mawquf): Suspended; refers to a contract that is concluded but depends on a later event (like permission) for its effectiveness.
رقیت (riqq): The state of being a slave; legal ownership by another.
تقوم (taqawwum): Being considered valuable property in the sight of Islamic law (i.e., having monetary value).
مالیت (maliyyah): Property value; the quality of being considered wealth (mal) under Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the sale of a regular slave valid when sold together with a mudabbar, according to the Hanafi view?
A) Because the mudabbar is non-property like a free person
B) Because the mudabbar has monetary value and is a valid object of sale
C) Because the price of the mudabbar is always known
D) Because the mudabbar is a dead animal

Key Takeaway
A regular slave sold together with a mudabbar, mukatab, umm walad, or another's slave is valid because these slaves are property (mal mutaqawwim), so no condition of accepting a non-saleable item arises.
