Validity of Buyer's Subsequent Sale of Fasid Goods
Ruling and reasoning for a second sale by the buyer in a fasid sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a buyer's subsequent sale of goods purchased in a fasid sale and explain the legal reasoning (ta'lil) based on the priority of human rights (ḥaqq al-ʿabd) over Sharia rights.

Core Idea
A fasid sale buyer's subsequent sale is valid because human needs override Sharia technicalities.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling in Hanafi fiqh: when a buyer in a defective (fasid) sale re-sells the item to a third party. The apparent defect in the first sale might suggest the buyer has no ownership. Yet the Hanafi school validly upholds the second sale. The reasoning, as presented in al-Hidayah, reveals a careful balancing of rights—human need (ḥaqq al-ʿabd) versus Sharia formality (ḥaqq al-sharʿ). Understanding this ruling sharpens your grasp of how Hanafi jurists prioritize human welfare in commercial transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the specific action being ruled upon? It is the buyer's sale of an item he purchased in a fasid (defective) contract. The ruling is that such a sale is valid (nafidh) and effective.
The ruling is stated at the beginning: 'If the buyer sells it, his sale is effective.'
2
Understand the conceptual framework of rights
The passage distinguishes between two types of rights: ḥaqq al-ʿabd (a human right, here the second buyer's right) and ḥaqq al-sharʿ (a Sharia right, here the first seller's right to annul the fasid contract). Hanafi law prioritizes human rights over Sharia rights in financial transactions when there is a conflict.
This priority is justified by the second buyer's need (ḥājah).
3
Analyze the ta'lil (reasoning)
The passage gives several reasons for the validity of the second sale: (1) The buyer becomes owner of the item by possession (al-milk bi al-qabd) in a fasid sale, so he has the right to dispose. (2) The second sale attaches a human right to the second buyer, which overrides the first seller's Sharia right to reclaim. (3) The first sale is valid in its essence (aṣl) but defective in description (waṣf), while the second sale is sound in both, so a mere defect in description cannot defeat a fully valid contract. (4) The second sale occurred with the authorization (taslīṭ) of the first seller, as he handed over possession to the buyer.
Each reason independently supports the ruling, showing the strength of the Hanafi position.
4
Differentiate from similar cases
The text contrasts this ruling with the case of a pre-emptor (shafiʿ). In that case, the buyer's disposal is not authorized by the pre-emptor, so it is not valid. Here, the first seller implicitly authorized the buyer's disposal by delivering possession, making the second sale effective.
This distinction highlights the importance of authorization (taslīṭ) in validating subsequent transactions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مشتری کا بیع فاسد سے خریدی ہوئی چیز کو آگے بیچنے کا حکم
قال فان باعه المشترى نفذ بيعه لانه ملکه فملك التصرف فيه وسقط حق الاسترداد لتعلق حق العبد بالثاني ونقض الأول لحق الشرع وحق العبد مقدم لحاجته ولان الاول مشروع باصله دون وصفه والثاني مشروع باصله ووصفه فلا يعارضه مجرد الوصف ولانه حصل بتسليط من جهة البائع بخلاف تصرف المشترى في ـدار المتنوعة لان كل واحد منهما حق العبد ويستويان فى المشروعية وما حصل بتسليط من الشفيع
ترجمہ پر اگر مبیع مقبوضہ کو مشتری نے فروخت کیا تو اس کی بیع نافذ ہو جائے گی کیونکہ مشتری اس کا مالک ہو گیا تو اس میں تصرف کا وہ مالک ہوتا اور بائع اول کا مبیع واپس لینے کا حق ساقط ہو گیا کیونکہ دوسری بیع سے بندہ کا حق متعلق ہو گیا اور بیع اول کا توڑنا حق شرع تھا
Ruling on the buyer selling onward the item purchased in a fasid sale.
He (al-Hidayah?) said: 'If the buyer sells it, his sale is effective, because he owns it, so he has the right to dispose of it. And the right of the first seller to reclaim it drops, because the right of the servant (ʿabd) becomes attached to the second (purchaser), and the first sale is broken due to the right of the Sharia. The right of the servant is given precedence due to his need. And because the first (sale) is prescribed in its essence but not in its description, while the second (sale) is prescribed in its essence and its description, so a mere description does not oppose it. And because it (the second sale) occurred by authorization from the seller, unlike the disposal of the buyer in the case of a sharecropper (shafi'), because each of them is a right of the servant, and they are equal in prescribability, and what occurred by authorization from the pre-emptor (shafi').'
Translation: So if the buyer sells the possessed sold item, his sale is valid, because the buyer has become its owner, so he is the owner of disposal in it. And the right of the first seller to take back the sold item drops, because the right of the servant becomes attached to the second sale, and breaking the first sale is a Sharia right.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a crucial question: if a buyer in a fasid (invalid) sale takes possession and then sells the item to a third party, is that second sale valid? The text affirms that it is valid. The reasoning is multi-faceted: First, the buyer is considered the owner of the item due to possession (al-milb bi al-qabd) in a fasid sale, so he has the authority to sell it. Second, the first seller's right to reclaim the item (haqq al-istirdad) is overridden because a new right of the 'servant' (haqq al-ʿabd, i.e., a private right of a human) has attached to the second buyer. This private right is given precedence over the Sharia right of the first seller to annul the defective contract, because the second buyer's need is more immediate. Third, the first sale was valid in its original basis (aṣl) but not in its description (waṣf), meaning it was fundamentally a sale but had a defect in description (e.g., invalid price). The second sale is valid both in its basis and description. A mere defect (description) cannot outweigh a fully valid second contract. Fourth, the second sale occurred with the authorization (taslīṭ) of the original seller indirectly, because the original seller delivered possession to the buyer, enabling him to sell. This contrasts with the case of a shafiʿ (pre-emptor) where the buyer's disposal is not authorized. The text ends by noting that if the first seller had a right of reclaim, it is a Sharia right, but the second buyer's right (as a human right) takes priority.

Key Terms
حق العبد (ḥaqq al-ʿabd): A human right, i.e., a right belonging to an individual (like a buyer) as opposed to a Sharia right (right of God).
حق الشرع (ḥaqq al-sharʿ): A right of the Sharia, i.e., a divine command that invalidates transactions for the sake of public interest.
تسليط (taslīṭ): Authorization or empowerment; here, the original seller's act of handing over possession authorizes the buyer to sell.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a fasid sale, if the buyer sells the item to a third party after taking possession, what happens?
A) The second sale is invalid because the first sale was defective
B) The second sale is valid and the first seller's right to reclaim is dropped
C) The second sale is valid but the first seller can still reclaim the item from the third party
D) The second sale is suspended until the first seller approves

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a buyer in a fasid sale who takes possession can validly sell the item to a third party, and the first seller's right to reclaim is overridden by the second buyer's human right.

General Ruling: Fasid Sale is Non-Binding and Rescindable
General ruling on fasid sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general ruling of a fasid sale and identify the right of each party to rescind.

Core Idea
A fasid sale is not binding; both parties have the right to rescind.

This lesson establishes the foundational principle regarding defective sales (fasid). In Hanafi fiqh, a fasid contract is valid in its essence but has an attribute that makes it irregular. Because the defect is strong and its removal is a right of Shari'ah, the contract does not become binding (lazim). Consequently, each contracting party retains the power to rescind (faskh) the contract. This right exists regardless of which party initiated the defect.

Guided Path
1
Define fasid sale
Understand the Hanafi distinction between fasid (defective) and batil (void). A fasid sale has valid pillars but an irregular attribute.
Examples: sale with an uncertain price, sale with a prohibited condition.
2
Identify the ruling
The passage states that a fasid sale is not binding (ghayr lazim) because removing the defect is a Shari'ah right.
This means neither party is forced to uphold the contract.
3
Right to rescind
Every contracting party can rescind a non-binding contract. Therefore, both parties have the option to rescind.
This right exists from the moment the defect is discovered.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب البيوع
فساد بہت قوی ہے اور فساد دور کرنا شریعت کا حق ہے اس لئے حق شرع کی وجہ سے عقد فاسد لازم نہ رہا اور عقد غیر لازم کو عاقدین میں سے ہر ایک فسخ کرنے کی قدرت رکھتا ہے اسلئے اس صورت میں عاقدین میں سے ہر ایک کو فسخ کرنے کا اختیار دیا گیا ہاں اتنا فرق ہے کہ طرفین کے نزدیک جو بھی فسخ کرنا چاہے اپنے ساتھی کی موجودگی میں فسخ کرے یعنی اپنے ساتھی کے علم میں لا کر فسخ کرے اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اس کی موجودگی اور عدم موجودگی دونوں حالتوں میں فسخ کر سکتا ہے امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بیع فاسد کو فسخ کر کے فساد کو دور کرنا شریعت کا حق ہے اور شریعت کا حق ادا کرنے کے لئے کسی کی موجودگی یا عدم موجودگی شرط نہیں ہے اس لئے بیع فاسد کو اپنے ساتھی کی موجودگی میں بھی فسخ کر سکتا ہے اور عدم موجودگی میں بھی فسخ کر سکتا ہے۔
طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ فسخ کر کے فساد دور کرنا شرع کا حق ہے نیز فسخ کرنے میں اپنے ساتھی پر الزام بھی ہے کیونکہ آدمی عقد اس وقت فسخ کرتا ہے جبکہ وہ اس میں ضرر محسوس کرتا ہے گویا فسخ کرنے والے نے اپنے ساتھی پر ضرر پہنچانے کا الزام لگایا ہے اور کسی پر الزام لگانے کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ اس کو معلوم بھی ہو جس پر الزام لگایا ہے۔ اس لئے فسخ کرنے والا اپنے ساتھی کی موجودگی میں فسخ کر سکتا ہے اس کی عدم موجودگی میں فسخ کرنے کی اجازت نہیں ہے۔
اور اگر فساد زائد میں ہو تو قبضہ مشتری سے پہلے عاقدین میں سے ہر ایک کو فسخ کرنے کا اختیار ہے لیکن قبضہ کے بعد حضرت امام محمد کے نزدیک صرف اس کو فسخ کرنے کا اختیار ہے جس کے لئے شرط کا نفع ہو مثلا قرض دینے یا ہدیہ دینے کی شرط میں بائع کا نفع ہے اور مہربانی کی شرط میں مشتری کا نفع ہے اور شرط جس کے خلاف ہو اس کو فسخ کرنے کا اختیار نہیں ہے مگر یہ یاد رہے کہ من لہ الشرط اگر اپنے اختیار کے تحت فسخ کرنا چاہے تو من علیہ الشرط کی موجودگی میں فسخ کرے اور شیخین کے نزدیک عاقدین میں سے ہر ایک کو فسخ کرنے کا اختیار ہے صاحب ہدایہ نے فقط امام محمد کا قول ذکر کیا ہے شیخین کا قول ذکر نہیں کیا حضرت امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ شرط زائد میں فساد پیدا ہونے سے فساد قوی نہیں ہوتا بلکہ عقد قوی ہوتا ہے لیکن اب سوال ہو گا کہ جب عقد قوی ہے تو عاقدین میں سے کسی کو بھی اختیار نہ ہونا چاہیے تھا اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ بغیر رضا کے چونکہ من لہ الشرط کی رضا مندی متحقق نہیں ہوتی اس لئے اس کو فسخ کرنے کا اختیار دیا گیا اور شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ فساد دور کرنا چونکہ شریعت کا حق ہے اس لئے عقد غیر لازم ہو گیا اور عقد غیر لازم کو عاقدین میں سے ہر ایک فسخ کر سکتا ہے اس لئے اس صورت میں عاقدین میں سے ہر ایک کو بیع فاسد کرنے کا اختیار ہوگا۔
The chain of sale. The defect is very strong, and removing the defect is a right of the Shari'ah. Therefore, due to the right of Shari'ah, a defective contract does not remain binding. And every one of the two contracting parties has the power to rescind a non-binding contract. Hence, in this case, each of the two contracting parties is given the option to rescind. However, there is this difference: according to the two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), whoever wishes to rescind must do so in the presence of his partner, i.e., inform his partner and then rescind. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, he can rescind in both situations: in the presence or absence of his partner. Imam Abu Yusuf's proof is that rescinding a defective sale to remove the defect is a right of the Shari'ah, and for fulfilling a right of the Shari'ah, the presence or absence of someone is not a condition. Therefore, he can rescind the defective sale both in the presence and absence of his partner. The proof of the two sides is that rescinding to remove the defect is a right of the Shari'ah, but rescinding also involves blaming one's partner, because a person rescinds a contract when he perceives harm in it. So the rescinder has accused his partner of causing harm, and to accuse someone, it is necessary that the accused be informed. Therefore, the rescinder can only rescind in the presence of his partner; he is not permitted to rescind in his absence. And if the defect is in an additional condition, then before the buyer takes possession, each contracting party has the option to rescind. But after possession, according to Imam Muhammad, only the one for whom the condition is beneficial has the option to rescind. For example, in the condition of giving a loan or a gift, the benefit is for the seller; in the condition of a favor, the benefit is for the buyer. The one against whom the condition is made does not have the option to rescind. However, it should be remembered that if the one for whom the benefit is intended wishes to rescind by his own option, he should rescind in the presence of the one upon whom the condition is imposed. According to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), each of the two contracting parties has the option to rescind. The author of Al-Hidayah mentioned only Imam Muhammad's statement; he did not mention the statement of the two shaykhs. Imam Muhammad's proof is that the defect arising from an additional condition does not make the defect strong; rather, the contract becomes strong. But then a question arises: when the contract is strong, no one should have the option. The answer is that without consent, since the consent of the one for whom the benefit is intended is not realized, he is given the option to rescind. The proof of the two shaykhs is that removing the defect is a right of the Shari'ah, so the contract becomes non-binding, and a non-binding contract can be rescinded by either party. Therefore, in this case, each of the two parties will have the option to rescind the defective sale.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage addresses the right to rescind a fasid (defective) sale. It begins with the general principle: because the defect is strong and its removal is a right of Shari'ah, the fasid contract is not binding (ghayr lazim), giving each party the option to rescind. The passage then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: the 'tarafayn' (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) require the rescission to be in the presence of the other party, while Abu Yusuf allows it even in absence. The reasoning is that rescission implies blame for harm, so the absent party must be informed. The passage then moves to a second dispute regarding an additional condition (shart za'id) that causes the defect. Before possession, both parties can rescind. After possession, Imam Muhammad holds that only the party benefiting from the condition can rescind, and must do so in the presence of the other. The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that both parties can rescind because the contract remains non-binding. The author notes that Al-Hidayah only reports Imam Muhammad's view, implying it is the preferred one (mufta bihi). The overall structure is: general ruling, then two ikhtilafs with proofs.

Key Terms
عقد فاسد (aqd fasid): A defective contract with valid pillars but an irregular attribute; it is not binding.
فسخ (faskh): Rescission or annulment of a contract.
لازم (lazim): Binding; a contract that cannot be unilaterally rescinded.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the general ruling of a fasid sale according to this passage?
A) It is binding and cannot be rescinded.
B) It is not binding and each party can rescind.
C) It is void ab initio and requires no rescission.
D) It is binding but only the buyer can rescind.

Key Takeaway
A fasid sale is non-binding; both parties have the unilateral right to rescind.

Condition of Presence for Rescission: Tarafayn vs Abu Yusuf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on presence requirement for rescission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ikhtilaf between the 'tarafayn' (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding whether the rescinding party must be in the presence of the other party.

Core Idea
Tarafayn require presence; Abu Yusuf permits rescission even in absence.

In the previous lesson, we learned that both parties can rescind a fasid sale. However, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the procedural requirement: must the rescinding party do so in the presence of his partner? The tarafayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) answer yes, because rescission implies blame. Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees, arguing that since rescission is a Shari'ah right, the presence of the partner is irrelevant.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Tarafayn: rescission must be in presence of partner. Abu Yusuf: presence is not required.
Tarafayn here means Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
2
Analyze the proof of Abu Yusuf
His proof: rescission is a Shari'ah right, and fulfilling a Shari'ah right does not depend on someone's presence.
This is a straightforward textual reasoning (dalil aqli).
3
Analyze the proof of the tarafayn
Their proof: rescission involves blaming the partner for harm, and blame requires informing the accused.
This is based on a social consideration (adab).
4
Determine the operative ruling
The author of Al-Hidayah does not explicitly choose, but later Hanafi practice tends to follow the tarafayn because it is more cautious.
Check fatwa references.

Source Text

كتاب البيوع
فساد بہت قوی ہے اور فساد دور کرنا شریعت کا حق ہے اس لئے حق شرع کی وجہ سے عقد فاسد لازم نہ رہا اور عقد غیر لازم کو عاقدین میں سے ہر ایک فسخ کرنے کی قدرت رکھتا ہے اسلئے اس صورت میں عاقدین میں سے ہر ایک کو فسخ کرنے کا اختیار دیا گیا ہاں اتنا فرق ہے کہ طرفین کے نزدیک جو بھی فسخ کرنا چاہے اپنے ساتھی کی موجودگی میں فسخ کرے یعنی اپنے ساتھی کے علم میں لا کر فسخ کرے اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اس کی موجودگی اور عدم موجودگی دونوں حالتوں میں فسخ کر سکتا ہے امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بیع فاسد کو فسخ کر کے فساد کو دور کرنا شریعت کا حق ہے اور شریعت کا حق ادا کرنے کے لئے کسی کی موجودگی یا عدم موجودگی شرط نہیں ہے اس لئے بیع فاسد کو اپنے ساتھی کی موجودگی میں بھی فسخ کر سکتا ہے اور عدم موجودگی میں بھی فسخ کر سکتا ہے۔
طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ فسخ کر کے فساد دور کرنا شرع کا حق ہے نیز فسخ کرنے میں اپنے ساتھی پر الزام بھی ہے کیونکہ آدمی عقد اس وقت فسخ کرتا ہے جبکہ وہ اس میں ضرر محسوس کرتا ہے گویا فسخ کرنے والے نے اپنے ساتھی پر ضرر پہنچانے کا الزام لگایا ہے اور کسی پر الزام لگانے کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ اس کو معلوم بھی ہو جس پر الزام لگایا ہے۔ اس لئے فسخ کرنے والا اپنے ساتھی کی موجودگی میں فسخ کر سکتا ہے اس کی عدم موجودگی میں فسخ کرنے کی اجازت نہیں ہے۔
اور اگر فساد زائد میں ہو تو قبضہ مشتری سے پہلے عاقدین میں سے ہر ایک کو فسخ کرنے کا اختیار ہے لیکن قبضہ کے بعد حضرت امام محمد کے نزدیک صرف اس کو فسخ کرنے کا اختیار ہے جس کے لئے شرط کا نفع ہو مثلا قرض دینے یا ہدیہ دینے کی شرط میں بائع کا نفع ہے اور مہربانی کی شرط میں مشتری کا نفع ہے اور شرط جس کے خلاف ہو اس کو فسخ کرنے کا اختیار نہیں ہے مگر یہ یاد رہے کہ من لہ الشرط اگر اپنے اختیار کے تحت فسخ کرنا چاہے تو من علیہ الشرط کی موجودگی میں فسخ کرے اور شیخین کے نزدیک عاقدین میں سے ہر ایک کو فسخ کرنے کا اختیار ہے صاحب ہدایہ نے فقط امام محمد کا قول ذکر کیا ہے شیخین کا قول ذکر نہیں کیا حضرت امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ شرط زائد میں فساد پیدا ہونے سے فساد قوی نہیں ہوتا بلکہ عقد قوی ہوتا ہے لیکن اب سوال ہو گا کہ جب عقد قوی ہے تو عاقدین میں سے کسی کو بھی اختیار نہ ہونا چاہیے تھا اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ بغیر رضا کے چونکہ من لہ الشرط کی رضا مندی متحقق نہیں ہوتی اس لئے اس کو فسخ کرنے کا اختیار دیا گیا اور شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ فساد دور کرنا چونکہ شریعت کا حق ہے اس لئے عقد غیر لازم ہو گیا اور عقد غیر لازم کو عاقدین میں سے ہر ایک فسخ کر سکتا ہے اس لئے اس صورت میں عاقدین میں سے ہر ایک کو بیع فاسد کرنے کا اختیار ہوگا۔
The chain of sale. The defect is very strong, and removing the defect is a right of the Shari'ah. Therefore, due to the right of Shari'ah, a defective contract does not remain binding. And every one of the two contracting parties has the power to rescind a non-binding contract. Hence, in this case, each of the two contracting parties is given the option to rescind. However, there is this difference: according to the two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), whoever wishes to rescind must do so in the presence of his partner, i.e., inform his partner and then rescind. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, he can rescind in both situations: in the presence or absence of his partner. Imam Abu Yusuf's proof is that rescinding a defective sale to remove the defect is a right of the Shari'ah, and for fulfilling a right of the Shari'ah, the presence or absence of someone is not a condition. Therefore, he can rescind the defective sale both in the presence and absence of his partner. The proof of the two sides is that rescinding to remove the defect is a right of the Shari'ah, but rescinding also involves blaming one's partner, because a person rescinds a contract when he perceives harm in it. So the rescinder has accused his partner of causing harm, and to accuse someone, it is necessary that the accused be informed. Therefore, the rescinder can only rescind in the presence of his partner; he is not permitted to rescind in his absence. And if the defect is in an additional condition, then before the buyer takes possession, each contracting party has the option to rescind. But after possession, according to Imam Muhammad, only the one for whom the condition is beneficial has the option to rescind. For example, in the condition of giving a loan or a gift, the benefit is for the seller; in the condition of a favor, the benefit is for the buyer. The one against whom the condition is made does not have the option to rescind. However, it should be remembered that if the one for whom the benefit is intended wishes to rescind by his own option, he should rescind in the presence of the one upon whom the condition is imposed. According to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), each of the two contracting parties has the option to rescind. The author of Al-Hidayah mentioned only Imam Muhammad's statement; he did not mention the statement of the two shaykhs. Imam Muhammad's proof is that the defect arising from an additional condition does not make the defect strong; rather, the contract becomes strong. But then a question arises: when the contract is strong, no one should have the option. The answer is that without consent, since the consent of the one for whom the benefit is intended is not realized, he is given the option to rescind. The proof of the two shaykhs is that removing the defect is a right of the Shari'ah, so the contract becomes non-binding, and a non-binding contract can be rescinded by either party. Therefore, in this case, each of the two parties will have the option to rescind the defective sale.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage addresses the right to rescind a fasid (defective) sale. It begins with the general principle: because the defect is strong and its removal is a right of Shari'ah, the fasid contract is not binding (ghayr lazim), giving each party the option to rescind. The passage then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: the 'tarafayn' (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) require the rescission to be in the presence of the other party, while Abu Yusuf allows it even in absence. The reasoning is that rescission implies blame for harm, so the absent party must be informed. The passage then moves to a second dispute regarding an additional condition (shart za'id) that causes the defect. Before possession, both parties can rescind. After possession, Imam Muhammad holds that only the party benefiting from the condition can rescind, and must do so in the presence of the other. The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that both parties can rescind because the contract remains non-binding. The author notes that Al-Hidayah only reports Imam Muhammad's view, implying it is the preferred one (mufta bihi). The overall structure is: general ruling, then two ikhtilafs with proofs.

Key Terms
طرفین (tarafayn): The two sides: here referring to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, as opposed to Imam Abu Yusuf.
فسخ (faskh): Rescission or annulment of a contract.
شریعت کا حق (Shari'ah right): A right established by Islamic law, here the right to remove the defect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the dispute between tarafayn and Abu Yusuf?
A) The contract remains binding if rescinded in absence.
B) Rescission in absence is valid according to tarafayn, invalid according to Abu Yusuf.
C) Rescission in presence is valid for both, but only tarafayn allow it in absence.
D) Rescission in absence is valid according to Abu Yusuf, invalid according to tarafayn.

Key Takeaway
The tarafayn require presence for rescission due to blame; Abu Yusuf permits absence as a Shari'ah right.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

7 min
Rescission with Additional Condition: Muhammad vs Shaykhayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on rescission with additional condition after possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ikhtilaf between Imam Muhammad and the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) regarding who can rescind a fasid sale after possession when the defect is due to an additional condition.

Core Idea
After possession, Muhammad limits rescission to the benefiting party; the shaykhayn allow both parties.

This lesson addresses a specific type of fasid sale: one where the defect arises from an additional condition (shart za'id), such as a condition to give a loan or gift. Before possession, both parties can rescind. After possession, a dispute arises: Imam Muhammad holds that only the party for whom the condition is beneficial can rescind, because the other party has consented to the condition. The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that both parties can rescind because the contract remains non-binding. Al-Hidayah reports only Muhammad's view, suggesting it is the mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The defect is due to an additional condition (e.g., loan, gift, favor). Note the stages: before and after possession.
The condition benefits one party.
2
Muhammad's position and proof
After possession, only the one benefiting from the condition can rescind. His proof: the contract becomes strong (qawi) because the condition is part of the agreement; however, the other party's consent is not fully realized, so he retains the right to rescind. The party against the condition does not have the right because he agreed to the condition.
The contract is strong, but due to lack of full consent, the benefiting party can rescind.
3
Shaykhayn's position and proof
Both parties can rescind. Their proof: removing the defect is a Shari'ah right, so the contract remains non-binding for both.
They treat it like a general fasid sale.
4
Tarjih in Al-Hidayah
The author only mentions Muhammad's view, indicating it is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
This is a common pattern: Al-Hidayah often prefers Muhammad's view.

Commentary
This passage addresses the right to rescind a fasid (defective) sale. It begins with the general principle: because the defect is strong and its removal is a right of Shari'ah, the fasid contract is not binding (ghayr lazim), giving each party the option to rescind. The passage then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: the 'tarafayn' (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) require the rescission to be in the presence of the other party, while Abu Yusuf allows it even in absence. The reasoning is that rescission implies blame for harm, so the absent party must be informed. The passage then moves to a second dispute regarding an additional condition (shart za'id) that causes the defect. Before possession, both parties can rescind. After possession, Imam Muhammad holds that only the party benefiting from the condition can rescind, and must do so in the presence of the other. The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that both parties can rescind because the contract remains non-binding. The author notes that Al-Hidayah only reports Imam Muhammad's view, implying it is the preferred one (mufta bihi). The overall structure is: general ruling, then two ikhtilafs with proofs.

Key Terms
شرط زائد (shart za'id): An additional condition that introduces a defect into the sale, such as a loan or gift condition.
شیخین (shaykhayn): The two shaykhs: referring to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as opposed to Imam Muhammad.
من لہ الشرط (man lahu al-shart): The one for whom the condition is beneficial.
من علیہ الشرط (man alayhi al-shart): The one upon whom the condition is imposed.

A) Both parties can rescind.
B) Only the buyer can rescind.
C) Only the party benefiting from the condition can rescind.
D) Neither party can rescind.

Key Takeaway
After possession, Muhammad restricts rescission to the benefiting party; the shaykhayn allow both.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Buyer's Sale of Fasid-Purchased Item: Ruling and Proofs
States the ruling when a buyer sells a fasid-purchased item and provides three proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a buyer sells an item purchased through a fasid contract and explain the three proofs that make the subsequent sale effective.

Core Idea
A subsequent sale by a fasid buyer is effective because the second buyer's right outweighs the Shari'ah's right to rescind.

In this passage, Al-Marghinani presents a clear ruling on a common commercial scenario: what happens when someone buys an item through a defective (fasid) contract, takes possession, and then sells it to another? The ruling might seem counterintuitive, but the Hanafi school affirms the second sale as sahih (valid) based on three proofs rooted in the priority of individual rights and the nature of the contracts. This lesson will walk you through the scenario, the ruling, and the detailed reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
Understand the facts: a buyer purchases an item via a fasid sale, takes possession with the seller's permission, then sells it to a third party. The ruling is that this second sale is effective (nāfidh), and the original seller loses the right to reclaim the item.
The fasid sale is valid in essence but defective in attribute.
2
Examine the first proof: priority of the servant's right
The second buyer's right (haqq al-‛abd) is attached to the valid second sale, while the first seller's right to rescind is a right of the Sharī‛ah (haqq Allāh). Since the servant is needy and Allāh is self-sufficient, the servant's right takes precedence.
This is a key Hanafi principle: haqq al-‛abd is preferred over haqq Allāh when they conflict.
3
Examine the second proof: difference in validity
The first sale is valid only in its essence (asl) but defective in its attribute (waṣf), i.e., it is fāsid. The second sale is valid in both essence and attribute, i.e., it is ṣaḥīḥ. A fāsid contract cannot oppose a ṣaḥīḥ contract, so the second sale stands.
A mere defect (waṣf) in the first sale does not nullify a fully valid subsequent transaction.
4
Examine the third proof: authorization (taslīṭ)
The second sale was made possible because the first seller authorized the buyer to take possession. Thus the first seller effectively enabled the second sale and cannot later undo it. This is contrasted with the case of a preempted house, where the preemptor's right is also a servant's right but no authorization was given.
The principle of estoppel: one who facilitates a transaction cannot later invalidate it.

مشتری کا بیع فاسد سے خریدی ہوئی چیز کو آگے بیچنے کا حکم
قال فان باعه المشترى نفذ بيعه لانه ملکه فملك التصرف فيه وسقط حق الاسترداد لتعلق حق العبد بالثاني ونقض الأول لحق الشرع وحق العبد مقدم لحاجته ولان الاول مشروع باصله دون وصفه والثاني مشروع باصله ووصفه فلا يعارضه مجرد الوصف ولانه حصل بتسليط من جهة البائع بخلاف تصرف المشترى في الدار المشفوعه لان كل واحد منهما حق العبد ويستويان فى المشروعية وما حصل بتسليط من الشفيع
ترجمہ پر اگر میچ مقبوضہ کو مشتری نے فروخت کیا تو اس کی بیع نافذ ہو جائے گی کیونکہ مشتری اس کا مالک ہو گیا تو اس میں تصرف کا مالک ہوتا اور بائع اول کا مبیع واپس لینے کا حق ساقط ہو گیا کیونکہ دوسری بیع سے بندہ کا حق متعلق ہو گیا اور بیع اول کا توڑ نا حقِ شرع تھا اور بندہ کا حق اس کے محتاج ہونے کی وجہ سے مقدم ہوتا ہے اور اس لئے کہ بیع اول اپنی ذات کے اعتبار سے مشروع ہے نہ وصف کے اعتبار سے اور بیع ثانی اپنی ذات اور وصف دونوں اعتبار سے مشروع ہے لہذا محض وصف بیع ثانی کا معارض نہ ہوگا اور اس لئے کہ بیع ثانی بائع اول کی جانب سے قدرت دینے سے حاصل ہوئی ہے برخلاف دار مشفوعہ میں مشتری کے تصرف کے کیونکہ ہر ایک بندہ کا حق ہے اور مشروع ہونے میں دونوں برابر ہیں اور شفیع کے قدرت دینے سے یہ تصرف حاصل نہیں ہوا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے شراء فاسد کے طور پر کوئی چیز خریدی پھر مشتری نے بائع کی اجازت سے مبیع پر قبضہ کیا ہو۔ مشتری نے اس کو کسی دوسرے کے ہاتھ فروخت کر دیا تو مشتری کی یہ بیع نافذ ہو جائے گی کیونکہ مشتری بائع کی اجازت سے مبیع پر قبضہ کے اس کا مالک ہو گیا ہے اور مملوکہ چیز میں چونکہ ہر طرح کے تصرف کا اختیار ہوتا ہے اس لئے مشتری اس مبیع میں تصرف کرنے کا مالک ہوگا تصرف خواہ فروخت کرنے کی صورت میں ہو یا ہبہ کرنے کی اور یا صدقہ کرنے کی صورت میں ہو ہاں اگر مبیع ماکولات کے قبیل سے ہو تو مشتری کے لئے اس کا کھانا حلال نہیں ہے اور اگر باندی ہو تو اس سے وطی کرنا حلال نہیں ہے (بنا یہ) اور شمس الائمہ حلوائی کا خیال ہے کہ وطی کرنا حرام تو نہیں ہے البتہ مکروہ ہے بہر حال مشتری مبیع مقبوضہ کو بیچنے کا مالک ہے پس جب مشتری نے اس مبیع کو فروخت کر دیا تو اب بائع اول کو یہ حق نہ ہوگا کہ وہ بیع ثانی کو باطل کر کے مبیع واپس لے بلکہ مشتری پر مبیع کی قیمت واجب ہوئی اگر مبیع ذوات القیم میں سے ہو اور اگر مبیع ذوات الامثال میں سے ہو تو مشتری اول پر اس کا مثل واجب ہوگا اور مشتری ثانی کے لئے یہ بیع حلال اور طیب ہوگی کیونکہ مشتری ثانی اس کا مالک عقد صحیح سے ہوا ہے اور مشتری اول چونکہ عقد فاسد سے مالک ہوا تھا اس کے لئے مبیع حلال اور طیب نہ ہوگی۔ رہی یہ بات کہ مشتری کے فروخت کر دینے کے بعد بائع اول کو مبیع واپس لینے کا حق کیوں نہیں رہا تو اس کی پہلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بیع ثانی کے ساتھ مشتری ثانی یعنی بندہ کا حق متعلق ہے اور فساد کی وجہ سے بیع اول کو فسخ کرنا حق شرعی ہے یعنی بندہ (مشتری ثانی) کا حق تقاضہ کرتا ہے کہ بیع نافذ کی جائے اور شریعت کا حق تقاضہ ہے کہ بیع کو فسخ کیا جائے اور قاعدہ ہے کہ حق شرع اور حق عبد جمع ہونے کی صورت میں حق عبد مقدم ہوتا ہے کیونکہ شارع یعنی اللہ عز و جل غنی ہے اور بندہ محتاج ہے اور محتاج رعایت کا زیادہ مستحق ہے بہ نسبت غنی کے اس لئے بندہ یعنی مشتری ثانی کا حق مقدم ہوگا اور مشتری ثانی کے حق کا تقاضہ کرتا ہے کہ بیع نافذ کی جائے اس لئے اس صورت میں بیع فسخ کر کے مبیع بائع اول کی طرف واپس نہ کی جائے گی دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ بیع اول اپنی ذات کے اعتبار سے مشروع ہے مگر وصف کے اعتبار سے غیر مشروع ہے جیسا کہ سابق میں معلوم ہو چکا اور بیع ثانی اپنی ذات اور وصف دونوں اعتبار سے مشروع ہے یعنی بیع اول فاسد ہے اور بیع ثانی صحیح ہے اور فاسد صحیح کا معارض نہیں ہو سکتا اس لئے بیع اول فاسد کی وجہ سے بیع ثانی صحیح کو ختم نہیں کیا جائے گا اور جب ختم نہیں کیا جا سکتا تو بائع اول کا حق استرداد بھی ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ تیسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ بیع ثانی پر مشتری اول کو بائع اول ہی کی طرف سے قدرت حاصل ہوئی ہے کیونکہ مشتری نے بائع اول کی اجازت سے قبضہ کیا ہے پس بائع اول کا مبیع واپس لینا اس بیع کو ختم کرنا ہو گا جو خود اس کی طرف سے مکمل ہوئی ہے اور یہ باطل ہے اس لئے بائع اول کو مبیع واپس لینے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا۔
The ruling of the buyer selling the item purchased through a fasid sale:
He said: If the buyer sells it, his sale is effective because he owns it, so he owns the right to dispose of it, and the right of the first seller to take it back falls because the right of a servant (the second buyer) is attached to the second sale, and the abrogation of the first is due to the right of the Shari'ah. And the right of the servant is preferred due to his need. Also because the first is valid in its essence but not in its attribute, while the second is valid both in its essence and attribute, so a mere attribute cannot oppose it. Also because it (the second sale) occurred by authorization from the seller, unlike the buyer's disposal of a preempted house, because each of them is the right of a servant and they are equal in legitimacy, and it was not obtained by authorization from the preemptor.
Translation: When the buyer sells the possessed item, his sale will be effective because the buyer has become its owner, so he is the owner of disposal in it, and the first seller's right to take back the sold item falls because the right of a servant (the second buyer) is attached to the second sale, and annulling the first sale was a right of the Shari'ah, and the right of the servant is preferred due to his need. Also because the first sale is valid in its essence but not in its attribute, and the second sale is valid in both its essence and attribute, so a mere attribute will not oppose the second sale. Also because the second sale was obtained by authorization from the first seller, unlike the buyer's disposal in a preempted house, because each is a right of a servant and they are equal in legitimacy, and this disposal was not obtained by authorization from the preemptor.
Explanation of the scenario: If a person buys something through a fasid purchase, then the buyer takes possession of the sold item with the seller's permission, and then sells it to another, the buyer's sale is effective because the buyer became its owner by taking possession with the seller's permission, and since he owns it, he has authority over any disposal, whether by sale, gift, or charity. However, if the sold item is from the category of food, it is not permissible for the buyer to eat it; and if it is a slave girl, it is not permissible for him to have intercourse with her. According to Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, intercourse is not haram but makruh. In any case, the buyer is the owner of the possessed item. So when the buyer sells it, the first seller no longer has the right to nullify the second sale and take back the item. Rather, the buyer becomes liable for the price of the item if it is from the category of items with a fixed value (dhawat al-qeem), and if it is from the category of items with similar ones (dhawat al-amthal), the first buyer must pay the equivalent. And for the second buyer, this sale is halal and pure, because the second buyer became owner by a valid contract, while the first buyer became owner by a fasid contract, so for him the item is not halal and pure. As for why the first seller's right to reclaim the item is lost after the buyer sells it: The first proof is that the right of the servant (the second buyer) is attached to the second sale, and the annulment of the first sale due to defect is a right of the Shari'ah. The right of the servant demands that the sale be effective, while the right of the Shari'ah demands that it be rescinded. The rule is that when the right of Shari'ah and the right of a servant come together, the right of the servant is preferred because Allah, Glorious and Exalted, is self-sufficient, while the servant is needy, and the needy is more deserving of consideration than the self-sufficient. Therefore, the right of the servant (the second buyer) will be preferred, and his right demands that the sale be effective, so the sale will not be rescinded and the item will not be returned to the first seller. The second proof is that the first sale is valid in its essence but not in its attribute, as previously known, while the second sale is valid in both its essence and attribute. That is, the first is fasid and the second is sahih. A fasid cannot oppose a sahih, so the fasid first sale cannot terminate the valid second sale, and when it cannot be terminated, the first seller's right to reclaim also falls. The third proof is that the first buyer obtained the authority to make the second sale from the first seller himself, because the buyer took possession with the permission of the first seller. So the first seller's reclaiming of the item would terminate a sale that was made effective by his own authorization, and this is invalid. Therefore, the first seller does not have the option to take back the item.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage presents a clear ruling with three proofs. The scenario: A person buys something via a fasid contract, takes possession with the seller's permission, then sells it to a third party. The ruling: the subsequent sale is effective (nifaz), and the original seller loses the right to reclaim the item. The three proofs are: (1) The right of the servant (the second buyer) is attached to the second sale, and this right is preferred over the right of Shari'ah (to rescind the fasid sale) because of the latter's need. (2) The first sale is valid in essence but deficient in attribute (it is fasid), while the second is fully valid (sahih), so a lesser right cannot override a greater one. (3) The second sale was made possible by the authorization (tasleet) of the first seller (through permitting possession), so the first seller cannot undo a transaction he effectively enabled. The passage also clarifies that the buyer's ownership is restricted: he may not consume food or have intercourse with a slave girl, but he may sell, gift, or give in charity. After the sale, the first buyer owes the value or equivalent of the item to the first seller, while the second buyer's ownership is pure.

Key Terms
حق العبد (haqq al-abd): A right belonging to an individual servant (human being), as opposed to the right of Allah (haqq Allah).
حق الله (haqq Allah): A right that belongs to Allah, such as the obligation to remove a defect in a contract.
ذوات القیم (dhawat al-qeem): Items that have a unique value and are not replaced by similar items; the buyer must pay the market price.
ذوات الامثال (dhawat al-amthal): Items that can be replaced by similar ones; the buyer must pay the equivalent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the original seller lose the right to reclaim the item after the buyer sells it to a third party?
A) Because the original seller gave permission
B) Because the right of the third-party buyer (haqq al-abd) takes precedence over the right of Shari'ah
C) Because the first sale was void
D) Because the second sale is also fasid

Key Takeaway
The second sale by a fasid buyer is sahih because the second buyer's right (haqq al-abd) takes precedence over the Shari'ah's right to rescind, and the first seller cannot reclaim the item.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Second Sale After Corrupt Purchase Prevents Original Seller's Reclamation
Explains ruling that after a valid second sale, the original seller cannot reclaim the item.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a second sale after a corrupt purchase and explain the three proofs and the distinction from pre-emption.

Core Idea
A valid second sale after a corrupt purchase secures the second buyer's title; the original seller can only claim compensation.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi ruling in sales (buyu'): when a buyer takes possession of an item through a corrupt contract with the seller's permission, then sells it to a third party, the second sale is valid and the original seller cannot reclaim the item. The ruling is supported by three rational proofs based on istihsan (juristic preference). Understanding this ruling clarifies the interplay between defective ownership and valid dispositions, and the hierarchy of rights in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenario
State the facts: a corrupt purchase, possession with seller's permission, then a second sale to a third party.
The corrupt purchase (bay' fasid) is the first sale that is defective in description.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The second sale is valid and binding. The original seller loses the right to reclaim the item and can only claim compensation (price or its like) from the first buyer.
This is the mufta bihi position from zahir al-riwayah.
3
Work through the three proofs
Proof 1: The second buyer's human right (haqq al-'abd) overrides the Shari'a's right (haqq al-shar') to rescind. Proof 2: A valid sale cannot be nullified by a corrupt sale. Proof 3: The original seller's permission for possession enabled the first buyer to dispose, so he cannot revoke it.
These proofs are examples of istihsan.
4
Understand the usul principle
When haqq al-shar' and haqq al-'abd conflict, haqq al-'abd is given precedence because Allah is independent and humans are needy.
This principle is applied here to protect the second buyer.
5
Distinguish from the shuf'a case
In pre-emption, both rights are human rights, and the pre-emptor's prior right prevails, so the second sale is rescinded.
The difference hinges on the nature of the conflicting rights.

بائع اول کو مبیع واپس لینے کا حق کیوں نہیں رہا تو اس کی پہلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بیع ثانی کے ساتھ مشتری ثانی یعنی بندہ کا حق متعلق ہے اور فساد کی وجہ سے بیع اول کو فسخ کرناحق شرع کی وجہ سے ہے یعنی بندہ ( مشتری ثانی ) کا حق تقاضہ کرتا ہے کہ بیع نافذ کی جائے اور شریعت کا حق تقاضہ ہے کہ بیع کو فسخ کیا جائے اور قاعدہ ہے کہ حق شرع اور حق عبد جمع ہونے کی صورت میں حق عبد مقدم ہوتا ہے کیونکہ شارع یعنی اللہ عز و جل غنی ہے اور بند محتاج ہے اور محتاج رعایت کا زیادہ مستحق ہے بہ نسبت غنی کے اس لئے بندہ یعنی مشتری ثانی کا حق مقدم ہوگا اور مشتری ثانی کے حق کا تقاضہ کرتا ہے کہ بیع نافذ کی جائے اس لئے اس صورت میں بیع فسخ کر کے مبیع بائع اول کی طرف واپس نہ کی جائے گی۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ بیع اول اپنی ذات کے اعتبار سے مشروع ہے مگر وصف کے اعتبار سے غیر مشروع ہے جیسا کہ سابق میں معلوم ہو چکا اور بیع ثانی اپنی ذات اور وصف دونوں اعتبار سے مشروع ہے یعنی بیع اول فاسد ہے اور بیع ثانی صحیح ہے اور فاسد صحیح کا معارض نہیں ہو سکتا اس لئے بیع اول فاسد کی وجہ سے بیع ثانی صحیح کو ختم نہیں کیا جائے گا اور جب بیع ثانی ختم نہیں کی جا سکتی تو بائع اول کا حق استرداد بھی ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ تیسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ بیع ثانی پر مشتری اول کو بائع اول ہی کی طرف سے قدرت حاصل ہوئی ہے کیونکہ مشتری نے بائع اول کی اجازت سے قبضہ کیا ہے پس بائع اول کا مبیع واپس لینا اس بیع کو ختم کرنا ہو گا جو خود اس کی طرف سے مکمل ہوئی ہے اور یہ باطل ہے اس لئے بائع اول کو مبیع واپس لینے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا۔ خلاف تصرف المشتری الخ سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے سوال یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے ایک گھر خریدا جس کا کوئی شفیع ہے اور شفیع نے شفعہ بھی طلب کیا مگر مشتری نے خریدنے کے بعد اس گھر کو دوسرے کے ہاتھ فروخت کر دیا تو اس صورت میں مشتری کا کیا ہوا عقد فسخ کر کے شفیع کو حق دلا جاتا ہے حالانکہ اس صورت میں بھی مشتری ثانی کا حق متعلق ہو گیا ہے اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں دونوں یعنی مشتری ثانی کا حق اور شفیع کا حق حق عبد ہیں تو ان میں کوئی مقدم نہ ہوگا بلکہ شفیع کا حق خود مقدم تھا وہی مقدم رہے گا یعنی بیع اول کے منعقد ہوتے ہی صفقہ شفیع کی طرف منتقل ہو گیا اور جب صفقہ شفیع کی طرف منتقل ہو گیا تو اس کے بعد مشتری کے تمام تصرفات بلا سند باقی رہے اور بلا سند تصرف کو توڑنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اس لئے اس تصرف کو تو ڑ کر شفیع کا حق دلایا جائے گا اور تصرف شفیع اور تصرف مشتری چونکہ مشروع ہونے میں بھی برابر ہیں۔ اس لئے بھی مشتری کی بیع کو ترجیح نہ ہوگی بلکہ اس کو تو ڑ کر شفیع کا حق دلایا جائے اور یہ بات بھی نہیں ہے کہ شفیع کی طرف سے مشتری کو تصرفات کی قدرت حاصل ہوئی کیونکہ قدرت یا تو اجازت سے حاصل ہوتی ہے اور یا ملک ثابت کرنے سے حاصل ہوتی ہے اور یہاں دونوں باتیں نہیں ہیں کیونکہ شفیع نے نہ تو مشتری کو تصرف کی اجازت دی ہے اور نہ ہی مشتری کی ایسی ملک تسلیم کی ہے جو اس کے تصرف کو جائز کرے پس جب شفیع کی جانب سے مشتری کو قدرت تصرف حاصل نہیں ہوئی ہے تو مشتری کا تصرف تو ڑ کر شفیع کا حق دلایا جائے گا۔
Explanation of the case: If someone bought something in a corrupt purchase, then the buyer took possession with the seller's permission. The buyer then sold it to another person. Then this sale by the buyer is valid because the buyer became owner by taking possession with the seller's permission, and the owned item gives authority for all types of disposition, so the buyer is authorized to dispose of the sold item, whether by selling, gifting, or charity. However, if the sold item is of the category of edibles, it is not permissible for the buyer to eat it; and if it is a slave girl, intercourse with her is not permissible. (According to this) Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani holds that intercourse is not prohibited but makruh. In any case, the buyer is authorized to sell the possessed sold item. So when the buyer sold that sold item, the original seller no longer has the right to invalidate the second sale and reclaim the sold item; rather, the buyer owes the price if it is among items of value, and if among items of measure, the like is owed. And for the second buyer, this sale will be lawful and pure because the second buyer became owner by a valid contract, while the first buyer became owner by a corrupt contract, so for him the sold item was not lawful and pure. As for why the original seller no longer has the right to reclaim after the buyer sold it, the first proof is that with the second sale the right of the second buyer, i.e., a human being, is attached, and due to corruption the right to rescind the first sale is the right of the Shari'a. That is, the right of the human (second buyer) demands that the sale be executed, and the right of the Shari'a demands that the sale be rescinded. The rule is that when the right of the Shari'a and the right of a human are combined, the right of the human is given precedence because the Lawgiver, Allah Almighty, is independent, and the human is needy, and the needy is more deserving of consideration than the independent. Therefore, the right of the human, i.e., the second buyer, takes precedence, and the right of the second buyer demands that the sale be executed, so in this case the sale is not rescinded and the sold item is not returned to the original seller. The second proof is that the first sale is valid in essence but invalid in description, as known before, while the second sale is valid in both essence and description. That is, the first sale is corrupt and the second sale is valid, and the corrupt cannot oppose the valid, so the valid second sale cannot be terminated because of the corrupt first sale, and when the second sale cannot be terminated, the original seller's right of reclamation also falls. The third proof is that the first buyer obtained power over the second sale from the original seller, because the buyer took possession with the seller's permission. So the original seller's reclaiming the sold item would terminate the sale that was completed by his own permission, and that is invalid, so the original seller does not have the option to reclaim. The phrase 'contrary to the disposition of the buyer...' is an answer to a question: if someone bought a house that has a pre-emptor, and the pre-emptor claimed pre-emption, but the buyer after purchasing sold the house to another, in that case the buyer's contract is rescinded and the pre-emptor is given the right, even though here also the second buyer's right is attached. The answer is that in this case both rights, of the second buyer and of the pre-emptor, are human rights, so neither takes precedence over the other; rather, the pre-emptor's right was already prior, so it remains prior. That is, upon the conclusion of the first sale, the transaction transfers to the pre-emptor, and when it has transferred, all the buyer's subsequent dispositions remain without basis, and there is no harm in breaking a disposition without basis. Therefore, that disposition is broken and the pre-emptor's right is given. Also, the disposition of the pre-emptor and the disposition of the buyer are equal in being legislated, so the buyer's sale is not given precedence; rather it is broken and the pre-emptor's right is given. And it is also not the case that the buyer obtained power of disposition from the pre-emptor, because power is obtained either by permission or by establishing ownership, and neither is present here: the pre-emptor neither permitted the buyer to dispose nor confirmed such ownership in the buyer as would legitimize his disposition. So when the buyer did not obtain power of disposition from the pre-emptor, his disposition is broken and the pre-emptor's right is given.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage explains a ruling from the Hanafi school: when a person buys something through a corrupt contract (e.g., buying with an invalid exchange) and then, after taking possession with the seller's permission, sells it to a second buyer, the second sale is valid and the original seller loses the right to reclaim the item. The buyer (first buyer) becomes liable for the price (or its like). The passage provides three proofs for this ruling, each based on rational legal reasoning (istihsan). The first proof uses the principle that the right of a human (haqq al-'abd) takes precedence over the right of the Shari'a (haqq al-shar') when they conflict; the second proof argues that a valid sale (second) cannot be overridden by a corrupt sale (first); the third proof argues that since the original seller authorized the buyer's possession, he cannot later invalidate a sale that his own authorization made possible. The passage then addresses a potential objection based on the case of pre-emption (shuf'a): in pre-emption, a second sale by the buyer is rescinded in favor of the pre-emptor. The author distinguishes this by noting that in pre-emption, both rights are human rights and the pre-emptor's right was already established at the time of the first contract, so the buyer's subsequent disposition is invalid. This distinction reinforces the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
حق شرع (haqq al-shar'): The right of the Shari'a, i.e., the legal requirement that the corrupt sale be rescinded.
حق عبد (haqq al-'abd): The right of a human being, here the second buyer's right to have his valid sale upheld.
استرداد (istirdad): The right of the original seller to reclaim the sold item from the buyer.
شفعہ (shuf'a): Pre-emption: the right of a co-owner or neighbor to purchase a property that has been sold to an outsider.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a corrupt purchase where the buyer takes possession with the seller's permission and then sells the item to a third party, what happens to the original seller's right to reclaim the item?
A) The original seller can reclaim the item from the third party.
B) The original seller loses the right to reclaim and can only claim compensation from the first buyer.
C) The second sale is void and the item returns to the original seller.
D) The third party must return the item to the original seller, but then can claim from the first buyer.

Key Takeaway
After a second valid sale from a corrupt purchase, the original seller's right to reclaim is lost; he can only claim compensation from the first buyer.
